Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
The Four Fards of Wudu and Their Scriptural Proofs
Opening of Kitab al-Taharah listing four fards of wudu with six proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four fards of wudu according to the Hanafi school and identify the primary Quranic proof for each, distinguishing fard from wajib.

Core Idea
Wudu has four fards: washing face, hands, feet, and wiping the head — proven by the Quranic command in Surah al-Ma'idah.

In this passage, al-Quduri opens the Book of Purity by defining the obligatory acts (fards) of wudu. He grounds these in the Quranic verse of wudu and then reinforces them with six lines of evidence from the Quran, Sunnah, and Companion practice. Understanding these fards is essential for every Muslim, as they are conditions for the validity of prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that the fard (obligatory) acts of taharah are washing three limbs and wiping the head. Note that 'fard' here means the act is absolutely required; omission invalidates the wudu.
In Hanafi fiqh, fard is proven by qati (definitive) evidence, as opposed to wajib.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The author cites the Quranic verse (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:6) as the main proof. The verse commands washing face and hands to elbows, wiping the head, and washing feet to ankles.
The verse uses imperative verbs: 'اغسلوا' (wash) and 'امسحوا' (wipe), which indicate obligation per Hanafi usul.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative form (amr) implies wujub (obligation). The specification of limbs (face, hands, feet) and boundaries (elbows, ankles) defines the minimal obligatory coverage.
The Hanafi principle: 'Al-amr yufidu al-wujub' unless there is a qarinah (context) indicating otherwise.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools differ on wiping the head: some consider it part of the face or merely recommended. The Hanafi school holds it as a separate fard based on the conjunction 'wa' (and) in the verse.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf (mukhtalaf fih).
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi (relied upon) and is supported by the zahir al-riwayah. No intra-Hanafi difference exists.
Tarjih authority: The six proofs in the passage further strengthen the Hanafi stance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الطَّهَارَةِ

قَالَ اللهُ تَعَالَى {يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا إِذَا قُمْتُمْ إِلَى الصَّلاةِ} [المائدة: 6] الآيَةَ.

فَقَرْضُ الطَّهَارَةِ قَوْلُهُ غَسْلُ الْأَعْضَاءِ الثَّلَاثَةِ قَوْلُهُ: وَمَسْحُ الرَّأْسِ قَوْلُهُ

الوجه الأول: الآية لثبوت قَالَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى {يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا إِذَا قُمْتُمْ إِلَى الصَّلَاةِ فَاغْسِلُوا وُجُوهَكُمْ وَأَيْدِيَكُمْ إِلَى الْمَرَافِقِ وَأَمْسَحُواْ بِرُءُوسِكُمْ وَأَرْجُلَكُمْ إِلَى الْكَعْبَيْنِ وَإِن كُنتُمْ جُنُبًا فَأَطَهَّرُوا} (سورة المائدة 6)

الوجه الثاني: الحديث لثبوت «الطُّهُورُ شَطْرُ الْإِيمَانِ» (صحيح مسلم، باب فضل الوضوء، برقم: 223)

الوجه الثالث: الحديث لثبوت «مِفْتَاحُ الصَّلَاةِ الطُّهُورُ» (سنن الترمذي، باب ما جاء أن مفتاح الصلاة الطهور، برقم: 3)

الوجه الرابع: الآية لثبوت قَالَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى {وَالَّذِينَ يُؤْمِنُونَ بِالْغَيْبِ وَيُقِيمُونَ الصَّلَوةَ} (سورة البقرة 3)

الوجه الخامس: الحديث لثبوت «الصَّلَاةُ عِمَادُ الدِّينِ مَنْ أَقَامَهَا فَقَدْ أَقَامَ الدِّينَ» وَ «وَيْلٌ لِلْأَعْقَابِ مِنَ النَّارِ» (صحيح مسلم، باب وجوب غسل الرجلين بكمالهما، برقم: 240؛ صحيح البخاري، باب غسل الأعقاب، برقم: 165)

الوجه السادس: قول الصحابي لثبوت «أَتَانَا عَلِيٌّ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ وَقَدْ صَلَّى ثُمَّ غَسَلَ رَجُلَهُ الْيُمْى ثَلاثًا، وَرِجْلَهُ الشِّمَالَ ثَلاثًا» (سنن أبي داود، باب صفة وضوء النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم، برقم: 111/114)

أصول: وضو میں چار فرض ہیں: (۱) پورا چہرہ (۲) ہاتھوں کو کہنیوں تک (۳) پیروں کو ٹخنوں تک دھونا (۴) سر کا مسح کرنا۔
Book of Purity. Allah the Exalted says: O you who believe, when you stand for prayer... [Al-Ma'idah: 6]. So the fard of purification is his statement: washing the three limbs, his statement: and wiping the head, his statement: Aspect one: The verse for proof: Allah the Exalted says: O you who believe, when you stand for prayer, wash your faces and your hands to the elbows and wipe your heads and your feet to the ankles, and if you are in a state of major impurity, then purify yourselves (Surah Al-Ma'idah 6). Aspect two: The hadith for proof: 'Purity is half of faith' (Sahih Muslim, chapter on virtue of wudu, no. 223). Aspect three: The hadith for proof: 'The key to prayer is purification' (Sunan al-Tirmidhi, chapter on 'The key to prayer is purification', no. 3). Aspect four: The verse for proof: Allah the Exalted says: 'And those who believe in the unseen and establish prayer' (Surah al-Baqarah 3). Aspect five: The hadith for proof: 'Prayer is the pillar of religion; whoever establishes it has established religion' and 'Woe to the heels from the Fire' (Sahih Muslim, chapter on obligation of washing both feet completely, no. 240; Sahih al-Bukhari, chapter on washing heels, no. 165). Aspect six: The saying of the Companion for proof: 'Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, came to us after praying and then washed his right foot three times and his left foot three times' (Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter on description of the Prophet's wudu, no. 111/114). Principle: In wudu, there are four fards: (1) the whole face, (2) washing the hands to the elbows, (3) washing the feet to the ankles, (4) wiping the head.
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage opens the Book of Purity (Kitab al-Taharah). The author begins by citing the Quranic verse of wudu (Surah al-Ma'idah: 6). He then states the fard (obligatory) acts of taharah according to the Hanafi school: washing the three limbs (face, hands, feet) and wiping the head. The phrase 'قَوْلُهُ' likely refers to the author's own statement. He then provides six 'wujuh' (aspects/evidence) to support the obligation of these acts. The first evidence is the verse itself specifying the limbs. The second is the hadith 'Purity is half of faith' from Sahih Muslim. The third is the hadith 'The key to prayer is purification' from Sunan al-Tirmidhi. The fourth is a verse from Surah al-Baqarah (2:3) emphasizing establishment of prayer, implying necessity of wudu. The fifth combines hadiths about prayer being the pillar of religion and a warning about washing heels. The sixth is the action of Ali (RA) washing his feet, demonstrating the practice. The Urdu line summarizes the four fards of wudu clearly.

Key Terms
طهارة (taharah): Ritual purity, specifically the purification required for acts of worship like prayer.
فرض (fard): A legally obligatory act that must be performed; omission incurs sin.
الوجه (al-wajh): An aspect, viewpoint, or piece of evidence in support of a ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as presented in this passage, how many fards are there in wudu?
A) Three: washing face, hands, and feet
B) Four: washing face, hands, feet, and wiping the head
C) Two: washing face and hands
D) Six: as listed in the six aspects

Key Takeaway
The four fards of wudu in the Hanafi school are washing the face, washing the hands to the elbows, washing the feet to the ankles, and wiping the head, all proven by the Quranic verse in Surah al-Ma'idah.

Taharah — Purification

Elbows and Ankles Are Obligatory to Wash in Wudu
Ruling with two proofs for the inclusion of elbows and ankles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that elbows and ankles are included in the fard washing of wudu and explain the two proofs from this passage.

Core Idea
Washing the hands and feet in wudu includes the elbows and ankles as fard.

This passage addresses a specific point of wudu: the boundaries of the obligatory washing. The three founding imams of the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) agree that the elbows and ankles are included in the commanded washing, contrary to a fourth Hanafi scholar, Zufar. Two proofs are cited: the practice of Abu Hurayra and a hadith about bright limbs, plus a direct hadith that the Prophet ﷺ poured water on his elbows. The passage establishes that failing to wash these areas invalidates wudu.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Disagreement
Read the matn: 'The two elbows and the two ankles enter into the washing according to our three scholars, contrary to Zufar.' Recognize that the default Hanafi position includes these parts, and Zufar differs.
The 'three scholars' are Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
2
Analyze the First Proof (Practice of Abu Hurayra and Hadith of Ghurrah)
The text narrates that Abu Hurayra washed up to the upper arm and shin, and attributed this to the Prophet ﷺ. It also cites the hadith: 'You are the ones with bright faces and limbs (ghurr muhajjalun) on the Day of Resurrection due to completing the wudu, so whoever can, let him lengthen his brightness.' The command 'falyutil' (let him lengthen) supports extending the wash to include the elbows and ankles.
This proof combines a prophetic practice (fi'l) and a statement (qawl).
3
Analyze the Second Proof (Direct Hadith on Pouring Water on Elbows)
The hadith from Jabir states: 'When the Messenger of Allah ﷺ performed wudu, he poured water on his elbows.' This explicitly shows that the Prophet washed his elbows, proving they must be included.
This hadith is a direct proof (dalil) that the elbows are part of the wash.
4
Recognize the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Zufar's opinion that the elbows and ankles are not included is mentioned. The three scholars' agreement is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position. Understand that within the Hanafi school, there is a difference, but the majority view prevails.
Zufar is a respected Hanafi scholar, but his view is not taken for fatwa in this case.
5
Apply the Ruling
In practice, when performing wudu, one must ensure that water reaches the elbows (including the joint) and the ankles (the protruding bones). Omitting these parts deliberately or forgetfully invalidates the wash of that limb, and thus the wudu is incomplete.
This is a confirmed fard in the Hanafi school; there is no dispensation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَاب الطهارت
{3} وَالْمِرْفَقَانِ وَالْكَعْبَانِ يَدْخُلَانِ فِي الْغَسْلِ عِنْدَ عُلَمَائِنَا الثَّلَاثَةِ, خِلَافًا لِزُفَرَ.
وجه : (۱) قول التابعي لثبوت الْمِرْفَقَانِ وَالْكَعْبَانِ يَدْخُلَانِ فِي الْغَسْلِ اعَنْ نُعَيْمِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ الْمُجْمِرٍ، قَالَ: رَأَيْتُ أَبَا هُرَيْرَةَ يَتَوَضَّأُ فَغَسَلَ وَجْهَهُ فَأَسْبَغَ الْوُضُوءَ، ثُمَّ غَسَلَ يَدَهُ الْيُمْنَ حَتَّى أَشْرَعَ فِي الْعَضُدِ، ثُمَّ يَدَهُ الْيُسْرَى حَتَّى أَشْرَعَ فِي الْعَضُدِ، ثُمَّ مَسَحَ رَأْسَهُ، ثُمَّ غَسَلَ رِجْلَهُ الْيُمْنَى حَقَّ أَشْرَعَ فِي السَّاقِ، ثُمَّ غَسَلَ رِجْلَهُ الْيُسْرَى حَتَّى أَشْرَعَ فِي السَّاقِ"، ثُمَّ قَالَ: هَكَذَا رَأَيْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ يَتَوَضَّأُ وَقَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «أَنْتُمُ الْغُرُّ الْمُحَجَّلُونَ يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ مِنْ إِسْباغِ الْوُضُوءِ، فَمَنِ اسْتَطَاعَ مِنْكُمْ فَلْيُطِلْ غُرَّتَهُ وَتَحْجِيلَهُ» (صَحِيْحُ مُسْلِمَ، بَابُ اسْتِحْبَابِ إِطَالَةِ الْغُرَّةِ وَالتَّحْجِيلِ فِي الْوُضُوءِ، برقم: 246)
وجه : (٢) الحديث لثبوت الْمِرْفَقَانِ وَالْكَعْبَانِ يَدْخُلَانِ فِي الْغَسْلِ أَعَنْ جَابِرِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ, قَالَ: كَانَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ إِذَا تَوَضَّأَ أَذَارَ الْمَاءَ عَلَى مِرْفَقَيْهِ». (سنن الدارقطني بَابُ وُضُوءِ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ برقم (268) 272 / السنن الكبرى للبيهقي، بَابُ إِدْخَالِ الْمِرْفَقَيْنِ فِي الْوُضُوءِ وَبِهِ قَالَ عَطَاء، برقم: 256)
Book of Purification. {3} The two elbows and the two ankles enter into the washing according to our three scholars, contrary to Zufar. Proof (1): Saying of the follower (tabi'i) to establish that the elbows and ankles enter into the washing from Nu'aym ibn 'Abdillah al-Mujmir, he said: I saw Abu Hurayra performing wudu and he washed his face, completing the wudu, then he washed his right hand until he entered into the upper arm, then his left hand until he entered into the upper arm, then he wiped his head, then he washed his right foot until he entered into the shin, then he washed his left foot until he entered into the shin, then he said: Thus I saw the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) perform wudu, and he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'You are the ones with bright faces and limbs on the Day of Resurrection due to completing the wudu, so whoever among you can, let him lengthen his brightness and his brightness of limbs.' (Sahih Muslim, chapter on recommendation of lengthening the bright mark and limb brightness in wudu, no. 246). Proof (2): Hadith to establish the elbows and ankles enter into the washing from Jabir ibn 'Abdillah, he said: When the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) performed wudu, he poured water on his elbows. (Sunan al-Daraqutni, chapter on the wudu of the Prophet, no. 268/272; al-Sunan al-Kubra lil-Bayhaqi, chapter on including the elbows in wudu, and 'Ata said the same, no. 256).
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Book of Purification. The matn states that according to the three scholars (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani), the elbows and ankles are included in the commanded washing, contrary to Zufar who held they are not. The author then provides two pieces of evidence: (1) a saying of a tabi'i (Nu'aym) reporting that Abu Hurayra washed up to the upper arms and shins, demonstrating inclusion of elbows and ankles, and he attributed this practice to the Prophet ﷺ. Additionally, the hadith about the muhajjalun (those with bright limbs) encourages extending the washing to include these areas. (2) A hadith from Jabir that the Prophet ﷺ would pour water on his elbows, directly showing that the elbows are washed. This is a strong proof for the Hanafi position that the limit of washing the hands includes the elbows, not just the forearms. The ruling is that the commanded washing of the hands and feet in wudu necessarily includes the elbows and ankles.

Key Terms
المِرْفَقَانِ (al-mirfaqān): The two elbows; the joint between the upper arm and forearm.
الْكَعْبَانِ (al-ka‘bān): The two ankle bones; the protruding bones on each side of the foot.
الغَسْل (al-ghasl): The act of washing in wudu, which is fard.
زُفَر (Zufar): Imam Zufar al-'Abdi, a companion of Abu Hanifa who differed on this point.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the three Hanafi scholars, what is the ruling regarding the elbows and ankles in wudu?
A) They are not included in the washing.
B) They are included in the washing, contrary to Zufar.
C) They are included only if one intends to lengthen the ghurrah.
D) They are mustahabb but not fard.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that washing the elbows and ankles is part of the obligatory wash in wudu, supported by prophetic practice and direct hadith.

Obligatory Wiping of the Head: The Amount of the Forelock
Ruling with proof on the fard amount for head wiping.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that the obligatory amount for wiping the head is the forelock and explain the hadith evidence from al-Mughirah.

Core Idea
The minimum fard wipe is the forelock, not the whole head.

We often learn that wiping the head is fard in wudu, but what is the bare minimum? The Hanafi school, relying on the action of the Prophet ﷺ, holds that wiping just the forelock suffices. This lesson unpacks the hadith proof and the legal implication.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Wiping the head is fard in wudu; the text specifies the minimum is the forelock.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith of al-Mughirah ibn Shu'bah where the Prophet ﷺ wiped his forelock.
Sahih Muslim no. 274/633
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'masaha bi nasiatihi' shows that wiping the forelock alone fulfills the obligation.
Linguistically, 'bi' indicates partial coverage.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Shafi'is require wiping the entire head; Hanafis accept the forelock as sufficient.
5
Apply to practice
In Hanafi, wiping at least the forelock validates wudu; less than that invalidates it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
{4} وَالْمَفْرُوضُ فِي مَسْحِ الرَّأْسِ مِقْدَارَ النَّاصِيَةِ لِمَا رَوَى الْمُغِيرَةُ بْنُ شُعْبَةَ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ - صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ - أَتَى سُبَاطَةَ قَوْمٍ إِلَى آخِرِهِ.
{4} وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت الْمَفْرُوضُ فِي مَسْح الرَّأْسِ مِقْدَارَ النَّاصِيَةِ اعَنْ عُرْوَةَ بْنِ الْمُغِيرَةِ بْنِ شُعْبَةَ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، قَالَ: تَخَلَّفَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَتَخَلَّفْتُ مَعَهُ فَلَمَّا قَضَى حَاجَتَهُ وَمَسَحَ بِنَاصِيَتِهِ وَعَلَى الْعِمَامَةِ وَعَلَى خَفَّيْهِ، صَحِيحُ مُسْلِمَ، بَابُ الْمَسْحَ عَلَى النَّاصِيَةِ وَالْعِمَامَةِ، برقم: 274 / 633 / سُنَنُ أَبِي دَاوُدَ، بَابُ الْمَسْحِ عَلَى الْخَفَّيْنِ، برقم: 150)
وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت الْمَفْرُوضُ فِي مَسْحِ الرَّأْسِ مِقْدَارَ النَّاصِيَةِ اعَنْ ابْنِ الْمُغِيرَةِ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «مَسَحَ عَلَى الْخُفَّيْنِ، وَمُقَدَّمِ رَأْسِهِ وَعَلَى عِمَامَتِهِ» (صَحِيْحُ مُسْلِمَ، بَابُ الْمَسْحِ عَلَى النَّاصِيَةِ وَالْعِمَامَةِ، برقم: 634/274 سُنَنُ أَبِي دَاوُدَ، بَابُ الْمَسْحِ عَلَى الْعِمَامَةِ، برقم: (147) وَمَسَحَ بِنَاصِيَتِهِ وَعَلَى الْعِمَامَةِ صَحِيحُ مُسْلِمَ، برقم: 633/ سُنَنُ أَبِي داؤد، برقم: 150)
{4} And the obligatory in wiping of the head is the amount of the forelock, due to what al-Mughirah ibn Shu'bah narrated that the Prophet ﷺ came to the garbage dump of a people... to the end. {4} Proof (1): Hadith to establish that the obligatory in wiping the head is the amount of the forelock from 'Urwah ibn al-Mughirah ibn Shu'bah, from his father, he said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ lagged behind and I lagged with him; when he finished his need, he wiped with his forelock and over the turban and over his khuffs. (Sahih Muslim, chapter on wiping over the forelock and turban, no. 274/633; Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter on wiping over khuffs, no. 150). Proof (2): Hadith to establish that the obligatory in wiping the head is the amount of the forelock from Ibn al-Mughirah, from his father, that the Prophet ﷺ 'wiped over the khuffs, and the front of his head, and over his turban.' (Sahih Muslim, chapter on wiping over the forelock and turban, no. 634/274; Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter on wiping over the turban, no. 147; and 'he wiped with his forelock and over the turban' Sahih Muslim no. 633/ Sunan Abi Dawud no. 150).
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This is a ruling from the Book of Purification stating that the obligatory (fard) amount for wiping the head in wudu is the size of the forelock (nasiyah). The author cites the hadith of al-Mughirah ibn Shu'bah, who reported that the Prophet ﷺ wiped his forelock (nasiyah) during wudu. This indicates that wiping just the forelock is sufficient to fulfill the obligation, though the Sunna is to wipe the entire head. The Hanafi position is that the minimum requirement is wiping one-fourth of the head, or the front part; this is derived from the Prophetic action of wiping his forelock. The two proofs (wajh) from Sahih Muslim and Sunan Abi Dawud confirm this. The passage also alludes to the permissibility of wiping over a turban, which is a separate ruling, but the main point here is the minimal obligation.

Key Terms
النَّاصِيَة (al-nāsiyah): The forelock; the front part of the hair on the head.
مَسْح (masḥ): Wiping; an act that replaces washing for certain body parts in wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the obligatory amount for wiping the head in wudu according to this passage?
A) The entire head
B) The size of the forelock
C) One-fourth of the head
D) The back of the head

Key Takeaway
The minimum fard for wiping the head in wudu is the forelock, proven by the Prophet's action.

Usul Principle: Genus Enters the Specified Limit
Usul principle applied to wudu ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi usul principle that the genus enters the specified limit and apply it to identify which parts of a limb are included in a wudu command.

Core Idea
The genus enters the specified limit: the endpoint of a commanded limb is included in the obligation.

This lesson introduces a key Hanafi usul principle that determines the scope of a legal limit (ghayah). The source text links this to wudu: the command to wash the hands includes the elbows because the elbow is the natural limit of the hand. Understanding this principle clarifies why the Hanafi school rules that elbows are obligatory to wash.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle
Read the Arabic/Urdu passage and state the usul principle in your own words.
The principle is: 'When the genus is one, it enters into the specified limit.'
2
Define key terms
Define 'genus' (jins) and 'specified limit' (ghayah mu'ayyanah) as used in this context.
Genus refers to the category or kind; the limit is the endpoint defined by the Lawgiver.
3
Apply to wudu
Apply the principle to the wudu command: the hand is the genus, the elbow is the limit. Why does the elbow need to be washed?
Because the elbow is part of the hand genus, the limit includes it.
4
Consider a counterexample
Think of a scenario where the limit might be external to the genus. Does the principle still hold?
If the limit were something separate (e.g., 'to the wrist' while hand includes forearm), it would not be included.
5
Note the Hanafi reliance
Recognize that this principle is foundational for deriving rulings in purification and other areas.
It ensures a consistent method for interpreting limits across fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اصول: جنس ایک ہو تو غایت معیا میں داخل ہوتی ہے، لہذا وضو میں کہنیوں سمیت دھونا فرض ہے۔
Usul: When the genus is one, it enters into the specified limit; therefore, in wudu, washing including the elbows is fard.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage is a usul (principles of jurisprudence) note explaining a foundational legal maxim: 'When the genus is one, it enters into the specified limit.' This means that if the Quran or Sunnah commands washing a particular limb but specifies a limit (e.g., 'to the elbows' in Q5:6), then what is included within that limit (the elbows themselves) is part of the commanded act. The application here is in wudu: the command to wash the hands includes the elbows because the elbow joint is the natural limit of the hand. This supports the earlier ruling that elbows must be washed. The note is in Urdu and directly links the theoretical principle to the practical fiqh ruling.

Key Terms
جنس (jins): Genus; a category that includes multiple species under a single command.
غایت معیا (ghāyah mu‘ayyanah): A specified limit or endpoint defined by the Lawgiver.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the usul principle stated, how does the genus relate to the specified limit?
A) The genus is excluded from the limit.
B) The genus enters into the specified limit.
C) The genus determines the limit but is separate.
D) The limit applies only to the genus, not the species.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi usul principle that the genus enters the specified limit ensures that the endpoint of a commanded limb is included in the obligation.

Taharah — Purification
beginner

The Sunan of Wudu: Acts and Proofs
Ruling with proof listing the sunan acts of wudu.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four sunan of wudu listed in the text and identify the hadith proof for each.

Core Idea
The sunan of wudu are recommended acts proven by specific hadiths, not obligatory but regularly practiced by the Prophet.

In the Hanafi school, wudu has certain recommended acts (sunan) that enhance its perfection. This passage lists four sunan and provides their textual proofs from the Sunnah. Understanding these helps distinguish between obligatory (fard) and recommended (sunnah) elements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sunan
List the four sunan explicitly named in the passage: washing hands three times after waking, saying tasmiyah, using siwak, and rinsing the mouth (madmadah).
These are separate from the fard acts.
2
Find the dalil for each sunnah
Match each act to its hadith proof from the text. For hand washing: hadith of Abu Hurayra about not dipping hand until washed three times. For tasmiyah: hadith of Abu Sufyan 'no wudu for one who does not mention Allah's name'. For siwak: hadith 'were it not to burden my nation, I would have ordered siwak'. For madmadah: practice of 'Uthman.
The madmadah proof is a companion saying (qawl al-sahabi).
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how each hadith indicates a sunnah, not an obligation. For hand washing, the prohibition 'do not dip' before washing three times implies recommendation. For tasmiyah, the phrase 'no wudu' is interpreted by Hanafis as lacking perfection, not validity. For siwak, 'lawla' (were it not) shows the Prophet withheld an order, so it is recommended.
Hadiths are ahad (zanni) so they establish sunnah, not fard.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) consider tasmiyah wajib based on the same hadith. The Hanafi response is that the negation in the hadith refers to perfection, not invalidity, and other evidences support its sunnah status.
The mufta bihi in Hanafi school is that tasmiyah is sunnah muakkadah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
{5} سُنَنُ الطَّهَارَةِ قَوْلُهُ: لـ وَسُنَنُ الطَّهَارَةِ غَسْلُ الْيَدَيْنِ ثَلَاثَا قَوْلُهُ قَبْلَ إِدْخَالِهِمَا الْإِنَاءَ إِذَا اسْتَيْقَظَ الْمُتَوَفِّئُ مِنْ نَوْمِهِ لَ وَتَسْمِيَةُ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى فِي ابْتِدَاءِ الْوُضُوءِ ٣ وَالسَوَاكُ لِ وَالْمَضْمَضَةُ
(۳) الحديث لثبوت الْمَفْرُوضُ فِي مَسْحِ الرَّأْسِ مِقْدَارَ النَّاصِيَةِ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ زَيْدٍ ثُمَّ مَسَحَ رَأْسَهُ بِيَدَيْهِ، فَأَقْبَلَ بِهِمَا وَأَدْبَرَ ، بَدَأَ بِمُقَدَّمِ رَأْسِهِ حَتَّى ذَهَبَ بِهِمَا إِلَى قَفَاهُ، ثُمَّ رَدَّهُمَا إِلَى المَكَانِ الَّذِي بَدَأَ مِنْهُ، صَحِيحُ البُخَارِي، بَابُ مَسْحِ الرَّأْسِ كُلِهِ، برقم: 185 / سُنَنُ أَبِي دَاوُدَ، بَابُ صِفَةِ وُضُوءِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ، برقم: 118)
{5} وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت سُنَنُ الطَّهَارَةِ غَسْلُ الْيَدَيْنِ ثَلَاثًا عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ، أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «إِذَا اسْتَيْقَظَ أَحَدُكُمْ مِنْ نَوْمِهِ، فَلَا يَعْمِن يَدَهُ فِي الْإِنَاءِ حَتَّى يَغْسِلَهَا ثَلَاثًا، فَإِنَّهُ لَا يَدْرِي أَيْنَ بَاتَتْ يَدُهُ». (صَحِيْحُ مُسْلِمَ، بَابُ كَرَاهَةِ غَمْسِ الْمُتَوَفِّيِّ وَغَيْرِهِ يَدَهُ الْمَشْكُوكَ فِي نَجَاسَتِهَا فِي الْإِنَاءِ قَبْلَ غَسْلِهَا ثَلَاثًا ، برقم : 278 / 643، سُنَنُ التِّرْمِذِيِّ، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ إِذَا اسْتَيْقَظَ أَحَدُكُمْ مِنْ مَنَامِهِ، فَلَا يَغْمِسْ يَدَهُ فِي الْإِنَاءِ حَتَّى يَغْسِلَهَا، برقم: 24)
ل وجه : (۱)قول الصحابي لثبوت تَسْمِيَةُ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى فِي ابْتِدَاءِ الْوُضُوءِ اعَنْ أَبِي سُفْيَانَ حُوَيْطِبٍ، عَنْ جَدَّتِهِ، عَنْ أَبِيهَا ، قَالَ : سَمِعْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ، يَقُولُ: «لَا وُضُوءَ لِمَنْ لَمْ يَذْكُرْ اسْمَ اللَّهِ عَلَيْهِ سُنَنُ التِّرْمِذِي بَابٌ فِي التَّسْمِيَةِ عِنْدَ الْوُضُوءِ، برقم: 25، سُنَنُ أَبِي دَاوُدَ، بَابٌ فِي التَّسْمِيَةِ عِلَى الْوُضُوءِ، برقم: 101) وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت سُنَنُ الطَّهَارَةِ قَوْلُهُ: السَوَاكُ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «لَوْلَا أَنْ أَشُقَّ عَلَى الْمُؤْمِنِينَ - وَفِي حَدِيثِ زُهَيْرٍ عَلَى أُمَّتِي - لَأَمَرْتُهُمْ بِالسَّوَاكِ عِنْدَ كُلِ صَلَاةٍ صَحِيْحُ مُسْلِمَ بَابُ السَّوَاكِ، برقم: 589/252، سُنَنُ التِرْمِذِيّ، بَابُ ما جاء في السِّوَاكِ، برقم: 22، صَحِيْحُ البُخَارِي، بَابُ السِّوَاكِ، برقم: 244) وجه (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت سُنَنُ الطَّهَارَةِ قَوْلُهُ: الْمَضْمَضَةُ رَأَيْتُ عُثْمَانَ بْنَ عَفَّانَ سُئِلَ عَنِ الْوُضُوءِ «فَدَعَا بِمَاءٍ، فَأَتِي عِيضَأَةٍ فَأَصْغَاهَا عَلَى يَدِهِ الْيُمْنَ، ثُمَّ أَدْخَلَهَا اصول: سنت طریقہ یا راستہ کو کہتے ہیں، اور شریعت میں نبی اکرم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے جس عمل کو بطورِ عبادت اکثر دائمی کیا ہو اس کو سنت کہتے ہیں، اور جس کو بطور عادت دائمی کیا ہو تو اس کو مستحب کہتے ہیں۔
{5} The sunan of purification: His saying: 'And the sunan of purification are: washing the hands three times' his saying: 'before inserting them into the vessel when the one who wakes up from his sleep' and 'mentioning Allah the Exalted at the beginning of wudu' and 'the siwak' and 'the madmadah (rinsing the mouth)'. (3) Hadith to establish the obligatory in wiping the head is the amount of the forelock from 'Abdullah ibn Zayd: then he wiped his head with his hands, bringing them forward and backward, starting from the front of his head until he reached the nape, then returned them to the place he started. (Sahih al-Bukhari, chapter on wiping the entire head, no. 185; Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter on the description of the Prophet's wudu, no. 118). {5} Proof (1): Hadith to establish the sunan of purification: washing the hands three times from Abu Hurayra that the Prophet ﷺ said: 'When one of you wakes up from sleep, let him not dip his hand into the vessel until he washes it three times, for he does not know where his hand spent the night.' (Sahih Muslim, chapter on dislike of dipping the hand..., no. 278/643; Sunan al-Tirmidhi, no. 24). Proof (1): Saying of a companion to establish tasmiyah at the beginning of wudu from Abu Sufyan Huwaytib, from his grandmother, from her father, he said: I heard the Messenger of Allah ﷺ say: 'There is no wudu for one who does not mention the name of Allah upon it.' (Sunan al-Tirmidhi, chapter on tasmiyah at wudu, no. 25; Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter on tasmiyah over wudu, no. 101). Proof (1): Hadith to establish the siwak from Abu Hurayra that the Prophet ﷺ said: 'Were it not that I would burden the believers (or in the hadith of Zuhayr: my nation), I would have ordered them to use siwak for every prayer.' (Sahih Muslim, chapter on siwak, no. 589/252; Sunan al-Tirmidhi, no. 22; Sahih al-Bukhari, no. 244). Proof (1): Saying of a companion to establish the madmadah: 'I saw 'Uthman ibn 'Affan when asked about wudu, he called for water, then a vessel was brought, he tilted it over his right hand, then inserted it...' Usul: Sunnah is called a way or path, and in Shariah, an act that the Prophet ﷺ did regularly as worship is called sunnah, and what he did regularly as a habit is called mustahabb.
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage lists the sunan (recommended acts) of wudu and provides textual proofs. The sunan include: (1) washing the hands three times before inserting them into the water vessel upon waking from sleep, based on the hadith of Abu Hurayra; (2) saying tasmiyah (Bismillah) at the beginning, based on the hadith 'no wudu for one who does not mention the name of Allah'; (3) using siwak (toothstick), based on the Prophet's wish to command it; (4) madmadah (rinsing the mouth), based on the practice of 'Uthman. Note: There is also an inserted hadith about wiping the head entirely (from 'Abdullah ibn Zayd) which seems out of place but is included in the scanning. The author then gives a brief usul note in Urdu defining sunnah as regular worship acts, and mustahabb as regular habitual acts. This clarifies that these sunan are not obligatory but strongly recommended.

Key Terms
سُنَن (sunan): Plural of sunnah; recommended acts in wudu that are regularly performed by the Prophet.
تَسْمِيَة (tasmiyah): Saying 'Bismillah' at the start of wudu.
السَّوَاك (al-siwāk): Using a toothstick to clean the mouth.
الْمَضْمَضَة (al-madmaḍah): Rinsing the mouth with water.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Wiping the entire head
B) Washing the face
C) Using siwak
D) Washing the feet

Key Takeaway
The sunan of wudu are four: washing hands after sleep, tasmiyah, siwak, and madmadah, each proven by specific hadiths, and they are recommended, not obligatory.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate

Madmadah and Istinshaq as Sunnah of Wudu
Proving the sunnah of rinsing mouth and nose with hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on madmadah and istinshaq in wudu and identify the hadith evidence that supports the sunnah muakkadah classification.

Core Idea
Madmadah and istinshaq are emphasized sunnah, not fard — proof is the Prophet's action, not command.

In this lesson, we examine the status of rinsing the mouth (madmadah) and sniffing water (istinshaq) during wudu. The Hanafi school classifies these as sunnah muakkadah, while the Shafi'i school considers them wajib. We will analyze the hadith evidence cited by Hanafi jurists to establish the sunnah ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sunnah acts in wudu
Recognize that madmadah and istinshaq are among the sunan (recommended acts) of wudu according to the Hanafi school.
2
Locate the hadith evidence
Examine the two hadith cited: one showing the Prophet separating madmadah and istinshaq, and another showing they are performed from one handful of water.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the hadith proves sunnah: the Prophet's action is not accompanied by an imperative command, so it indicates recommendation, not obligation.
4
Recognize the ikhtilaf
Note that Imam al-Shafi'i considers these acts wajib based on the same hadith, interpreting consistent practice differently.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi position
The Hanafi relied-upon position is that madmadah and istinshaq are sunnah muakkadah, not wajib or fard.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطهارت
هو الاستنشاق ومسح الأذنين في الماء فتمضمض ثلاثًا واستنثر ثلاثًا، سنن أبي داود، باب صفة وضوء النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم، برقم: 108 / 112، صحيح مسلم، باب صفة الوضوء وكماله، برقم: 538/226) د. وجه : (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت سنن الطهارة قوله : الاستنشاق عن طلحة، عن أبيه، عن جده، قال: «دخلت - يعني - على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وهو يتوضأ، والماء يسيل من وجهه ولحيته على صدره، فرأيته يفصل بين المضمضة والاستنشاق» (سنن أبي داود، باب في الفرق بين المضمضة والاستنشاق، برقم: 139)
وجه: (٢)قول الصحابي لثبوت سنن الطهارة قوله: الاستنشاق أعن عبد الله بن زيد بن عاصم الأنصاري - وكانت له صحبة - قال: قيل له: " توضأ لنا وضوء رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: ..... ثم أدخل يده فاستخرجها فمضمض، واستنشق من كف واحدة (صحيح مسلم، باب في وضوء النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم، برقم: 555/235، صحيح البخاري، باب من مضمض واستنشق من غرفة واحدة، برقم: 140/191)
The book of purity: It is sniffing water and wiping the ears in water, then he rinsed his mouth three times and sniffed water three times. Sunan Abi Dawud... Aspect (1): The statement of a companion for establishing the sunan of purity, his saying: 'sniffing water' from Talhah from his father from his grandfather who said: 'I entered upon the Prophet, peace be upon him, while he was performing wudu, and water was flowing from his face and beard onto his chest, and I saw him separate between rinsing the mouth and sniffing water.' Aspect (2): ... from Abdullah ibn Zaid ibn Asim al-Ansari, who had companionship, he said: 'It was said to him: Perform wudu for us like the wudu of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him... Then he inserted his hand and brought it out, then rinsed his mouth and sniffed water from one handful.'
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on al-Quduri's matn, establishing the sunnah acts of wudu through hadith evidence. The first act is madmadah (rinsing the mouth) and istinshaq (sniffing water into the nose). The text states that the Prophet performed these actions three times each. Two hadith are cited: one from Talhah showing the Prophet separated madmadah and istinshaq, and another from Abdullah ibn Zaid showing he performed both from one handful of water. This proves that these acts are sunnah, not obligatory. The Hanafi school holds them as sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah).

Key Terms
الْمَضْمَضَة (al-madmadah): Rinsing the mouth with water during wudu.
الاِسْتِنْشَاق (al-istinshaq): Sniffing water into the nose and then expelling it during wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Wajib
C) Sunnah muakkadah
D) Mustahab

Key Takeaway
Madmadah and istinshaq are sunnah muakkadah in Hanafi wudu, proven by hadith but not obligatory.

The Ruling on Wiping the Ears: Sunnah with the Same Water
Proving the sunnah of wiping the ears and resolving the water dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wiping the ears, cite the primary hadith proof, and explain why separate water is not required.

Core Idea
The ears are part of the head; wiping them with the head's water is sufficient.

This passage establishes the sunnah of wiping the ears in wudu and clarifies a key dispute: whether fresh water is needed. The Hanafi school, relying on the explicit hadith 'The ears are from the head,' holds that the same water used for the head suffices. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, requiring fresh water. Let's examine the proofs and the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being discussed and its legal classification in the Hanafi school. The act is wiping the ears during wudu, and the ruling is sunnah (recommended), not fard or wajib.
The Hanafi school considers wiping the ears a sunnah act, meaning it is rewarding but omission does not invalidate wudu.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the primary proof cited for this ruling. The passage provides three hadith; the key one is from Abu Umamah where the Prophet said: 'The ears are from the head.'
This hadith is recorded in Sunan al-Tirmidhi and Sunan Abi Dawud.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the hadith proves the ruling. The explicit statement 'al-udhunani min al-ra's' indicates that the ears are included in the head for the purpose of wiping. Therefore, wiping the head covers the ears, and no separate water is needed.
This is a straightforward linguistic indication (dalala) – the part is included in the whole.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify the opposing view. Imam al-Shafi'i holds that wiping the ears is wajib and requires fresh water, citing the hadith of Abdullah ibn Zaid where the Prophet took new water for his ears.
The Shafi'i position considers the ears a separate member of wudu.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Understand why the Hanafi position is preferred. The explicit statement of the Prophet (qawl) takes precedence over his action (fi'l). The action of taking fresh water is interpreted as a recommendation (mustahab) rather than an obligation.
This is a common usul principle: when words and actions conflict, words are given priority if they are clear and general.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت سنن الطهارة قوله: مسح الأذنين أعن ابن عباس: «أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم مسح برأسه وأذنيه، ظاهرهما وباطنهما». (سنن الترمذي، باب مسح الأذنين ظاهرهما وباطنهما، برقم: 36، سنن أبي داود، باب صفة وضوء النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: (121)
وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت سنن الطهارة قوله: مسح الأذنين أعن أبي أمامة، قال: توضأ النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فغسل وجهه ثلاثًا ويديه ثلاثًا، ومسح برأسه، وقال: «الأذنان من الرأس» (سنن الترمذي، باب ما جاء أن الأذنين من الرأس، برقم: 37)
وجه : (۳) الحديث لثبوت سنن الطهارة قوله: مسح الأذنين سمع عبد الله بن زيد يذكر أنه رأى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم " يتوضأ فأخذ لأذنيه ماء خلاف الماء الذي أخذ لرأسه ". (السنن الكبرى للبيهقي، باب مسح الأذنين بماء جديد، برقم: 308)
اصول: حدیث میں الاذنان من الر اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ کان سر کا ہی حصہ ہے ، اسی معنی کر حنفیہ کے یہاں مسح اذن کے لئے الگ پانی ضروری نہیں، بر خلاف امام شافعی کے۔
Aspect (1): The hadith for establishing the sunan of purity, his saying: wiping the ears from Ibn Abbas: 'The Prophet, peace be upon him, wiped his head and his ears, their exterior and interior.' Aspect (2): ... from Abu Umamah, he said: The Prophet performed wudu and washed his face three times and his hands three times, and wiped his head, and said: 'The ears are from the head.' Aspect (3): ... He heard Abdullah ibn Zaid mentioning that he saw the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, perform wudu and take for his ears water different from the water he took for his head. Principle: From the hadith 'the ears are from the head' it is understood that the ear is part of the head; accordingly, according to the Hanafis, separate water is not necessary for wiping the ears, contrary to Imam al-Shafi'i.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage provides three hadith to establish the sunnah of wiping the ears (masah al-udhunain) during wudu. The first hadith from Ibn Abbas shows the Prophet wiped both the outside and inside of his ears. The second from Abu Umamah includes the explicit statement 'the ears are from the head.' The third from Abdullah ibn Zaid shows the Prophet took fresh water for his ears, separate from the water for his head. The usul note clarifies the Hanafi position: since the ears are part of the head, wiping them with the same water used for the head is sufficient; new water is not required. Imam al-Shafi'i holds that separate water is needed because the ears are a separate member. The Hanafi position relies on the hadith 'the ears are from the head' and the principle that the part follows the whole.

Key Terms
مسح الأذنين (masah al-udhunain): Wiping the ears during wudu, including both inner and outer parts.
الأذنان من الرأس (al-udhunani min al-ra's): A hadith phrase meaning 'the ears are from the head,' used as a proof that the ears are part of the head for wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because the ears are part of the head, as per the hadith.
C) Because water from the face suffices.
D) Because wiping ears is not sunnah.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that wiping the ears is sunnah and can be done with the same water as the head, based on the hadith 'al-udhunani min al-ra's'.

Sunnah Acts of Combing Beard and Fingers and Repeating Washes
Establishing sunan of combing beard and fingers and repeating washes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three sunnah acts of wudu related to combing the beard and fingers and repeating washes, and apply the distinction between thick and sparse beard to determine the requirement of water reaching the skin.

Core Idea
Combing the beard and fingers and washing each limb three times are sunnah; for thick beards, only external combing suffices.

This passage presents three additional sunnah acts of wudu that enhance the completeness of purification. Each act is supported by specific hadith evidence, demonstrating that these practices are deeply rooted in the Prophet's ﷺ practice. Understanding these sunan not only increases reward but also clarifies common misunderstandings about their obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Three Sunnah Acts
Read the opening line: 'And combing the beard and the fingers: and repeating the wash up to three times.' These are the three acts covered in this passage.
All three are sunnah, not fard or wajib.
2
Examine the Hadith Evidence
For each act, a hadith is cited. For combing the beard: from Uthman and Anas. For combing fingers: from Ibn Abbas with the command 'When you perform wudu, then comb between your fingers.' For repeating washes: the long hadith of Uthman's wudu washing each part three times.
The hadith for fingers uses an imperative (فخلل), but it is interpreted as sunnah because the command comes after wudu is already obligatory.
3
Understand the Hanafi Legal Classification (Sunnah)
The Hanafi position classifies these acts as sunnah. The proof is that the imperative 'fakhlil' (then comb) after the general obligation of wudu indicates recommendation unless there is evidence to raise it to wajib. There is no such evidence here.
Sunnah acts are rewarded when done but not sinful to omit.
4
Apply the Thick vs. Sparse Beard Principle
The passage notes: if the beard is thick, it is not necessary to reach the skin underneath; combing with fingers suffices. If the beard is sparse, water must reach the skin because the obligation of washing the face includes the beard if it is not dense.
This is a practical application of takhlil al-lihyah.
5
Note the Limit on Repeating Washes
Washing each limb up to three times is sunnah. Washing more than three times is makruh (disliked) because it goes beyond the sunnah and may be considered wasteful.
The hadith of Uthman shows exactly three times for each limb.

وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت سنن الطهارة قوله: تخليل اللحية أعن أنس يعني ابن مالك، «أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كان إذا توضأ أخذ كفا من ماء فأدخله تحت حنكه فخلل به لحيته» (سنن أبي داود، باب تخليل اللحية، برقم: 145)

And combing the beard and the fingers: and repeating the wash up to three times.
Aspect (1): The hadith for establishing the sunan of purity, his saying: combing the beard from Uthman ibn Affan, 'that the Prophet, peace be upon him, used to comb his beard.' Aspect (2): ... from Anas ibn Malik, 'that the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, when he performed wudu, took a handful of water and put it under his chin and combed his beard with it.'
And Aspect (1): ... for the fingers from Ibn Abbas, that the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'When you perform wudu, then comb between the fingers of your hands and feet.'
And Aspect (1): The statement of a companion for establishing the sunan of purity, his saying: repeating the wash up to three times. He saw Uthman ibn Affan call for a vessel and pour water on his hands three times, washing them, then put his right hand in the vessel, rinsed his mouth, sniffed water, then washed his face three times, his arms to the elbows three times, then wiped his head, then washed his feet three times to the ankles, then said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever performs wudu like this wudu of mine, then prays two rak'ahs without talking to himself, his previous sins will be forgiven.'
Principle: If the beard is thick, it is not necessary to reach the skin underneath, but he should comb it with his fingers. If the beard is sparse, he should reach the skin.
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage covers three additional sunan of wudu: takhlil al-lihyah (combing the beard), takhlil al-asabi' (combing between the fingers and toes), and takhlil al-ghusl ila al-thalath (repeating each wash up to three times). Two hadith support combing the beard: one from Uthman showing the Prophet combed his beard, and another from Anas showing he used water under his chin. For combing fingers, a hadith from Ibn Abbas commands combing between fingers of hands and feet. For repeating washes three times, the long hadith of Uthman's wudu demonstrates washing each part three times, with a promise of forgiveness. The usul note clarifies that for a thick beard, water need not reach the skin; combing with fingers suffices. For a sparse beard, water must reach the skin.

Key Terms
تخليل اللحية (takhlil al-lihyah): Running fingers through the beard during wudu to ensure water reaches the skin, or combing it out.
تخليل الأصابع (takhlil al-asabi'): Interlacing fingers and passing water between them, and similarly for toes.
تكرار الغسل إلى الثلث (tikrar al-ghusl ila al-thalath): Washing each limb (face, hands, feet) up to three times.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) It is sunnah, and for thick beards, water must reach the skin.
C) It is sunnah, and for thick beards, combing with fingers suffices.
D) It is wajib.

Key Takeaway
Combing the beard and fingers and washing each limb three times are sunnah acts that complete wudu; the beard's density determines the obligation of wetting the skin.

The Recommendation of Intention in Wudu
Ruling with proof: recommendation of intention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on intention (niyyah) in wudu and explain how the hadith 'Actions are but by intentions' supports it without making niyyah obligatory.

Core Idea
Niyyah in wudu is recommended for reward, not required for validity.

In this lesson, we examine a key difference between the Hanafi school and others: the status of intention in wudu. The passage from Al-Quduri states that niyyah is mustahab (recommended), and it cites the famous hadith of 'Umar as evidence. We will explore how the Hanafis interpret this hadith to reach a ruling that prioritizes the inherent purifying effect of water while still encouraging intentional worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What act is being discussed? What is the hukm level according to the Hanafi school? Note that the passage explicitly uses 'yustahab' (it is recommended).
The act is wudu, and the ruling is sunnah/mustahab for making intention.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? It is a hadith from Umar ibn al-Khattab, transmitted on the pulpit, that 'Actions are but by intentions.' Identify the source and its transmission.
The hadith is mutawatir in meaning, but its text is from Sahih al-Bukhari.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
How does this hadith prove the recommendation of niyyah? The hadith is general: actions are judged by intentions. For wudu, the intention distinguishes a mere wash from an act of worship. However, the Hanafi school argues that the validity of wudu does not depend on it because water itself purifies; the intention only affects reward.
The Hanafi usul principle: general texts (amm) can be interpreted as recommendations when there is a qarina (indication) that obligation is not intended.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Which school disagrees and why? The Shafi'i school considers niyyah fard for wudu. They argue that the hadith's imperative tone implies obligation, and wudu, like salah, requires intention to be an act of worship.
The Shafi'i position is based on a different usul interpretation: the command in the hadith is general and for acts of 'ibadah.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Which position is relied upon for fatwa in the Hanafi school? The Hanafi position (mustahab) is mufta bihi. The evidence is that wudu is a means of purification, and the goal (cleanness) is achieved even without intention. The hadith primarily relates to reward and sincerity.
The thamarah al-khilaf: in the Shafi'i school, wudu without intention is invalid; in the Hanafi school, it is valid but less rewarded.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
١٠ ويستحب للمتوضئ أن ينوي الطهارة
و وجه (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت سنن الطهارة قوله: يستحب للمتوضئ أن ينوي الطهارة عن عمر بن الخطاب رضي الله عنه على المنبر قال: سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول: «إنما الأعمال بالنيات، وإنما لكل امرئ ما نوى» (صحيح البخاري، كيف كان بدء الوحي إلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم؟، برقم: 1)
10. And it is recommended for the one performing wudu to intend purification.
And Aspect (1): The statement of a companion for establishing the sunan of purity, his saying: it is recommended for the one performing wudu to intend purification from Umar ibn al-Khattab, may Allah be pleased with him, on the pulpit, he said: I heard the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, say: 'Actions are but by intentions, and each person will have only what he intended.'
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage states that it is mustahab (recommended) for a person performing wudu to make the intention (niyyah) for purification. The evidence is the famous hadith of Umar: 'Actions are but by intentions.' In Hanafi fiqh, niyyah is not a condition for the validity of wudu; wudu is valid even without an explicit intention if the water is used for the purpose of purification. However, making the intention is recommended to gain reward and to align the act with the Prophet's practice. The hadith emphasizes that the reward depends on intention, so making niyyah ensures the act is worship ('ibadah) rather than mere habit.

Key Terms
النية (al-niyyah): The intention in the heart to perform an act of worship, here specifically intention to purify for wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It is fard (obligatory).
B) It is sunnah (recommended).
C) It is not required at all.
D) It is wajib.

Key Takeaway
Intention in wudu is recommended for reward, but not required for validity according to the Hanafi school.

The Sunan of Wudu: Proofs and Hanafi Classification
Lists four sunan acts of wudu with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four sunan acts of wudu, identify their proofs from the Sunnah, and explain why they are classified as sunnah muakkadah rather than fard.

Core Idea
The Prophet's action (fi'l) indicates recommendation, not obligation — the sunan of wudu perfect it but do not invalidate it.

In this passage from Al-Quduri, we encounter four acts that the Hanafi school considers sunan muakkada (emphasized recommendations) of wudu: combing the beard, combing the fingers, washing each limb three times, and making intention. Each act is supported by explicit hadith. We will walk through the proofs and understand why these acts are not obligatory, but highly encouraged. Special attention is given to the nuance of intention, which the school generally treats as a condition (shart) despite the text calling it 'mustahabb'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four sunan
List the four acts the author presents as sunan: combing the beard, combing the fingers, repeating the wash up to three times, and intending purification.
These are found in the first line of the passage.
2
Locate the hadith proof for each sunnah
For each act, find the specific hadith cited. Note the source (e.g., Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud, Bukhari).
The passage provides multiple hadith for some acts.
3
Analyze the evidence: why sunnah, not fard?
In Hanafi usul, the Prophet's habitual action (fi'l) indicates recommendation (sunniyyah) unless there is a command (amr) indicating obligation. Each hadith describes what the Prophet did or said in a directive form—examine the wajh al-dalalah.
The dalil_block in the analytical toolbox explains this.
4
Understand the classification of intention
Though the text says 'yustahabb' (recommended) for intention, the established Hanafi view holds intention as a condition (shart) for wudu. Note this tension and the reason: the matn reflects a minority position or a lenient phrasing.
The hanafi_position_box elaborates the nuance.
5
Apply the ruling to a practical scenario
Consider a person who performs wudu omitting all four sunan. The wudu remains valid but incomplete in reward. Understand the consequence: no invalidation, but loss of perfection.
The application_bridge provides a concrete example.

كِمْ تَخْلِيلُ اللَّحْيَةِ هُوَ الْأَصَابِعِ : وَتَكْرَارُ الْغَسْلِ إِلَى الثَّلَاثِ. ١٠ وَيُسْتَحَبُّ لِلْمُتَوَفِّى أَنْ يَنْوِيَ الطَّهَارَةَ (۱) الحديث لثبوت سُنَنُ الطَّهَارَةِ قَوْلُهُ: تَخْلِيلُ اللَّحْيَةِ اعَنْ عُثْمَانَ بْنِ عَفَّانَ، «أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ كَانَ يُخَلَّلُ لِيَتَهُ». (سُنَنُ التِرْمِذِيّ، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي تَخْلِيلِ اللَّحْيَةِ، برقم: (31 وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت سُنَنُ الطَّهَارَةِ قَوْلُهُ: تَخْلِيلُ اللَّحْيَةِ اعَنْ أَنَسٍ يَعْنِي ابْنَ مَالِكٍ، «أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ كَانَ إِذَا تَوَضَّأَ أَخَذَ كَفَّا مِنْ مَاءٍ فَأَدْخَلَهُ تَحْتَ حَنَكِهِ فَخَلَّلَ بِهِ لحيتَهُ» سُنَنُ أَبي دَاوُدَ، بَابُ تَخليل اللحية، برقم: (145) د وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت سُنَنُ الطَّهَارَةِ قَوْلُهُ: الْأَصَابِعِ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «إِذَا تَوَضَّأْتَ فَخَلَّلْ بَيْنَ أَصَابِع يَدَيْكَ وَرِجْلَيْكَ». (سُنَنُ التَرْمِذِيِّ، بَابٌ فِي تَخْلِيلِ الأَصابع، برقم: 39 / سنن النسائي، الْأَمْرِ بِتَخْلِيلِ الْأَصَابِعِ، برقم: 114) و وجه (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت سُنَنُ الطَّهَارَةِ قَوْلُهُ: تَكْرَارُ الْغَسْل إِلَى الثَّلَاثِ أَرَأَى عُثْمَانَ بْنَ عَفَّانَ دَعَا بِإِنَاءٍ، فَأَفْرَغَ عَلَى كَفَّيْهِ ثَلاثَ مِرَارٍ، فَغَسَلَهُمَا ، ثُمَّ أَدْخَلَ يَمِينَهُ فِي الإِنَاءِ، فَمَضْمَضَ، وَاسْتَنْشَقَ، ثُمَّ غَسَلَ وَجْهَهُ ثَلَاثًا، وَيَدَيْهِ إِلَى الْمِرْفَقَيْنِ ثَلَاثَ مِرَارٍ، ثُمَّ مَسَحَ بِرَأْسِهِ، ثُمَّ غَسَلَ رِجْلَيْهِ ثَلَاثَ مِرَارٍ إِلَى الكَعْبَيْنِ، ثُمَّ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ «مَنْ تَوَضَّأَ نَحْوَ وُضُوئِي هَذَا، ثُمَّ صَلَّى رَكْعَتَيْنِ لا يُحَدِّثُ فِيهِمَا نَفْسَهُ، غُفِرَ لَهُ مَا تَقَدَّمَ مِنْ ذَنْبِهِ» (صَحِيحُ البُخَارِيِّ، بَابُ الوُضُوءُ ثَلَاثًا ثَلاثًا ، برقم : 159، سُنَنُ أَبِي دَاوُدَ، بَابُ الوُضُوءُ ثَلَاثًا ثَلاثًا، برقم: 135) وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت سُنَنُ الطَّهَارَةِ قَوْلُهُ: يُسْتَحَبُّ لِلْمُتَوَفِّى أَنْ يَنْوِيَ الطَّهَارَةَ عُمَرَ بْنَ الخطَّابِ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ عَلَى المِنْبَرِ قَالَ: سَمِعْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ يَقُولُ: «إِنَّمَا الأَعْمَالُ بِالنِّيَّاتِ، وَإِنَّمَا لِكُلِّ امْرِئٍ مَا نَوَى صَحِيحُ البُخَارِي، كَيْفَ كَانَ بَدْءُ الْوَحْيِ إِلَى رَسُولِ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ؟، برقم: (1) وجه: (٢) الآية لثبوت سُنَنُ الطَّهَارَةِ قَوْلُهُ: يُسْتَحَبُّ لِلْمُتَوَضِي أَنْ يَنْوِيَ الطَّهَارَةَ ا﴿وَأَنزَلْنَا مِنَ السَّمَاءِ مَاءً طَهُورًا﴾ (سورة الفرقان، 25 آيت نمبر 48) وجه : (۳) الحديث لثبوت سُنَنُ الطَّهَارَةِ قَوْلُهُ: يُسْتَحَبُّ لِلْمُتَوَضِى أَنْ يَنْوِيَ الطَّهَارَةَ قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «هُوَ الطَّهُورُ مَاؤُهُ الحِلُّ مَيْتَتُهُ سُنَنُ التَّرْمِذِيِّ، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي مَاءِ البَحْرِ أَنَّهُ طَهُورٌ، برقم: 69) اصول: نیت دل کے ارادہ کا نام ہے، البتہ دل کیسا تھ زبان سے بھی کہ لے تو زیادہ بہتر ہے۔
How many: Combing the beard and combing the fingers, and repeating the wash up to three times. 10. And it is recommended for the one performing wudu to intend purification. (1) The hadith for establishing the sunan of purification - his statement: Combing the beard - from Uthman ibn Affan that the Prophet ﷺ used to comb his beard. (Sunan al-Tirmidhi, chapter on combing the beard, no. 31) (2) The hadith ... from Anas ibn Malik that when the Messenger of Allah ﷺ performed wudu, he took a handful of water and put it under his chin and combed his beard with it. (Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter on combing the beard, no. 145) And (1) The hadith ... his statement: The fingers - from Ibn Abbas that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'When you perform wudu, comb between the fingers of your hands and feet.' (Sunan al-Tirmidhi, chapter on combing fingers, no. 39; Sunan al-Nasa'i, no. 114) And (1) The statement of a companion for establishing the sunan ... his statement: Repeating the wash up to three times - I saw Uthman ibn Affan call for a vessel and pour water on his hands three times, washing them, then he put his right hand into the vessel and rinsed his mouth and nose, then washed his face three times, and his hands up to the elbows three times, then wiped his head, then washed his feet three times up to the ankles, then said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'Whoever performs wudu like this wudu of mine, then prays two rak'ahs without talking to himself, his previous sins will be forgiven.' (Sahih al-Bukhari, chapter on wudu three times, no. 159; Sunan Abi Dawud, no. 135) (1) The hadith ... his statement: It is recommended for the one performing wudu to intend purification - Umar ibn al-Khattab on the pulpit said: I heard the Messenger of Allah ﷺ say: 'Actions are but by intentions, and each person will have only what he intended.' (Sahih al-Bukhari, beginning of revelation, no. 1) (2) The verse for establishing the sunan ... his statement: It is recommended for the one performing wudu to intend purification - 'And We sent down from the sky pure water' (Surah al-Furqan, 25:48) (3) The hadith ... his statement: It is recommended for the one performing wudu to intend purification - The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'Its water is pure, its dead are permissible.' (Sunan al-Tirmidhi, chapter on sea water, no. 69) Principle: Intention is the name of the heart's resolve, but if one also utters it with the tongue, that is better.
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage is a ruling listing four sunan (recommended acts) of wudu, each supported by proofs from the Sunnah. The author, Al-Quduri, states the rulings first: combing the beard, combing the fingers, repeating each wash up to three times, and intending purification. Then he provides the evidence. For combing the beard, two hadith are cited: from Uthman and from Anas, showing that the Prophet ﷺ did so. For combing the fingers between hands and feet, a hadith from Ibn Abbas commands it. For repeating washes, a detailed description of Uthman's wudu is given, with the Prophet's promise of forgiveness. For intention, the famous hadith 'Actions are by intentions' from Umar is cited, along with a Quranic verse about pure water and a hadith about sea water. The Urdu note clarifies that intention is in the heart, but verbalizing is better. According to the Hanafi school, these acts are sunan muakkada (emphasized sunan) of wudu; omitting them does not invalidate wudu but reduces perfection. The combing of the beard applies only to those with thick beards; for thin beards, water must reach the skin.

Key Terms
تخليل اللحية (tahlil al-lihya): Combing the beard with wet fingers during wudu to ensure water reaches the skin.
سنن الطهارة (sunan al-tahara): The recommended acts of purification (wudu and ghusl) that are not obligatory.
نية (niyyah): Intention in the heart to perform an act of worship; in wudu, it distinguishes ritual purification from mere washing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on repeating each wash three times (as a sunnah) during wudu?
A) It is fard (obligatory).
B) It is sunnah muakkadah (emphasized recommended).
C) It is mustahabb (recommended, but not emphasized).
D) It is makruh (disliked).

Key Takeaway
The four sunan of wudu — combing beard, combing fingers, washing thrice, and intending — are recommended acts perfected by Prophetic practice; omitting them does not invalidate wudu but loses reward, though intention is a condition for validity in the relied-upon Hanafi view.

Taharah — Purification

Sunnah of Wiping the Entire Head in Wudu
Proof-texts for the sunnah of full head wiping.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wiping the entire head during wudu and identify the evidence from the Prophet's practice that supports it as sunnah.

Core Idea
Wiping the entire head is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah muakkadah), not an obligation; the fard is at least a quarter.

This passage from Al-Quduri asserts that one should encompass the entire head with wiping, then provides multiple hadith reports and companion statements as evidence. The Hanafi school considers wiping the entire head to be a highly recommended sunnah (sunnah muakkadah), while the obligatory (fard) minimum is only a quarter of the head. Through this lesson, you will learn how the Hanafi school uses prophetic action, companion practice, and follower testimony to establish a sunnah ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling from the text
Identify that Al-Quduri says 'yasta'wibu ra'sahu bi al-mash' (he should encompass his head with wiping). This is the sunnah act.
The ruling is about the recommended complete wipe, not the obligatory minimum.
2
Distinguish fard from sunnah in head wiping
In Hanafi fiqh, the fard in wudu is to wipe at least a quarter of the head. The entire head is sunnah muakkadah. The passage here is proving the sunnah, not the fard.
Common error: assuming the passage proves obligation.
3
Examine the first proof: hadith of Abdullah ibn Zaid
This hadith shows the Prophet (ﷺ) wiping his head once, moving his hands forward and backward. It demonstrates the method and the act of encompassing the head, but not the number of repetitions.
The hadith is from Sahih al-Bukhari and Muslim.
4
Examine the additional proofs: Uthman and Ali
The report from Uthman shows the Prophet wiping three times, and from Ali shows wiping once. Both indicate the permissibility of one or three, and the sunnah is to encompass the head each time.
The variation shows flexibility; the sunnah is in the coverage, not the count.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school holds that wiping the entire head is fard (obligatory). The Hanafi position is that the fard is only a quarter, and the rest is sunnah. This difference leads to different rulings on the validity of wudu when only part of the head is wiped.
This highlights how the same proofs can yield different rulings based on usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ال وَيَسْتَوْعِبُ رَأْسَهُ بِالْمَسْحَ الوجه (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت سُنَنُ الطَّهَارَةِ قَوْلُهُ: يَسْتَوْعِبُ رَأْسَهُ بِالْمَسْحَ اعَبْدَ اللَّهِ بْنَ زَيْدٍ عَنْ وُضُوءِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ ثُمَّ أَدْخَلَ يَدَهُ فِي الإِنَاءِ فَمَسَحَ بِرَأْسِهِ، فَأَقْبَلَ بِيَدَيْهِ وَأَدْبَرَ بِهِمَا، ثُمَّ أَدْخَلَ يَدَهُ فِي الإِنَاءِ فَغَسَلَ رِجْلَيْهِ» وَحَدَّثَنَا مُوسَى قَالَ: حَدَّثَنَا وُهَيْبٌ قَالَ: مَسَحَ رَأْسَهُ مَرَّةً صَحِيحُ البُخَارِي، بَابُ مَسْح الرَّأْسِ مَرَّةً، برقم: 192 ، صَحِيحُ مُسْلِمَ، بَابٌ فِي وُضُوءِ النَّبيِّ صلَّى الله عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ، برقم: 555/235) وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت سُنَنُ الطَّهَارَةِ قَوْلُهُ: يَسْتَوْعِبُ رَأْسَهُ بِالْمَسْحِ ارَأَيْتُ عُثْمَانَ بْنَ عَفَّانَ غَسَلَ ذِرَاعَيْهِ ثَلَاثًا ثَلَاثًا، وَمَسَحَ رَأْسَهُ ثَلَانَّا»، ثُمَّ قَالَ: «رَأَيْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فَعَلَ هَذَا» (سُنَنُ أَبِي دَاوُدَ، بَابُ صِفَةِ وُضُوءِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ، برقم: 110) وجه : (۳)الحديث لثبوت سُنَنُ الطَّهَارَةِ قَوْلُهُ: يَسْتَوْعِبُ رَأْسَهُ بِالْمَسْحِ افَأَقْبَلَ بِهِمَا وَأَدْبَرَ بَدَأَ مُقَدَّمِ رَأْسِهِ، ثُمَّ ذَهَبَ بِهِمَا إِلَى قَفَاهُ ثُمَّ رَدَّهُمَا حَتَّى رَجَعَ إِلَى الْمَكَانِ الَّذِي بَدَأَ مِنْهُ وَغَسَلَ رِجْلَيْهِ (صَحِيحُ مُسْلِمَ، بَابٌ فِي وُضُوءِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى الله عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ، برقم: 235 / 557، صَحِيحُ البُخَارِي، باب مسح الرأس گله، برقم: 185) وجه (۴) قول التابعي لثبوت سُنَنُ الطَّهَارَةِ قَوْلُهُ: يَسْتَوْعِبُ رَأْسَهُ بِالْمَسْحَ اقَالَ: رَأَيْتُ عَلِيًّا رَضِي اللَّهُ عَنْهُ تَوَضَّأَ فَغَسَلَ وَجْهَهُ ثَلَاثًا وَغَسَلَ ذِرَاعَيْهِ ثَلاثًا ، وَمَسَحَ بِرَأْسِهِ وَاحِدَةً» ، ثُمَّ قَالَ: «هَكَذَا تَوَضَّأَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ سُنَنُ أَبِي دَاوُدَ، بَابُ صِفَةِ وُضُوءِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ، برقم: 115، عن ابن عباس، برقم: 133)
And he should encompass his entire head with wiping. (1) The statement of a companion to establish the sunan of purification - his statement: He should encompass his head with wiping - from Abdullah ibn Zaid concerning the wudu of the Prophet ﷺ: then he put his hand into the vessel and wiped his head, moving his hands forward and backward, then he put his hand into the vessel and washed his feet. And Musa narrated to us: Wahb narrated to us: he wiped his head once. (Sahih al-Bukhari, chapter on wiping the head once, no. 192; Sahih Muslim, no. 555/235) (2) The hadith ... his statement: He should encompass his head with wiping - I saw Uthman ibn Affan wash his arms three times three, and wipe his head three times, then he said: I saw the Messenger of Allah ﷺ do this. (Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter on description of the Prophet's wudu, no. 110) (3) The hadith ... his statement: He should encompass his head with wiping - he moved them forward and backward, starting from the front of his head, then went with them to the back of his neck, then brought them back until he returned to the place he started from, and washed his feet. (Sahih Muslim, no. 235/557; Sahih al-Bukhari, chapter on wiping the head, no. 185) (4) The statement of a follower to establish the sunan of purification - his statement: He should encompass his head with wiping - he said: I saw Ali (رضي الله عنه) perform wudu: he washed his face three times, washed his arms three times, and wiped his head once, then said: This is how the Messenger of Allah ﷺ performed wudu. (Sunan Abi Dawud, no. 115, from Ibn Abbas, no. 133)
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage is a ruling stating that one should wipe the entire head during wudu, supported by four proofs: (1) The action of Abdullah ibn Zaid showing the Prophet's wiping moving forward and backward, done once. (2) The practice of Uthman showing three wipes. (3) A detailed description of the Prophet's wiping covering the whole head. (4) The action of Ali wiping once. In the Hanafi school, wiping the entire head is wajib (obligatory) in wudu, as it is part of the Quranic command 'wamsahu bi ru'usikum'. However, the sunnah includes the method: starting from the front, going to the back, and returning, and doing it once or thrice. The passage here proves the sunnah of encompassing the head and the manner. The Hanafi position is that the fard is to wipe at least a quarter of the head; wiping the entire head is sunnah muakkadah. But this text seems to present it as a sunnah act. The Urdu note at the end of page 22 about beard combing is separate.

Key Terms
استيعاب الرأس بالمسح (istī'āb al-ra's bi al-masḥ): Wiping the entire head, including the front, back, and sides, during wudu.
قول الصحابي (qawl al-ṣaḥābī): A statement or action of a companion used as evidence, considered a proof in Hanafi usul when it pertains to matters not open to opinion.
قول التابعي (qawl al-tābi'ī): A statement of a successor (tābi'ī) used as evidence, considered weaker than qawl al-sahabi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the minimum amount of the head that must be wiped for wudu to be valid?
A) The entire head.
B) A quarter of the head.
C) The front part only.
D) Any amount suffices.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between the obligatory minimum (quarter) and the highly recommended sunnah (full head), supported by prophetic practice and companion reports.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
10 min
Proofs for the Sunnah Acts of Wudu: Wiping the Entire Head and More
Commentary providing multiple proofs for sunan of wudu from hadith and athar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the proofs for the sunnah acts of wudu (especially wiping the entire head) and explain why they are classified as sunnah, not fard, in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The Prophet's practice (fi'l) establishes sunnah; Hanafi usul requires a command (amr) for fard, so these acts remain recommended.

This commentary on al-Quduri's matn dives deep into the proofs for the sunnah (recommended) acts of wudu. The author systematically cites Quran, hadith, and statements of Companions and successors to show that actions like wiping the entire head, maintaining order, starting with the right, and wiping the neck are firmly rooted in the Sunnah but are not obligatory. Understanding why these acts are sunnah—and not fard or wajib—is key to mastering Hanafi fiqh and the role of different types of evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling from the matn
Al-Quduri's matn states: 'He should wipe his entire head' (يستوعب رأسه بالمسح). The commentator labels this as sunnah, not fard. Locate this classification in the text.
The word 'sunah' appears in the headings (سُنَنُ الطَّهَارَةِ).
2
Examine the first proof: Quranic verse
The author cites verse 25:48 about pure water. Understand that this verse establishes the water must be pure, but does not directly prove the sunnah acts. It sets a general principle for purification.
This is a weak proof; the main proofs come from hadith.
3
Analyze the primary hadith proofs for wiping the head
The author gives several hadith: from Abdullah ibn Zaid (detailed description), from Uthman (wiping three times), from Ali (wiping once), and others. For each, note the action (fi'l) described and why it indicates sunnah rather than fard.
In Hanafi usul, a fi'l without an accompanying command indicates sunnah (max: mustahabb).
4
Distinguish between fard and sunnah in wudu
The commentary reinforces that wiping part of the head is fard (Quranic), but wiping the entire head is sunnah. Use the distinction to understand why multiple proofs are needed for the sunnah: they strengthen the recommendation but do not change the ruling.
The farḍ is derived from the Quranic command 'wip your heads' (interpreted as part); the sunnah is from the Prophet's practice.
5
Apply to other sunnah acts
The matn lists other sunan: tartib (order), tayammun (starting with right), tawali (continuity), and wiping the neck. The commentary provides proofs for each (e.g., hadith of Aisha on tayammun). See how the same pattern applies: the Prophet's practice or statements establish recommendation.
These are also considered sunnah mu'akkadah.

Book of Purification. And he should encompass his head with wiping. Proof (2): The verse for establishing the sunan of purification, his statement: It is recommended for the one performing wudu to intend purification: "And We sent down from the sky pure water." Proof (3): The hadith for establishing the sunan of purification, his statement: It is recommended for the one performing wudu to intend purification. The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: "Its water is pure, its dead animal is permissible." ..... Proof (1): Statement of a Companion for establishing the sunan of purification, his statement: He should encompass his head with wiping. Abdullah ibn Zaid [narrated] about the wudu of the Prophet (peace be upon him): Then he inserted his hand into the vessel and wiped his head, bringing his hands forward and back, then inserted his hand into the vessel and washed his feet. Proof (2): Hadith for establishing the sunan of purification, his statement: He should encompass his head with wiping. I saw Uthman ibn Affan wash his forearms three times and wipe his head three times, then he said: I saw the Messenger of Allah do this. Proof (3): Hadith for establishing the sunan of purification, his statement: He should encompass his head with wiping. Then he brought them forward and back: he began at the front of his head, then went with them to the back of his neck, then returned them until he came back to the place he started from, and washed his feet. Proof (4): Statement of a Tabi'i for establishing the sunan of purification, his statement: He should encompass his head with wiping. He said: I saw Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) perform wudu: he washed his face three times, washed his forearms three times, and wiped his head once, then he said: "This is how the Messenger of Allah performed wudu." Principle: Intention is the name of the heart's resolve; however, if he also speaks it with his tongue, it is better. And he should arrange the wudu, beginning with what Allah Almighty mentioned first, and with the right side, and continuity, and wiping the neck. Proof (5): Hadith for establishing the sunan of purification, his statement: He should encompass his head with wiping. He wiped his head with water not leftover from his hand. Proof (1): Statement of a Companion for establishing the sunan of purification, his statement: He should encompass his head with wiping. Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) said: "I do not mind, when I complete my wudu, with which of my limbs I begin." Proof (1): Hadith for establishing the sunan of purification, his statement: He should encompass his head with wiping. From Aishah, she said: The Prophet (peace be upon him) liked to begin with the right in putting on his sandals, combing his hair, his purification, and in all his affairs. 12. Proof (a): Statement of a Companion for establishing the sunan of purification, his statement: He should encompass his head with wiping. That Abdullah ibn Umar urinated in the market, then performed wudu and washed his face, hands, and wiped his head. Then he was called for a funeral prayer while entering the mosque, so he wiped over his leather socks, then prayed over it. 15. Proof (1): Hadith for establishing the sunan of purification, his statement: He should encompass his head with wiping. From Ibn Umar that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: "Whoever performs wudu and wipes with his hands over his neck will be protected from the shackles on the Day of Resurrection." Proof (2): Statement of a Companion for establishing the sunan of purification, his statement: He should encompass his head with wiping. Laith narrated from Talhah from his father from his grandfather that he saw the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) wiping his head until he reached the qadhāl (nape of the neck) and what adjoins it from the front of the neck once. Glossary: yurattib: to arrange in order; bil-mayāmin: to start with the right side; at-tawāli: consecutively.
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on al-Quduri's matn deals with the sunan (recommended acts) of wudu. The commentator provides multiple proofs (wujuh) for each sunnah, primarily from hadith and statements of Companions and Tabi'un. The first sunnah discussed is wiping the entire head (isti'ab al-ra's bil-mash). The author presents a Quranic verse (25:48) to establish the principle that water used must be pure, then several hadith: the hadith about sea water being pure and its dead animal permissible, the detailed description of the Prophet's wudu from Abdullah ibn Zaid, the narration of Uthman showing the practice, and the report from Ali. The passage also includes an Urdu principle about intention (niyyah) being in the heart but better uttered. Then the matn continues: 'And he should arrange the wudu, beginning with what Allah began with, and with the right side, and continuity, and wiping the neck.' For these, further proofs are given: a hadith about wiping the head with fresh water (not leftover), the statement of Ali that order does not matter (indicating this is sunnah not fard), and the hadith of Aishah about the Prophet's love of starting with the right. Then a report from Ibn Umar shows wiping over socks after wudu, indicating continuity of practice. Finally, a hadith about wiping the neck promising protection from shackles, and another about the Prophet wiping till the nape of the neck. The glossary explains key Arabic terms. Throughout, the commentator relies on authentic sources (Sahih al-Bukhari, Muslim, Sunan Abi Dawud, etc.) to establish these acts as sunnah, not fard. The overall argument is that these practices are firmly rooted in the Sunnah and should be followed to perfect one's wudu.

Key Terms
سُنَن الطَّهَارَة (sunan al-taharah): The recommended acts of purification, particularly in wudu, as distinct from the obligatory (fard) acts.
يَسْتَوْعِبُ رَأْسَهُ بِالْمَسْحَ (yasta'wibu ra'sahu bil-mas'hi): To wipe the entire head (including ears) during wudu, not just a part, as a recommended act.
التَّوَالِي (al-tawali): Continuity in wudu, meaning to wash each limb without significant delay between them.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, what is the ruling on wiping the entire head (isti'ab al-ra's) during wudu?
A) Fard (obligatory)
B) Wajib (necessary)
C) Sunnah (recommended)
D) Mubah (permissible)

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, wiping the entire head, maintaining order, starting with the right, continuity, and wiping the neck are all sunnah mu'akkadah—proven by the Prophet's practice—and omitting them does not invalidate wudu, but performing them earns greater reward.
