Taharah — Purification
beginner
8 min
The Recommended Acts (Sunan) of Wudu
Ruling with proof for sunan of wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four sunan of wudu according to the Hanafi school and explain the evidence from hadith and companion practice that establishes each.

Core Idea
Sunan of wudu are recommended, not obligatory — omission does not invalidate but loses reward.

Wudu has obligatory (fard) components and recommended (sunnah) ones. This passage identifies four key sunan: performing actions in the Quranic order, starting with the right side, maintaining continuity, and wiping the neck. Strongly emphasized, they are not required for validity. The text then provides a series of proofs from prophetic practice and companion statements to confirm their sunnah status.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four sunan
Read the opening sentence of the passage. It names the sunan: arrangement (tartib), right side (yamin), continuity (tawali), and wiping the neck (masah al-raqaba).
All four are considered sunnah mu'akkadah in the Hanafi school.
2
Locate the proof for each sunnah
The passage provides multiple proofs (wujuh). For arrangement: a saying of Ali indicating no specific order is required. For right side: Aisha's hadith. For continuity: action of Ibn Umar. For wiping neck: hadith from Ibn Umar and another from Musnad Ahmad.
Each proof is introduced with 'wajh' (the evidence).
3
Analyze why each proof supports sunnah, not fard
Hanafi methodology distinguishes between an emphatic command (fard) and a recommended act (sunnah). These proofs show prophetic preference or action, not a binding imperative. For example, Ali's statement explicitly says order does not matter, so it is not wajib.
This step requires applying Hanafi usul: a demand becomes wajib if definitive; otherwise it is sunnah.
4
Note cross-madhhab difference on arrangement
Some schools, especially Shafi'is, consider arrangement (tartib) wajib based on the Quranic order and prophetic consistency. The Hanafi position, relying on Ali's statement and the nature of the proofs, holds it is sunnah. This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
The practical difference: a Hanafi's wudu is valid without order; a Shafi'i considers it invalid without order.

وَيُرَتِّبُ الْوُضُوءَ فَيَبْدَأُ بِمَا بَدَأَ اللهُ تَعَالَى بِذِكْرِهِ وَبِالْمَيَامِنِ وَالتَّوَالِي, وَمَسْحُ الرَّقَبَةِ.  وَجْهُ الْحَدِيثِ لِثُبُوتِ سُنَنِ الطَّهَارَةِ قَوْلُهُ: يَسْتَوْعِبُ رَأْسَهُ بِالْمَسْحِ أَوْ مَسَحَ بِرَأْسِهِ بِمَاءٍ غَيْرِ فَضْلِ يَدِهِ. صَحِيحُ مُسْلِمَ بَابٌ فِي وُضُوءِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ، بَرَقْم: 559/236. وَجْهُ قَوْلِ الصَّحَابِيِّ: قَالَ عَلِيٌّ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ: «مَا أُبَالِي إِذَا أَثْمَمْتُ وُضُوئِي بِأَيِّ أَعْضَائِي بَدَأْتُ» (سُنَنُ الدَّارَقُطْنِيِّ، بَابُ مَا رُوِيَ فِي جَوَازِ تَقْدِيمِ غَسْلِ الْيَدِ الْيُسْرَى عَلَى الْيُمْنَى، بَرَقْم: 293). وَجْهُ الْحَدِيثِ: عَنْ عَائِشَةَ قَالَتْ: كَانَ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ يُعْجِبُهُ التَّيَمُّنُ فِي تَنَعْلِهِ وَتَرَجُلِهِ وَظُهُورِهِ وَفِي شَأْنِهِ كُلِّهِ (صَحِيحُ البُخَارِيِّ، بَابُ التَّيَمُّنِ فِي الوُضُوءِ وَالغَسْلِ، بَرَقْم: 168). وَجْهُ قَوْلِ الصَّحَابِيِّ: أَنَّ عَبْدَ اللَّهِ بْنَ عُمَرَ بَالَ بِالسُّوقِ ثُمَّ تَوَضَّأَ وَغَسَلَ وَجْهَهُ وَيَدَيْهِ وَمَسَحَ بِرَأْسِهِ ثُمَّ دُعِيَ جِنَازَةٍ لِيُصَلِّيَ عَلَيْهَا حِينَ دَخَلَ الْمَسْجِدَ فَمَسَحَ عَلَى خُفَّيْهِ ثُمَّ صَلَّى عَلَيْهَا (الْمُوَطَّأُ للإِمَامِ مَالِكٍ، مَا جَاءَ فِي الْمَسْحِ عَلَى الْخُفَّيْنِ، بَرَقْم: 101). وَجْهُ الْحَدِيثِ: عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «مَنْ تَوَضَّأَ وَمَسَحَ بِيَدَيْهِ عَلَى عُنُقِهِ وُقِيَ الْغُلَّ يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ» (التَّلْخِيصُ الحَبِيرُ، بَابُ سُنَنِ الوُضُوءِ، ج:1، ص:34). وَجْهُ قَوْلِ الصَّحَابِيِّ: حَدَّثَنَا لَيْفٌ عَنْ طَلْحَةَ عَنْ أَبِيهِ عَنْ جَدِّهِ أَنَّهُ رَأَى رَسُولَ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ يَمْسَحُ رَأْسَهُ حَتَّى بَلَغَ الْقَذَالَ وَمَا يَلِيهِ مِنْ مُقَدَّمِ الْعُنُقِ مَرَّةً (مُسْنَدُ أَحْمَدَ، ج:4، ص:531).
He arranges the wudu, beginning with what Allah the Exalted began mentioning, and with the right side, and continuity, and wiping the neck. The evidence from hadith for establishing the sunan of purification: his saying: 'He encompasses his head with wiping' or 'he wiped his head with water not from the excess of his hand' – Sahih Muslim, chapter on the wudu of the Prophet, no. 559/236. The evidence from a companion's saying: Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) said: 'I do not mind, if I have completed my wudu, with which of my limbs I began' – Sunan al-Daraqutni, no. 293. The evidence from hadith: from Aisha: 'The Prophet liked to start with the right in putting on sandals, combing hair, purification, and in all his affairs' – Sahih al-Bukhari, no. 168. The evidence from a companion's saying: that Abdullah ibn Umar relieved himself in the market, then performed wudu, washed his face and hands, wiped his head, then was called for a funeral prayer as he entered the mosque, so he wiped over his leather socks and then prayed over it – Muwatta of Imam Malik, no. 101. The evidence from hadith: from Ibn Umar that the Prophet said: 'Whoever performs wudu and wipes his hands over his neck will be protected from shackles on the Day of Resurrection' – Talkhis al-Habir, chapter on sunan of wudu, vol.1, p.34. The evidence from a companion's saying: Laith narrated from Talha from his father from his grandfather that he saw the Messenger of Allah wipe his head until he reached the back of the head and what follows from the front of the neck once – Musnad Ahmad, vol.4, p.531.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It lists the sunan (recommended acts) of wudu according to the Hanafi school: arranging the limbs in the order mentioned in the Qur'an (face, hands, head, feet), starting with the right side, performing the actions consecutively without a long gap, and wiping the neck. The author then provides multiple proofs (wujuh) for these sunan. The first proof is a hadith from Sahih Muslim describing the Prophet's wudu, indicating that he wiped his head with water not leftover from his hands. The second proof is a saying of Ali that the order of limbs is not obligatory, implying it is sunnah. The third proof is a hadith from Aisha showing the Prophet's general preference for starting with the right. The fourth is a companion action of Ibn Umar who, after urinating, washed his face and hands, wiped his head, and then later wiped his socks when called for prayer, demonstrating continuity. The fifth is a hadith about wiping the neck. The sixth is another hadith about wiping the head down to the neck. Together, these establish that these acts are sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized recommended) in wudu.

Key Terms
سنن الطهارة (sunan al-tahara): The recommended acts of purification (wudu) that are not obligatory but meritorious.
التوالي (al-tawali): Performing the acts of wudu consecutively without a lengthy gap between them.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on wiping the neck during wudu?
A) Fard
B) Wajib
C) Sunnah
D) Mustahabb

Key Takeaway
The four sunan of wudu—order, right side, continuity, and wiping the neck—are recommended; omitting them does not invalidate wudu but loses reward.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
7 min
The Nullifiers of Wudu: Hanafi Position and Proofs
Lists the things that invalidate wudu and provides Quranic and hadith proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi list of nullifiers of wudu and apply the condition that blood/pus must flow beyond the exit point to nullify wudu.

Core Idea
Only flowing blood/pus nullifies wudu; mere appearance does not.

This lesson examines the nullifiers of wudu as defined in the Hanafi school. While all schools agree that excretion from the private parts breaks wudu, the Hanafis uniquely require that blood and pus must flow to an area requiring washing. We will explore the textual proofs from the Quran and Sunnah that support this position, and clarify the key condition of 'flow' (tajawuz).

Guided Path
1
Identify the nullifiers
List the things that break wudu according to the Hanafi school as presented in the source: anything from the two passages, and blood or pus that flows beyond the exit point.
Note that the source uses 'al-ma'ani al-naqida' (the nullifying meanings) to refer to these causes.
2
Locate the condition for blood and pus
Find the phrase indicating that blood/pus must flow: 'tajawaza ila mawdi' yalhaquhu hukm al-tathir' (flows to a place where the ruling of washing applies). This is the key condition distinguishing Hanafis.
Flow means the liquid moves beyond the wound or exit point.
3
Examine the Quranic evidence
Analyze how Surah al-Ma'idah 5:6 proves that excretion nullifies wudu. The phrase 'jā'a aḥadun minkum min al-ghā'iṭ' literally 'one of you comes from relieving himself' indicates that the act of excretion requires purification, implying wudu is broken.
The word 'ghā'iṭ' originally means 'depression', but idiomatically refers to the act of defecation.
4
Examine the hadith evidence
Review the hadiths cited: (1) Safwan ibn Ammal: wiping over socks is not allowed except for janabah, but defecation, urine, and sleep break wudu. (2) Aisha: vomiting, nosebleed, madhy require wudu. (3) Fatimah bint Hubaysh: istihadah (chronic bleeding) does not break wudu because it is a vein, not menstruation. This supports that flowing blood from a wound does break wudu, but continuous non-menstrual bleeding is treated differently (the hadith does not require wudu for each prayer).
The hadith of Fatimah is used to show that if blood flows continuously, it is excused and does not nullify wudu for each occurrence.
5
Apply the flow condition
Given a scenario: a person gets a small cut that bleeds a drop but the blood does not flow beyond the cut. Apply the Hanafi principle: since there is no flow (tajawuz), wudu remains valid.
This is a common practical difference from other schools.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْمَعَانِي النَّاقِضَةُ لِلْوُضُوءِ كُلُّ مَا خَرَجَ مِنْ السَّبِيلَيْنِ ، وَالدَّمُ ، وَالْقَيْحُ إِذَا خَرَجَا مِنْ الْبَدَنِ فَتَجَاوَزَ إِلَى مَوْضِعٍ يَلْحَقُهُ حُكْمُ التَّطْهِيرِ. وَجْهُ الْآيَةِ لِثُبُوتِ الْمَعَانِي النَّاقِضَةِ: ﴿وَإِن كُنتُم جُنُبًا فَاطَّهَّرُوا وَإِن كُنتُم مَّرْضَىٰ أَوْ عَلَىٰ سَفَرٍ أَوْ جَاءَ أَحَدٌ مِنكُم مِّنَ الْغَائِطِ أَوْ لَامَسْتُمُ النِّسَاءَ فَلَمْ تَجِدُوا مَاءً فَتَيَمَّمُوا صَعِيدًا طَيِّبًا﴾ (سورة المائدة 5:6). وَجْهُ قَوْلِ الصَّحَابِيِّ: عَنْ صَفْوَانَ بْنِ عَمَّالٍ قَالَ: كَانَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ يَأْمُرُنَا إِذَا كُنَّا سَفَرًا أَنْ لَا نَنْزِعَ خِفَافَنَا ثَلَاثَةَ أَيَّامٍ وَلَيَالِيَهُنَّ إِلَّا مِنْ جَنَابَةٍ، وَلَكِنْ مِنْ غَائِطٍ وَبَوْلٍ وَنَوْمٍ (سُنَنُ التِّرْمِذِيِّ، بَابُ الْمَسْحِ عَلَى الْخُفَّيْنِ، بِرَقْم: 96). وَجْهُ الْآيَةِ لِثُبُوتِ النَّاقِضَةِ: ﴿قُل لَّا أَجِدُ فِي مَا أُوحِيَ إِلَيَّ مُحَرَّمًا عَلَىٰ طَاعِمٍ يَطْعَمُهُ إِلَّا أَن يَكُونَ مَيْتَةً أَوْ دَمًا مَّسْفُوحًا﴾ (سورة الأنعام 6:143). وَجْهُ الْحَدِيثِ: عَنْ عَائِشَةَ قَالَتْ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «مَنْ أَصَابَهُ قَيْءٌ أَوْ رُعَافٌ أَوْ فَلَسٌ أَوْ مَذْيٌ فَلْيَنْصَرِفْ فَلْيَتَوَضَّأْ ثُمَّ لِيَبْنِ عَلَىٰ صَلَاتِهِ، وَهُوَ فِي ذَلِكَ لَا يَتَكَلَّمُ» (سُنَنُ ابْنِ مَاجَةَ، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي الْبِنَاءِ عَلَى الصَّلَاةِ، بِرَقْم: 1221). وَجْهُ الْحَدِيثِ: عَنْ عَائِشَةَ قَالَتْ: جَاءَتْ فَاطِمَةُ بِنْتُ حُبَيْشٍ إِلَى النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فَقَالَتْ: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ إِنِّي امْرَأَةٌ أَسْتَحَاضُ فَلَا أَظْهُرُ أَفَأَدَعُ الصَّلَاةَ؟ فَقَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «لَا، إِنَّمَا ذَلِكِ عِرْقٌ، وَلَيْسَ بِحَيْضٍ، فَإِذَا أَقْبَلَتْ حَيْضَتُكِ فَدَعِي الصَّلَاةَ، وَإِذَا أَدْبَرَتْ فَاغْسِلِي عَنْكِ الدَّمَ ثُمَّ صَلِّي» (صَحِيحُ البُخَارِيِّ، بَابُ غَسْلِ الدَّمِ، بِرَقْم: 228). أُصُول: زَخْمٍ يَا چُوٹ لَگِی اَور خُون ظاہِر ہُوا لیکِن اَپنے مَقَام سے تَجاوُز نَہِیں کِیا، بَہا نَہِیں تو نَاقِض وُضُو نَہِیں ہے۔
And the nullifying meanings of wudu: everything that exits from the two passages, and blood, and pus if they exit from the body and flow to a place where the ruling of purification applies. The evidence from the verse for establishing the nullifiers: 'If you are in a state of janabah, purify yourselves. And if you are ill or on a journey or one of you comes from relieving himself or you have touched women and you do not find water, then perform tayammum with clean earth' (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:6). The evidence from a companion's saying: from Safwan ibn Ammal: The Messenger of Allah commanded us when we were traveling not to remove our leather socks for three days and nights except from janabah, but from defecation, urine, and sleep (Sunan al-Tirmidhi, no. 96). The evidence from the verse for establishing the nullifier: 'Say, I do not find in what was revealed to me anything forbidden to an eater to eat except that it be carrion or spilled blood' (Surah al-An'am 6:143). The evidence from hadith: from Aisha: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever experiences vomiting, nosebleed, [؟] or madhy, let him leave and perform wudu, then build upon his prayer, and during that he does not speak' (Sunan Ibn Majah, no. 1221). The evidence from hadith: from Aisha: Fatimah bint Hubaysh came to the Prophet and said: O Messenger of Allah, I have istihadah and I do not become pure, should I abandon prayer? He said: 'No, that is (from) a vein and not menstruation. When your menstruation comes, leave prayer, and when it ends, wash the blood from yourself and then pray' (Sahih al-Bukhari, no. 228). Principle: A wound or injury occurs and blood appears but does not flow from its place, then it does not nullify wudu.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, listing the nullifiers of wudu (nawaqid). The Hanafi position: wudu is invalidated by (1) anything exiting from the front or back passage (urine, stool, wind, etc.), (2) blood or pus that exits from the body and flows beyond the point of exit to an area requiring washing (i.e., it must be flowing, not just a spot). The text provides multiple proofs: first, the Quranic verse from Surah al-Ma'idah (5:6) which mentions 'coming from relieving oneself' as a reason for purification. Second, the hadith from Safwan showing that travel permits wiping over socks except for janabah, but not for lesser impurities from defecation, urine, and sleep, indicating these nullify wudu. Third, the verse from Surah al-An'am (6:143) declaring blood as 'rijs' (impure). Fourth, the hadith from Aisha listing vomiting, nosebleed, etc. as requiring wudu. Fifth, the hadith of Fatimah bint Hubaysh about istihadah (non-menstrual bleeding) that requires washing blood but does not necessarily break wudu if it is constant? Actually, the hadith instructs her to wash the blood and pray, and she did not repeat wudu for each prayer? The text implies that flowing blood from istihadah does not nullify wudu if it is continuous, which is a nuanced ruling. The final line (in Urdu) adds a principle: if blood appears from a wound but does not flow beyond the wound site, it does not nullify wudu. This is an important condition: mere appearance without flowing is not a nullifier.

Key Terms
المعاني الناقضة (al-ma'ani al-naqida): The things that nullify wudu; i.e., the nullifiers.
تجاوز إلى موضع يلحقه حكم التطهير (tajawaza ila mawdi' yalhaquhu hukm al-tathir): Flowing to a place where the ruling of washing applies, i.e., beyond the exit point so that it must be washed off.
الغائط (al-gha'it): Relieving oneself, specifically defecation; used in the verse to indicate the act that necessitates purification.
مذي (madhy): Pre-seminal fluid that exits due to arousal; it nullifies wudu according to all schools.
قيء (qay'): Vomiting; if it is mouthful, it nullifies wudu according to the hadith cited.
رعاف (ru'af): Nosebleed; if blood flows, it nullifies wudu according to the hadith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following nullifies wudu according to the Hanafi school?
A) A drop of blood from a mosquito bite that does not flow
B) A small wound that bleeds but the blood does not flow beyond the wound
C) Blood that flows from a wound
D) Dry cupping (hijama) without blood flow

Key Takeaway
Wudu is nullified by excretion from the private parts and by blood or pus that flows beyond the exit point; stationary blood does not break wudu.

Taharah — Purification

The Nullifiers of Wudu: Conditions and Evidences
Listing nullifiers of wudu with scriptural evidences and conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the nullifiers of wudu according to the Hanafi school, state the specific conditions for each, and identify the Quranic and hadith proofs that support them.

Core Idea
Wudu is nullified by exit from passages, flowing blood, full-mouth vomit, and heavy sleep—each defined by precise conditions.

In this passage from al-Quduri, the author lists the events that break wudu, each supported by evidence from the Quran and hadith. Understanding these nullifiers with their conditions is essential for correct practice of salah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the nullifiers listed
The passage lists seven categories: exit from passages, blood/pus flowing, vomit filling mouth, sleep in specific postures. List each.
2
Note the conditions attached
For each nullifier, the text includes a condition: blood must flow beyond the wound, vomit must fill mouth, sleep must be heavy (lying down or leaning). Without these conditions, wudu is not broken.
This is a key Hanafi distinction.
3
Match each nullifier to its evidence
The passage provides Quranic verses and hadiths for each nullifier. For exit from passages: Quran 5:6 and hadith of Safwan. For blood: Quran 6:143 and hadiths. For vomit: hadith of Abu al-Darda. For sleep: hadith of Ali.
4
Understand the Hanafi methodology
The author uses Quran for general impurity and hadith for specifics, showing how rulings are derived. Note the use of hadith and sayings of companions/tabi'in.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْمَعَانِي النَّاقِضَةُ لِلْوُضُوءِ كُلُّ مَا خَرَجَ مِنْ السَّبِيلَيْنِ، وَالدَّمُ، وَالْقَيْحُ إِذَا خَرَجَا مِنْ الْبَدَنِ فَتَجَاوَزَ إِلَى مَوْضِعَ يَلْحَقُهُ حُكْمُ التَّطْهِيرِ. وَالْقَيْءُ إِذَا مَلَأَ الْفَمَ، وَالنَّوْمُ مُضْطَجِعًا أَوْ مُتَّكِنًا أَوْ مُسْتَنِدًا إِلَى شَيْءٍ لَوْ أُزِيلَ عَنْهُ لَسَقَطَ.

وجه (1) الآية لثبوت الأول: ﴿وَإِن كُنتُمْ جُنُبًا فَاطَّهَّرُوا وَإِن كُنتُم مَّرْضَى أَوْ عَلَى سَفَرٍ أَوْ جَاءَ أَحَدٌ مِّنكُم مِّنَ الْغَائِطِ ...﴾ (المائدة 5:6).
وجه (2) قول الصحابي: عن صفوان بن عسال قال: «كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يأمرنا إذا كنا سفرا أن لا ننزع خفافنا ثلاثة أيام ولياليهن إلا من جنابة، ولكن من غائط وبول ونوم» (سنن الترمذي، رقم: 96).
وجه (3) الآية لثبوت الدم: ﴿قُل لَّا أَجِدُ فِي مَا أُوحِيَ إِلَيَّ مُحَرَّمًا عَلَى طَاعِمٍ يَطْعَمُهُ إِلَّا أَن يَكُونَ مَيْتَةً أَوْ دَمًا مَّسْفُوحًا أَوْ لَحْمَ خِنزِيرٍ فَإِنَّهُ رِجْسٌ﴾ (الأنعام 6:143).
وجه (4) الحديث: عن عائشة قالت: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «من أصابه قيء أو رعاف أو فلز أو مذي، فلينصرف فليتوضأ ثم ليبن على صلاته» (سنن ابن ماجة، رقم: 1221).
وجه (5) الحديث: عن عائشة قالت: جاءت فاطمة بنت حبيش إلى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فقالت: يا رسول الله إني امرأة أستحاض فلا أطهر أفأدع الصلاة؟ فقال: «لا، إنما ذلك عرق وليس بحيض، فإذا أقبلت حيضتك فدعي الصلاة، وإذا أدبرت فاغسلي عنك الدم ثم صلي» (صحيح البخاري، رقم: 228).
وجه (6) الحديث: قال تميم الداري: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «الوضوء من كل دم سائل» (سنن الدارقطني، رقم: 581).
وجه (7) الحديث: ... (سنن أبي داود، رقم: 198) – مختصر.
وجه (8) الحديث لثبوت القيء: عن أبي الدرداء أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قاء فتوضأ (سنن الترمذي، رقم: 87).
وجه (9) قول التابعي: عن الحسن قال: ليس في القلس وضوء (مصنف عبد الرزاق، رقم: 523).
وجه (10) الحديث: عن عمار بن ياسر قال: أتى علي رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وأنا على بئر أدلو ماء في ركوة لي فقال: «يا عمار ما تصنع؟» قلت: أغسل ثوبي من تخامة أصابته فقال: «يا عمار إنما يغسل الثوب من خمس: من الغائط، والبول، والقيء، والدم، والمني» (سنن الدارقطني، رقم: 458).
وجه (11) الحديث لثبوت النوم: عن علي بن أبي طالب قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «وكاء السه العينان، فمن نام فليتوضأ» (سنن أبي داود، رقم: 203).

أصول: زخم أو چوٹ لگی اور خون ظاہر ہوا لیکن اپنے مقام سے تجاوز نہیں کیا، بہا نہیں تو ناقض وضو نہیں ہے.

لغات: الْقَيْءُ: قے الٹی، مَلَأَ: منھ بھرنا، الْفَمَ: منھ.
And the nullifiers of wudu: everything that exits from the two passages, and blood, and pus when they exit from the body and exceed to a place that the ruling of purification reaches. And vomit when it fills the mouth, and sleep lying down or leaning or resting on something such that if it were removed he would fall. Evidence (1) The verse for establishing the first: ... Evidence (2) The saying of the Companion: ... Evidence (3) The verse for establishing blood: ... Evidence (4) The hadith: ... Evidence (5) The hadith: ... Evidence (6) The hadith: ... Evidence (7) The hadith: ... (abridged). Evidence (8) The hadith for establishing vomit: ... Evidence (9) The saying of the Tabi'i: ... Evidence (10) The hadith: ... Evidence (11) The hadith for establishing sleep: ... Principle: If a person gets a wound or bruise and blood appears but does not flow from its place, it is not a nullifier of wudu. Vocabulary: al-qay' = vomit; mala'a = filled; al-fam = mouth.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof from the classical Hanafi text al-Quduri, listing the nullifiers of wudu along with their scriptural evidences. The author begins by stating the nullifiers: anything exiting from the front or rear private parts, blood and pus that exit the body and flow beyond the point of exit, vomit that fills the mouth, and sleep in certain postures (lying down, leaning, or resting against something without which one would fall). These are all causes that invalidate wudu according to the Hanafi school. The author then provides proofs: for exiting from the passages, the Quranic verse in al-Ma'ida (5:6) is cited, which mentions coming from the toilet. The hadith from Safwan ibn 'Assal shows that the Prophet commanded not to remove khuffs except for janaba, but for urine, stool, and sleep, indicating these break wudu. For blood, the verse from al-An'am (6:143) declares blood to be 'rijs' (impure). Several hadiths are given: the hadith about vomiting, nosebleed, etc., the hadith of Fatima bint Hubaysh about istihada, the hadith of Tamim al-Dari 'wudu from every flowing blood', and another hadith about a man who was shot and continued praying without renewing wudu. For vomit, the hadith of Abu al-Darda that the Prophet vomited and performed wudu, and a saying of al-Hasan that there is no wudu from 'qals' (slight vomit). The hadith of Ammar ibn Yasir lists five things from which clothes are washed, including vomit and blood. For sleep, the hadith of Ali that 'the eyes are the tie of the anus, so whoever sleeps should perform wudu'. At the end, the author adds a principle: if blood appears from a wound but does not flow beyond its place, it does not nullify wudu. This passage demonstrates the Hanafi methodology of deriving rulings from both explicit Quranic texts and authentic hadith, with careful attention to conditions (e.g., flowing blood, sleep posture).

Key Terms
الناقضة (al-nawaqid): Things that break or invalidate wudu.
السبيلين (al-sabilayn): The two passages: front (penis/vagina) and back (anus).
القيء (al-qay'): Vomiting; in this context, vomit that fills the mouth nullifies wudu.
النوم (al-nawm): Sleep in specific postures (lying down, leaning, resting) that cause loss of control.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as stated in this passage, which of the following conditions makes vomiting a nullifier of wudu?
A) Any amount of vomit, regardless of quantity
B) Vomit that fills the mouth
C) Vomit accompanied by nausea
D) Vomit that exits the body

Key Takeaway
Wudu is nullified only by specific events with precise conditions; not every impurity or loss of control breaks wudu.

Vomiting a Mouthful Nullifies Wudu
State ruling and provide hadith and athar proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on vomiting as a nullifier of wudu and identify the proofs from hadith and athar that support it.

Core Idea
Vomiting a mouthful nullifies wudu; less than that does not.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position that vomiting which fills the mouth (mala'a al-fam) invalidates wudu. We will explore the primary proof: the hadith of Abu al-Darda that the Prophet (peace be upon him) vomited and performed wudu, along with supporting statements from the tabi‘un. Understanding this distinction is essential for correct practice of wudu and prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is vomiting a mouthful (mala'a al-fam). The ruling is that it nullifies wudu, requiring renewal of wudu.
2
Locate the primary hadith proof
The hadith from Abu al-Darda reports that the Prophet vomited and then performed wudu. This is the key evidence.
Found in Sunan al-Tirmidhi, no. 87.
3
Understand the evidence from the hadith
According to Hanafi usul, the Prophet's action in a context of explanation (bayan) indicates obligation. Thus, the hadith proves vomiting is a cause for wudu.
The hadith is zanni al-thubut but qati‘ al-dalala.
4
Note the secondary proofs
Hasan al-Basri's statement distinguishes qay' (mouthful) from qals (less). The hadith of Ammar lists vomit among impurities that require washing garments, reinforcing its significance.
These support the threshold and importance of vomiting.
5
Recognize the cross-madhhab disagreement
Imam al-Shafi‘i does not consider vomiting a nullifier of wudu. This ikhtilaf arises from different interpretations of the same proofs.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْقَيْءُ إِذَا مَلَأَ الْفَمَ. وجه (۱) الحديث لثبوت المعاني الناقضة: القيء إذا ملأ الفم. عَنْ أَبِي الدَّرْدَاءِ: «أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَاءَ، فَتَوَضَّأَ»، فَلَقِيتُ ثَوْبَانَ فِي مَسْجِدِ دِمَشْقَ، فَذَكَرْتُ ذَلِكَ لَهُ، فَقَالَ: صَدَقَ أَنَا صَبَبْتُ لَهُ وَضُوءَهُ. (سنن ترمذي، بَابُ الوُضُوءِ مِنَ القَيْءِ وَالرُّعَافِ، برقم: 87) وجه (۲) قول التابعي لثبوت المعاني الناقضة: القيء إذا ملأ الفم. عن الحسن قال: «ليس في القلس وضوء». (مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب الوضوء من القيء والقلس، برقم: 523; مصنف ابن أبي شيبة، مَنْ كَانَ لَا يَرَى فِي الْقَلْسِ وُضُوءًا، برقم: 443) وجه (۳) قول التابعي لثبوت المعاني الناقضة: القيء إذا ملأ الفم. عَنْ عَمَّارِ بْنِ يَاسِرٍ، قَالَ: أَتَى عَلَيَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَأَنَا عَلَى بِئْرٍ أَدْلُو مَاءً فِي رَكْوَةٍ لِي فَقَالَ: «يَا عَمَّارُ مَا تَصْنَعُ؟»، قُلْتُ: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ بِأَبِي وَأَمِي أَغْسِلُ ثَوْبِي مِنْ تُخَامَةٍ أَصَابَتْهُ فَقَالَ: «يَا عَمَّارُ إِنَّمَا يُغْسَلُ الثَّوْبُ مِنْ خَمْسٍ: مِنَ الْغَائِطِ وَالْبَوْلِ وَالْقَيْءِ وَالدَّمِ وَالْمَنِي. يَا عَمَّارُ مَا تُخَامَتُكَ وَدُمُوعُ عَيْنَيْكَ وَالْمَاءُ الَّذِي فِي رَكْوَتِكَ إِلَّا سَوَاءٌ». (سنن الدارقطني، بَابُ لَجَاسَةِ الْبَوْلِ وَالْأَمْرِ بِالتَّنَزُّهِ مِنْهُ وَاحْكُم فِي بَوْلِ مَا يُؤْكَلُ حَمُهُ، برقم: 458)
And vomiting when it fills the mouth. Proof (1) the hadith for establishing the meanings of the nullifiers: vomiting when it fills the mouth. From Abu al-Darda: that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) vomited and performed wudu. So I met Thawban in the mosque of Damascus and mentioned that to him, and he said: He told the truth, I poured his water for wudu. (Sunan al-Tirmidhi, chapter on wudu from vomiting and nosebleed, no. 87) Proof (2) statement of a tabi'i for establishing the meanings of the nullifiers: vomiting when it fills the mouth. From al-Hasan: he said: there is no wudu from less than a mouthful. (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on wudu from vomiting and qals, no. 523; Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, those who do not consider qals requiring wudu, no. 443) Proof (3) statement of a tabi'i for establishing the meanings of the nullifiers: vomiting when it fills the mouth. From Ammar ibn Yasir: he said: the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) came upon me while I was at a well drawing water in a small water skin of mine. He said: 'O Ammar, what are you doing?' I said: O Messenger of Allah, may my father and mother be sacrificed for you, I am washing my garment from saliva that reached it. He said: 'O Ammar, a garment is only washed from five things: stool, urine, vomit, blood, and seminal fluid. O Ammar, your saliva, tears of your eyes, and the water in your skin are all the same.' (Sunan al-Daraqutni, chapter on impurity of urine and the command to avoid it and the ruling on urine of animals whose meat is eaten, no. 458)
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is from a commentary on al-Quduri's matn. It presents the ruling that vomiting a mouthful nullifies wudu, followed by three proofs. The first proof is a hadith from Abu al-Darda that the Prophet (peace be upon him) vomited and then performed wudu, indicating that vomiting negates wudu. The second proof is a statement from Hasan al-Basri, who distinguishes between qay' (a mouthful) and qals (less than a mouthful), confirming that only a mouthful requires wudu. The third proof is a hadith from Ammar ibn Yasir, where the Prophet lists vomit among five impurities that require washing a garment. Although this hadith deals with impurity (najasah) rather than nullification of wudu, the author uses it to reinforce the importance of vomit as a significant event that necessitates purification. The Hanafi ruling is clear: any vomit that fills the mouth breaks wudu, while less than that does not.

Key Terms
الْقَيْءُ (al-qay'): Vomiting that exits the stomach and fills the mouth
مَلَأَ الْفَمَ (mala'a al-fam): Fills the mouth; a legal measure for the quantity of vomit that nullifies wudu

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what condition must vomiting meet to nullify wudu?
A) Any amount of vomit
B) Vomit that fills the mouth
C) Vomit that comes from the stomach
D) Vomit accompanied by blood

Key Takeaway
Vomiting a mouthful is a nullifier of wudu in the Hanafi school, supported by the Prophet's action and the distinction from qals.

Sleep and Wudu: The Hanafi Position
Ruling with proofs from hadith and companion practice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sleep nullifying wudu and apply the distinction between deep and light sleep.

Core Idea
Deep sleep that relaxes joints nullifies wudu; light sleep does not.

This lesson examines the ruling on sleep as a nullifier of wudu. The Hanafi school distinguishes between deep sleep (nawm thaqil), which relaxes the joints and thus nullifies wudu, and light sleep (nawm khafif), such as dozing while seated, which does not. We will explore the proofs from hadith and companion practice that support this position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the opening statement: sleep lying down, reclining, or leaning nullifies wudu. Note that the ruling applies only to postures where joints relax.
The matn specifies postures: مضطجعًا (lying down), متكئًا (reclining), and مستندًا (leaning).
2
Examine the first hadith (from Ali)
The Prophet said, 'The two eyes are the tie of the anus; so whoever sleeps, let him perform wudu.' This indicates that sleep causes loss of muscular control, hence wudu is required. Hanafis interpret this as applying to deep sleep specifically.
The command 'falyatawadda'' (let him perform wudu) is taken as wajib (obligatory) in the context of deep sleep.
3
Examine the second hadith (from Ibn Abbas)
The Prophet said, 'Wudu is only obligatory for one who sleeps lying down, for when he lies down his joints relax.' This directly links the nullification to the relaxation of joints.
This hadith restricts the general command in the first hadith, providing a criterion for deep sleep.
4
Examine the companion practice (from Anas)
The companions would doze while waiting for the night prayer, then pray without wudu. This shows that light sleep (dozing) does not nullify wudu.
This practice reinforces the distinction between deep and light sleep.
5
Understand the cross-madhhab difference
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that sleep does not nullify wudu at all, as he considers sleep a minor event that does not break wudu. The Hanafi school uses the hadith evidence to establish wujub for deep sleep.
The practical consequence: in the Hanafi school, one must renew wudu after deep sleep; in the Shafi'i school, sleep never nullifies wudu.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالنَّوْمُ مُضْطَجِعًا أَوْ مُتَّكِنًا أَوْ مُسْتَنِدًا إِلَى شَيْءٍ لَوْ أُزِيلَ عَنْهُ لَسَقَطَ. وجه (۱) الحديث لثبوت المعاني الناقضة: النوم مضطجعًا. عَنْ عَلِيِّ بْنِ أَبِي طَالِبٍ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ: «وِكَاءُ السَّهِ الْعَيْنَانِ، فَمَنْ نَامَ فَلْيَتَوَضَّأْ». (سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ فِي الْوُضُوءِ مِنَ النَّوْمِ، برقم: 203) وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت المعاني الناقضة: النوم مضطجعًا. عَنْ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ، أَنَّهُ رَأَى النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم نَامَ وَهُوَ سَاجِدٌ، حَتَّى غَطَّ أَوْ نَفَخَ، ثُمَّ قَامَ يُصَلِّي، فَقُلْتُ: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، إِنَّكَ قَدْ نِمْتَ قَالَ: «إِنَّ الوُضُوءَ لَا يَجِبُ إِلَّا عَلَى مَنْ نَامَ مُضْطَجِعًا، فَإِنَّهُ إِذَا اضْطَجَعَ اسْتَرْحَتْ مَفَاصِلُهُ». (سنن ترمذي، بَابُ الوُضُوءِ مِنَ النَّوْمِ، برقم: 77) وجه (۳) قول الصحابي لثبوت المعاني الناقضة: النوم مضطجعًا. عَنْ أَنَسٍ، قَالَ: «كَانَ أَصْحَابُ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَنْتَظِرُونَ الْعِشَاءَ الْآخِرَةَ حَتَّى تَحْفِقَ رُءُوسُهُمْ، ثُمَّ يُصَلُّونَ وَلَا يَتَوَضَّئُونَ». (سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ فِي الْوُضُوءِ مِنَ النَّوْمِ، برقم 200; سنن ترمذي، بَابُ الوُضُوءِ مِنَ النَّوْمِ، برقم: 77) وجه (ا) الحديث لثبوت المعاني الناقضة: النوم مضطجعًا. عَنِ الْحَسَنِ، أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم كَانَ يُصَلِّي بِالنَّاسِ فَدَخَلَ أَعْمَى فَتَرَدَّى فِي بِئْرٍ كَانَتْ فِي الْمَسْجِدِ، فَضَحِكَ طَوَائِفُ مَنْ كَانَ خَلْفَ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم فِي صَلَاتِهِمْ، فَلَمَّا سَلَّمَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم أَمَرَ مَنْ كَانَ ضَحِكَ أَنْ يُعِيدَ وُضُوءَهُ، وَيُعِيدَ صَلَاتَهُ. (السنن الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ تَرْكِ الْوُضُوءِ مِنَ الْقَهْقَهَةِ فِي الصَّلَاةِ، برقم: 680; سنن دارقطني، بَابُ أَحَادِيثِ الْقَهْقَهَةِ فِي الصَّلَاةِ وَعِلَلِهَا برقم (614) وجه (٢) الحديث لثبوت المعاني الناقضة: النوم مضطجعًا. عَنْ جَابِرٍ، قَالَ: «يُعِيدُ الصَّلَاةَ وَلَا يُعِيدُ الْوُضُوءَ». (السنن الكبرى للبيهقي، بَابُ تَرْكِ الْوُضُوءِ مِنَ الْقَهْقَهَةِ فِي الصَّلَاةِ، برقم: 674; سنن الدارقطني، بَابُ أَحَادِيثِ الْقَهْقَهَةِ فِي الصَّلَاةِ وَعِلَلِها، برقم: 650)
And sleep lying down, or reclining, or leaning on something such that if it were removed he would fall. Proof (1) the hadith for establishing the meanings of the nullifiers: sleep lying down. From Ali ibn Abi Talib: he said: the Messenger of Allah said: 'The two eyes are the tie of the anus; so whoever sleeps, let him perform wudu.' (Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter on wudu from sleep, no. 203) Proof (2) the hadith for establishing the meanings of the nullifiers: sleep lying down. From Ibn Abbas: he saw the Prophet (peace be upon him) sleeping while prostrating until he snored, then he stood and prayed. I said: O Messenger of Allah, you slept. He said: 'Wudu is only obligatory for one who sleeps lying down, for when he lies down his joints relax.' (Sunan al-Tirmidhi, chapter on wudu from sleep, no. 77) Proof (3) statement of a companion for establishing the meanings of the nullifiers: sleep lying down. From Anas: he said: The companions of the Messenger of Allah would wait for the night prayer until their heads nodded, then they would pray and not perform wudu. (Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter on wudu from sleep, no. 200; Sunan al-Tirmidhi, chapter on wudu from sleep, no. 77) Proof (a) the hadith for establishing the meanings of the nullifiers: sleep lying down. From al-Hasan: that the Prophet (peace be upon him) was praying with the people when a blind man entered and fell into a well that was in the mosque, and a group of those behind the Prophet laughed during their prayer. When the Prophet finished the prayer, he ordered those who laughed to repeat their wudu and repeat their prayer. (Al-Sunan al-Kubra by al-Bayhaqi, chapter on leaving wudu from laughter in prayer, no. 680; Sunan al-Daraqutni, chapter on hadith of laughter in prayer and their defects, no. 614) Proof (ii) the hadith for establishing the meanings of the nullifiers: sleep lying down. From Jabir: he said: 'He repeats the prayer but does not repeat wudu.' (Al-Sunan al-Kubra by al-Bayhaqi, chapter on leaving wudu from laughter in prayer, no. 674; Sunan al-Daraqutni, chapter on hadith of laughter in prayer and their defects, no. 650)
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on the nullifiers of wudu. The matn states that sleep nullifies wudu when it is lying down, reclining, or leaning on something such that if the support is removed, the person would fall. The commentator provides multiple proofs. The first hadith from Ali uses the expression that the eyes are the tie of the anus, meaning that when one is awake, the sphincter is controlled, but sleep releases that control. The second hadith from Ibn Abbas directly states that wudu is only obligatory for one who sleeps lying down, because the joints relax. The third proof is the practice of the companions who would doze while waiting for prayer and then pray without wudu, indicating that light sleep does not nullify wudu. The fourth and fifth proofs address laughter in prayer, which is also a nullifier. The hadith about the blind man shows that the Prophet ordered those who laughed to repeat both wudu and prayer. The hadith from Jabir says to repeat the prayer only, not wudu. This indicates an intra-school difference: Abu Hanifa holds that laughter nullifies both wudu and prayer, while the Sahibayn hold it nullifies only wudu. However, the passage uses these to support the general principle that deep sleep (which relaxes joints) nullifies wudu.

Key Terms
مُضْطَجِعًا (mudtaji'an): Lying down on one's side
مُتَّكِنًا (muttaki'an): Reclining or leaning on one side
مُسْتَنِدًا (mustanidan): Leaning on something for support

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following does NOT nullify wudu?
A) Sleeping lying down on a bed
B) Sleeping while leaning on a wall
C) Dozing while sitting upright
D) Sleeping while reclining on a couch

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school teaches that only deep sleep which relaxes the joints nullifies wudu, based on the prophetic hadith and companion practice.

Nullifiers of Wudu: Loss of Intellect and Laughter
State ruling from matn without proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three events that nullify wudu according to the Hanafi school and explain the effect of laughter in prayer.

Core Idea
Loss of intellect and laughter in prayer nullify wudu; laughter also invalidates the prayer.

The matn of al-Quduri presents a concise list of additional nullifiers of wudu beyond the usual causes. This lesson focuses on three specific events: fainting, insanity, and audible laughter during prayer. While the rule is straightforward, the Hanafi school has an internal difference regarding whether laughter nullifies only wudu or both wudu and the prayer itself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that three events nullify wudu: loss of intellect (by fainting or insanity) and laughter in prayer. First, note that these are nullifiers of wudu, not just makruh or disliked.
The term 'ghalabah 'ala al-'aql' encompasses both temporary and permanent loss of reason.
2
List the specific nullifiers
From the text, extract three items: 1) fainting (ighma'), 2) insanity (junun), and 3) laughter (qahqaha) in any prayer that includes bowing and prostration.
Laughter only nullifies wudu if it occurs during a prayer with ruku' and sujud; funeral prayer is excluded.
3
Understand the intra-Hanafi difference
Abu Hanifa holds that laughter in prayer nullifies both wudu and the prayer itself. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold it nullifies only wudu. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that of Abu Hanifa.
This difference arises from whether laughter is considered a minor or major interruption in prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْغَلَبَةُ عَلَى الْعَقْلِ بِالْإِغْمَاءِ وَالْجُنُونُ وَالْقَهْقَهَةُ فِي كُلِّ صَلَاةٍ ذَاتِ رَكُوعِ وَسُجُودِ.
And the overcoming of the intellect by fainting, and insanity, and laughter in every prayer that has bowing and prostration.
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This is a straightforward ruling statement from the matn of al-Quduri. It lists additional nullifiers of wudu: loss of intellect due to fainting (ighma'), insanity (junun), and laughter (qahqaha) during any prayer that includes bowing and prostration (i.e., all obligatory and supererogatory prayers except funeral prayer). The Hanafi school holds that laughter in prayer nullifies both wudu and the prayer itself, according to Abu Hanifa, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold it nullifies only wudu. The mufta bihi position is that it nullifies both. However, the text does not specify the ikhtilaf. The ruling is clear: these three events break wudu.

Key Terms
الْإِغْمَاءُ (al-ighma'): Fainting; temporary loss of consciousness
الْجُنُونُ (al-junun): Insanity; permanent or temporary loss of reason
الْقَهْقَهَةُ (al-qahqaha): Loud laughter; audible laughter in prayer

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) It nullifies wudu according to all Hanafi imams
C) It nullifies both wudu and prayer according to Abu Hanifa
D) It nullifies only the prayer

Key Takeaway
Fainting, insanity, and audible laughter in prayer are nullifiers of wudu; the mufta bihi is that laughter also invalidates the prayer.

The Fards of Ghusl: Mouth, Nose, and Whole Body
State ruling and provide Quranic and hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three fards of ghusl and explain the Quranic and hadith proofs that establish them according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Rinsing the mouth, snuffing water into the nose, and washing the whole body are all fard in ghusl; omission of any invalidates the ghusl.

Ghusl (full-body ritual purification) is required after janabah and certain other conditions. But what exactly must you wash? The Hanafi school, based on the Quran and Sunnah, specifies three obligatory acts, including rinsing the mouth and nose—a position that differs from other schools. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Locate the act being ruled upon: ghusl after janabah. The text states its fards: madmadah, istinshaq, and washing the entire body.
The ruling is fard 'ayn (individual obligation) for every adult Muslim when janabah occurs.
2
Locate the dalil (Quranic proof)
The first proof is the Quranic verse: 'And if you are in a state of major impurity, then purify yourselves' (5:6).
The command 'fattahharu' is general and includes washing the whole body. Hanafis interpret 'body' to include the mouth and nose as they are part of the face.
3
Analyze the hadith proof
The second proof is the hadith from 'Ali: 'Whoever leaves a spot the size of a hair from major impurity unwashed, such and such will be done to him.'
This emphasizes thoroughness, implying that every part must be washed, including oral and nasal cavities.
4
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
For the verse, the Hanafi rule that a general command (amm) is binding on all instances (qat'i) until exclusion. The verse is qat'i in transmission but zanni in dalalah; however, the Hanafi usul holds the general to be binding.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but accepted in fiqh; its wording indicates total coverage.
5
Note the cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i considers madmadah and istinshaq as sunnah in ghusl, not fard.
The practical consequence: in Hanafi school, omitting them invalidates ghusl; in Shafi'i, ghusl is valid but deficient.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
{7} وَفَرْضُ الْغُسْلِ الْمَضْمَضَةً وَالِاسْتِنْشَاقُ وَغَسْلُ سَائِرِ الْبَدَنِ. وجه (١) الآية لثبوت فرض الغسل: المضمضة والاستنشاق وغسل سائر البدن. وَإِن كُنتُمْ جُنُبًا فَأَطَّهَرُوا (سورة المائدة، آية 6). وجه (٢) الحديث لثبوت فرض الغسل: المضمضة والاستنشاق. عَنْ عَلِيٍّ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «مَنْ تَرَكَ مَوْضِعَ شَعْرَةٍ مِنْ جَنَابَةٍ لَمْ يَغْسِلْهَا فُعِلَ بِهِ كَذَا وَكَذَا». (سنن أبي داود، بَابُ الْمَضْمَضَةِ وَالِاسْتِنْشَاقِ فِي الْجَنَابَةِ، برقم: 248; سنن الترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي الْمَضْمَضَةِ وَالِاسْتِنْشَاقِ فِي الْجَنَابَةِ، برقم: 110) أصول: اصل یہ کہ گہری نیند اور پاگل پن سے عقل زائل ہو جاتی ہے، جس سے معلوم نہیں ہوتا ہے کہ ریح نکلی یا نہین نکلی، لہذا ابتداء ہی حکم لگا دیا جاتا ہے، اسی کو استرخاء مفاصل کہتے ہیں.
{7} And the fard of ghusl: rinsing the mouth, and snuffing water into the nose, and washing the rest of the body. Proof (1) the verse for establishing the fard of ghusl: rinsing the mouth, snuffing water into the nose, and washing the rest of the body. 'And if you are in a state of major impurity, then purify yourselves' (Surah al-Ma'idah, 5:6). Proof (2) the hadith for establishing the fard of ghusl: rinsing the mouth and snuffing water into the nose. From Ali (may Allah be pleased with him): the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever leaves a spot the size of a hair from major impurity unwashed, such and such will be done to him.' (Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter on rinsing mouth and nose in major impurity, no. 248; Sunan al-Tirmidhi, chapter on rinsing mouth and nose in major impurity, no. 110) Principles: The principle is that deep sleep and insanity cause the intellect to disappear, so it is not known whether wind passed or not, therefore the ruling is applied at the outset; this is called 'istirkha' al-mafasil' (relaxation of joints).
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage states the fards (obligatory acts) of ghusl (full-body ritual washing) according to the Hanafi school. There are three: rinsing the mouth (madmadah), snuffing water into the nose (istinshaq), and washing the entire body. The first proof is the Quranic verse from Surah al-Ma'idah: 'And if you are in a state of major impurity, then purify yourselves' (5:6). The Hanafi school interprets 'purify yourselves' (fattahharu) as a command that includes washing the whole body, and they consider madmadah and istinshaq as part of the body to be washed because they are part of the face. The second proof is a hadith from Ali that warns against leaving any hair spot unwashed, which implies thorough washing, including the mouth and nose. The Urdu text adds a principle: deep sleep and insanity cause loss of intellect, so one cannot be sure if wind has passed; therefore, the ruling of nullification is applied at the outset. This is called istirkha' al-mafasil (relaxation of joints), which is the underlying reason why deep sleep nullifies wudu.

Key Terms
الْمَضْمَضَةُ (al-madmadah): Rinsing the mouth with water
الِاسْتِنْشَاقُ (al-istinshaq): Snuffing water into the nose and then expelling it
الْجَنَابَةُ (al-janabah): State of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is NOT a fard of ghusl?
A) Rinsing the mouth
B) Snuffing water into the nose
C) Wiping the head
D) Washing the entire body

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school considers rinsing the mouth and snuffing water into the nose to be fard in ghusl, based on the Quran's general command and the hadith demanding complete washing.

Nullifiers of Wudu: Sleep and Laughter
Ruling on nullifiers of wudu with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sleep and laughter as nullifiers of wudu, identify the proofs, and distinguish between the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Only sleep lying down nullifies wudu; loud laughter in prayer nullifies both wudu and prayer.

In this lesson, we examine two specific nullifiers of wudu: sleep and laughter during prayer. The Hanafi school distinguishes between types of sleep based on body position, and holds that loud laughter in prayer invalidates both wudu and the prayer itself. We will explore the hadith evidence that supports these rulings and address a difference of opinion within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
First, recognize that the passage lists sleep lying down and laughter in prayer as nullifiers of wudu. Also note that fainting and madness, which remove intellect, are included.
Focus on the specific wording: النَّوْمُ مُضْطَجِعًا and الْقَهْقَهَةُ.
2
Locate the dalil
The passage provides several hadith. The primary proof for sleep is the hadith of Ibn Abbas: 'Wudu is obligatory only on one who sleeps lying down.' For laughter, the hadith of al-Hasan narrates the Prophet ordering repetition of both wudu and prayer.
Note the chain and source for each hadith.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
For sleep, the phrase 'لا يجب إلا على من نام مضطجعا' indicates exclusivity: only lying-down sleep requires wudu. For laughter, the Prophet's command to repeat both wudu and prayer shows that both are invalidated.
Consider the linguistic implication of 'إلا' (except).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Within the Hanafi school, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that laughter in prayer does not nullify wudu, only the prayer. The matn follows Abu Hanifa's view that both are nullified. Also, the Shafi'i school disagrees on both counts.
Another narration from Jabir says to repeat prayer only, not wudu.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The passage presents the hadith of al-Hasan as evidence for Abu Hanifa's position, and the narration from Jabir as weaker. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that loud laughter in prayer nullifies both wudu and prayer.
The Urdu commentary explains the principle: loss of intellect (through deep sleep or madness) leads to assumption of impurity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

عَنِ الْحَسَنِ، " أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم كَانَ يُصَلِّي بِالنَّاسِ فَدَخَلَ أَعْمَى فَتَرَدَّى فِي بِئْرٍ كَانَتْ فِي الْمَسْجِدِ، فَضَحِكَ طَوَائِفُ مَنْ كَانَ خَلْفَ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله خاء مفاصل کہتے ہیں۔
And overpowering of the intellect by fainting, madness, and laughter in every prayer that has bowing and prostration. Evidence (1) hadith for establishing the nullifiers: sleep lying down from Ibn Abbas, that he saw the Prophet ﷺ slept while prostrating until he snored or breathed heavily, then he stood to pray. I said: O Messenger of Allah, you have slept. He said: 'Wudu is obligatory only on one who sleeps lying down, for when he lies down his joints relax.' (Tirmidhi, #77) Evidence (3) saying of a Companion for establishing the nullifiers: sleep lying down from Anas, who said: 'The Companions of the Messenger of Allah ﷺ would wait for the last night prayer until their heads nodded, then they would pray and not perform wudu.' (Abu Dawud #200, Tirmidhi #77) Evidence (a) hadith: from al-Hasan that the Prophet ﷺ was leading people in prayer when a blind man entered and fell into a well in the mosque, and some people behind the Prophet laughed during their prayer. When the Prophet ﷺ greeted, he ordered those who had laughed to repeat their wudu and their prayer. (Bayhaqi #680, Darqutni #614) Evidence (2) hadith: from Jabir, said: 'He repeats the prayer but does not repeat the wudu.' (Bayhaqi #674, Darqutni #650) Principle: Deep sleep and madness remove intellect, so it is not known whether wind was released or not, therefore the ruling is applied from the beginning. This is called 'relaxation of joints'.
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the nullifiers of wudu. The matn states that loss of intellect through fainting, madness, and laughter in any prayer with ruku' and sujud nullifies wudu. The commentary then provides hadith evidence for the specific case of sleep while lying down: the Prophet ﷺ indicated that wudu is required only if one sleeps lying down because the joints relax, allowing possibility of passing wind. The practice of the Companions waiting for Isha' prayer with heads nodding but not repeating wudu confirms that light sleep (sitting or standing) does not nullify. For laughter in prayer, a hadith shows that those who laughed out loud in prayer were ordered to repeat both wudu and prayer. Another narration from Jabir says to repeat the prayer only, not wudu—this indicates a difference of opinion, but the relied-upon Hanafi position is that loud laughter in prayer nullifies both wudu and prayer. The Urdu commentary explains the underlying principle: deep sleep and madness cause loss of awareness, so one cannot be certain if wind was emitted, thus the ruling of nullification is preemptively applied.

Key Terms
النَّوْمُ مُضْطَجِعًا (al-nawm muḍṭajiʿan): Sleeping in a reclining position where joints relax, allowing possible release of wind.
الْقَهْقَهَةُ (al-qahqahah): Loud laughter in prayer that can be heard by others.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this lesson, what is the Hanafi mufta bihi (operative ruling) regarding loud laughter in prayer?
A) It nullifies only the prayer, not wudu
B) It nullifies both prayer and wudu
C) It does not nullify anything
D) It nullifies wudu only

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, sleep must be lying down with relaxed joints to nullify wudu; loud laughter in prayer nullifies both wudu and the prayer itself.

The Three Obligatory Acts of Ghusl: Rinsing Mouth, Nose, and Washing the Body
Listing obligatory acts of ritual bath with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three fard acts of ghusl according to the Hanafi school and explain the evidence from the Quran and hadith that establishes each.

Core Idea
Rinsing the mouth and nose are individually fard in ghusl, not mere sunnah.

This lesson examines a passage from al-Quduri's matn that lists the obligatory acts (fard) of ghusl. The Hanafi school holds that three acts are individually fard: rinsing the mouth (madmadah), drawing water into the nose (istinshaq), and washing the entire body. While the Quranic verse "fa-aṭṭahharū" provides the general command, the Hanafis rely on a specific hadith from Abu Hurairah to establish the obligation of the first two. We will walk through the evidence and the internal disagreement within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Read the matn: "Wafarḍu al-ghusli al-madmadatu wa al-istinshāqu wa ghaslu sā'iri al-badani." The three acts are declared fard (obligatory). Note that the ruling level for each act is fard within ghusl.
These are essential components; omitting any invalidates the ghusl.
2
Locate the dalil
The commentary cites four evidences: (1) Quran 5:6, (2) a weak hadith from Ali, (3) a hadith from Abu Hurairah in Darqutni, and (4) a saying of Ibn Sirin. Identify which are primary: the Quran and the Abu Hurairah hadith.
The weak hadith is not relied upon.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
For the Quran, the imperative "fa-aṭṭahharū" means purify yourselves; the Hanafi interpretation is that the whole body includes the mouth and nose as they are part of the outer body. For the hadith, the Prophet explicitly made madmadah and istinshaq an obligation (fariḍatan) for the junub.
The Dalil block in this lesson details the strength of evidence.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Within the Hanafi school, Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani considered madmadah and istinshaq as sunnah, not fard. The matn follows Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Outside the school, the Shafi'i and Maliki schools consider them sunnah; the Hanbali school considers them wajib (slightly less than fard).
This disagreement affects the validity of ghusl if these acts are omitted.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is that madmadah and istinshaq are fard. This is based on the explicit Darqutni hadith and the practice of the majority of Hanafi scholars. The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah.
When giving fatwa, the Hanafi mufti follows the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

{7} وَفَرْضُ الْغُسْلِ الْمَضْمَضَةً . وَالِاسْتِنْشَاقُ ٣ وَغَسْل سَائِرِ الْبَدَنِ. وجه : (۱) الآية لثبوت فَرْضَ الْغُسْل لى الْمَضْمَضَةُ : وَالِاسْتِنْشَاقُ ٣ وَغَسْل سَائِرِ الْبَدَنِ \ وَإِن كُنتُمْ جُنُبًا فَأَطَهَّرُوا (سورة المائدة5 ، آيت نمبر 6،) وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت فَرْضُ الْغُسْلِ لى الْمَضْمَضَةُ لـ وَالِاسْتِنْشَاقُ \ عَنْ عَلِيِّ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «مَنْ تَرَكَ مَوْضِعَ شَعْرَةٍ مِنْ جَنَابَةٍ لَمْ يَغْسِلْهَا فُعِلَ (حديث ضعيف) وجه : (۳) الحديث لثبوت فَرْضُ الْغُسْلِ : الْمَضْمَضَةُ وَالِاسْتِنْشَاقُ \ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ جَعَلَ الْمَضْمَضَةَ وَالاسْتِنْشَاقَ لِلْجُنُبِ ثَلَاثًا فَرِيضَةً» (سنن الدار قطني ، بَابُ مَا رُوِيَ فِي الْمَضْمَضَةِ وَالِاسْتِنْشَاقِ في غُسل الجنابة، غمبر (409) وجه (۴) قول التابعي لثبوت فَرْضُ الْغُسْل : الْمَضْمَضَةُ وَالاسْتِشَاقُ \ عَنِ ابْنِ سِيرِينَ ، قَالَ: سَنَّ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «الِاسْتِنْشَاقَ فِي الْجَنَابَةِ ثَلَاثًا (سنن الدار قطني، بَابُ مَا رُوِيَ فِي الْمَضْمَضَةِ وَالِاسْتِنْشَاقِ فِي غُسْلِ الجنَابَةِ،نمبر 407)
{7} And the obligatory acts of ghusl are: rinsing the mouth, drawing water into the nose, and washing the rest of the body. Evidence (1) from the verse for establishing the fard of ghusl: rinsing mouth, nose, and washing rest of body: 'And if you are in a state of janabah, then purify yourselves' (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:6). Evidence (2) hadith for establishing the fard of ghusl: rinsing mouth and nose: from Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'Whoever leaves a spot of hair from janabah unwashed, such and such will be done to him.' (weak hadith) Evidence (3) hadith for establishing the fard of ghusl: rinsing mouth and nose: from Abu Hurairah that the Prophet ﷺ made rinsing the mouth and nose for the junub three times an obligation. (Darqutni #409) Evidence (4) saying of a Tabi'i: from Ibn Sirin who said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ established as sunnah: 'drawing water into the nose in janabah three times.' (Darqutni #407)
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof on the obligatory elements (fard) of ghusl. The matn from al-Quduri states that the fard of ghusl are three: rinsing the mouth (madmadah), drawing water into the nose (istinshaq), and washing the entire body. The commentary provides evidence: first, the Quranic ayah 'If you are in a state of janabah, then purify yourselves'—interpreted as washing the whole body. The mouth and nose are included because they are part of the body and the command to wash is general. However, Hanafis consider them separate obligations based on additional hadith. A weak hadith from Ali emphasizes washing every hair, but the stronger proof is the hadith of Abu Hurairah where the Prophet explicitly made madmadah and istinshaq an obligation (fariḍatan) for the junub. A narration from Ibn Sirin uses the word 'sanna' but is interpreted as obligation. Thus, in the Hanafi school, these three acts are individually fard (obligatory) for ghusl to be valid.

Key Terms
الْمَضْمَضَةُ (al-madmadah): Rinsing the mouth with water and swishing it around before spitting it out.
الِاسْتِنْشَاقُ (al-istinshāq): Drawing water into the nose and then expelling it.
فَرْضُ الْغُسْلِ (farḍu al-ghusli): The obligatory acts of the ritual bath; omission invalidates the bath.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the matn of al-Quduri, how many fard acts are there in ghusl?
A) One: washing the entire body
B) Two: rinsing mouth and nose
C) Three: rinsing mouth, nose, and washing whole body
D) Four: including washing feet

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the three fard acts of ghusl are rinsing the mouth, rinsing the nose, and washing the entire body, with the first two established by a specific hadith.

Sunnah Method of Ghusl
Describing the recommended sequence of ghusl with hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah sequence of ghusl as described in the hadith of Aisha and explain the legal status of each step.

Core Idea
The Prophet's method of ghusl is sunnah muakkadah: wash hands, private parts, wudu, then pour water over head and body three times, then wash feet.

This lesson presents the recommended method of performing ghusl as practiced by the Prophet ﷺ and recorded in Sahih Muslim. The steps are sunnah muakkadah — emphasized but not obligatory. Understanding them helps fulfill the obligation of ghusl in the best manner.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sunnah sequence
List the steps in order: wash hands and private parts, remove impurity, perform wudu except feet, pour water over head and body three times, move away, wash feet.
2
Understand the evidence
The hadith of Aisha (Muslim) describes the Prophet's practice verbatim, establishing the sunnah.
3
Classify each step as fard, wajib, or sunnah
The only fard in ghusl is washing the entire body with intention. These steps are sunnah muakkadah.

Source Text

{8} وَسُنَّةُ الْغُسْلِ أَنْ يَبْدَأَ الْمُغْتَسِلُ فَيَغْسِلَ يَدَيْهِ وَفَرْجَهُ وَيُزِيلُ تَجَاسَةً إِنْ كَانَتْ عَلَى بَدَنِهِ يَتَوَضأُ وُضُوءَهُ لِلصَّلَاةِ إِلَّا رِجْلَيْهِ. ثُمَّ يُفِيضُ الْمَاءَ عَلَى رَأْسِهِ وَسَائِرٍ جَسَدِهِ ثَلَاثًا ثُمَّ يَتَنَحَّى عَنْ ذَلِكَ الْمَكَانِ فَيَغْسِلُ رِجْلَيْهِ وَلَيْسَ عَلَى الْمَرْأَةِ أَنْ تَنْقُضَ صَفَائِرَهَا فِي الْغُسْلِ إِذَا بَلَغَ الْمَاءُ أُصُولَ الشَّعْرِ.  وجه : (١) الحديث لثبوت سُنَّةُ الْغُسْلِ أَنْ يَبْدَأَ الْمُغْتَسِلُ فَيَغْسِلَ يَدَيْهِ \ عن عائشة؛ قالت كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إِذَا اغْتَسَلَ مِنَ الْجَنَابَةِ، يَبْدَأُ فَيَغْسِلُ يَدَيْهِ ثُمَّ يُفْرِخُ بِيَمِينِهِ عَلَى شِمَالِهِ. فَيَغْسِلُ فَرْجَهُ. ثم يتوضأ وضوئه لِلصَّلَاةِ. ثُمَّ يَأْخُذُ الْمَاءَ فَيُدْخِلُ أَصَابِعَهُ فِي أُصُولِ الشَّعْرِ. حَتَّى إِذَا رَأَى أَنْ قَدِ اسْتَبْرَأَ حَفَنَ عَلَى رَأْسِهِ ثَلَاثَ حَفَنَاتٍ ثُمَّ أَفَاضَ عَلَى سَائِرِ جَسَدِهِ. ثُمَّ غَسَلَ رجُلَيْهِ(مسلم شریف ، باب صفَةِ غُسل الجنابة، غمبر (316) ا وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت سُنَّةُ الْغُسْلِ: لَيْسَ عَلَى الْمَرْأَةِ أَنْ تَنْقُضَ صَفَائِرَهَا فِي الْغُسْلِ \ عَنْ أُمّ سَلَمَةَ، قَالَتْ: قُلْتُ يَارَسُولَ اللهِ إِنّي امْرَأَةٌ أَشُدُّ ضَفْرَ رَأْسِي فَأَنْقُضُهُ لِغُسْلِ الْجَنَابَةِ؟ قَالَ: «لَا. إِنَّمَا يَكْفِيكِ أَنْ تَحْيِي عَلَى رَأْسِكِ ثَلَاثَ حَشَيَاتٍ ثُمَّ تُفِيضِينَ عَلَيْكِ الْمَاءَ فَتَطْهُرِينَ» (مسلم، بَابُ حُكْمِ ضَفَائِرِ الْمُعْتَسِلَةِ، غير 330/) وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت سُنَّةُ الْغُسْلِ: لَيْسَ عَلَى الْمَرْأَةِ أَنْ تَنْقُضَ ضَفَائِرَهَا فِي الْغُسْلِ اثُمَّ تَصُبُّ عَلَى رَأْسِهَا فَتَدْلُكُهُ دَلْكًا شَدِيدًا حَتَّى تَبْلُغَ شُؤُونَ رَأْسِهَا، (مسلم، بَابُ اسْتِحْبَابِ اسْتِعْمَالِ الْمُغْتَسِلَةِ مِنَ الْخَيْضِ فِرْصَةً مِنْ مِسْكِ فِي مَوْضِعِ الدَّمِ، نمبر (332) لغات: فَرْجَه : شرم گاه ، وَيُزِيلُ : زائل کرنا ، ختم کرنا، يُفيضُ : بہانا، پہنچانا، يتنحى: صاف کرنا۔
{8} And the sunnah of ghusl is that the bather begins by washing his hands and private parts, and removes any impurity if on his body, then performs wudu as for prayer except his feet. Then he pours water over his head and the rest of his body three times, then moves away from that place and washes his feet. And it is not required for a woman to undo her braids in ghusl if water reaches the roots of the hair. Evidence (1) hadith for establishing the sunnah of ghusl: from Aisha that when the Messenger of Allah ﷺ performed ghusl from janabah, he would begin by washing his hands, then pour water from his right onto his left and wash his private parts, then perform wudu as for prayer, then take water and insert his fingers into the roots of his hair until he saw that he had thoroughly wetted, then he would scoop three handfuls onto his head, then pour over the rest of his body, then wash his feet. (Muslim #316) Evidence (1) hadith for establishing the sunnah: from Umm Salamah who said: I said, O Messenger of Allah, I am a woman who tightly braids my hair; should I undo it for ghusl of janabah? He said: 'No. It is sufficient for you to pour three handfuls over your head, then pour water over yourself and you become pure.' (Muslim #330) Evidence (2) hadith: (from the same) then she pours over her head and rubs it vigorously until water reaches the roots of her hair. (Muslim #332) Vocabulary: فَرْجَه : private parts, وَيُزِيلُ : to remove, يُفيضُ : to pour, يتنحى: to move away.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage details the sunnah (recommended) method of performing ghusl. The matn outlines the sequence: start by washing hands and private parts, remove any impurity, then perform wudu like for prayer but leave feet until the end. Then pour water over the head and body three times, then move to a different spot to wash the feet (to avoid standing in dirty water). It also specifies that women need not undo their braids if water can reach the roots; this is a dispensation to avoid hardship. The hadith from Aisha describes the Prophet's practice exactly as in the matn. The hadith from Umm Salamah confirms that women are not required to undo braids; pouring water over the head is sufficient. A second narration adds that she should vigorously rub her head to ensure water reaches the roots. The vocabulary list translates key terms into Urdu.

Key Terms
سُنَّةُ الْغُسْلِ (sunnat al-ghusl): The recommended method of performing the ritual bath, based on the Prophet's practice.
صَفَائِر (ṣafā'ir): Braids of hair on a woman's head.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on the specific sequence of ghusl described in this lesson?
A) It is fard and must be followed exactly.
B) It is sunnah muakkadah; omitting any step does not invalidate ghusl.
C) It is wajib and requires compensation if missed.
D) It is optional with no reward.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's method of ghusl is sunnah muakkadah; following it brings reward, but the obligation is merely washing the entire body with intention.

Ruling on Women Undoing Braids in Ghusl
Describing the ruling on women undoing braids for ghusl with hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a woman with braided hair performing ghusl and explain the evidence from the hadith of Umm Salamah.

Core Idea
Women need not undo braids for ghusl if water reaches the roots; pouring three handfuls suffices.

This lesson addresses a common concern for women with braided hair: must they undo their braids when performing ghusl? Based on the hadith of Umm Salamah, the Prophet ﷺ said it is not required, as long as water reaches the roots of the hair. This ruling alleviates hardship and is the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
State the question
The issue: is a woman required to undo her braids for ghusl to be valid?
2
Examine the hadith evidence
Umm Salamah asked the Prophet if she must undo her braids; he said 'No' and explained that pouring three handfuls is sufficient.
3
Apply the condition
The dispensation is conditional upon water reaching the roots of the hair. If braids are so tight that water does not penetrate, she must undo or at least ensure roots are wetted.
4
Understand the Hanafi vs Shafi'i difference
Hanafi: if water reaches roots, braids need not be undone. Shafi'i: they must be undone if water cannot reach the scalp through them.
The difference stems from interpreting the condition 'if water reaches the roots'.

{8} وَسُنَّةُ الْغُسْلِ أَنْ يَبْدَأَ الْمُغْتَسِلُ فَيَغْسِلَ يَدَيْهِ وَفَرْجَهُ وَيُزِيلُ تَجَاسَةً إِنْ كَانَتْ عَلَى بَدَنِهِ يَتَوَضأُ وُضُوءَهُ لِلصَّلَاةِ إِلَّا رِجْلَيْهِ. ثُمَّ يُفِيضُ الْمَاءَ عَلَى رَأْسِهِ وَسَائِرٍ جَسَدِهِ ثَلَاثًا ثُمَّ يَتَنَحَّى عَنْ ذَلِكَ الْمَكَانِ فَيَغْسِلُ رِجْلَيْهِ وَلَيْسَ عَلَى الْمَرْأَةِ أَنْ تَنْقُضَ صَفَائِرَهَا فِي الْغُسْلِ إِذَا بَلَغَ الْمَاءُ أُصُولَ الشَّعْرِ.  وجه : (١) الحديث لثبوت سُنَّةُ الْغُسْلِ أَنْ يَبْدَأَ الْمُغْتَسِلُ فَيَغْسِلَ يَدَيْهِ \ عن عائشة؛ قالت كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إِذَا اغْتَسَلَ مِنَ الْجَنَابَةِ، يَبْدَأُ فَيَغْسِلُ يَدَيْهِ ثُمَّ يُفْرِخُ بِيَمِينِهِ عَلَى شِمَالِهِ. فَيَغْسِلُ فَرْجَهُ. ثم يتوضأ وضوئه لِلصَّلَاةِ. ثُمَّ يَأْخُذُ الْمَاءَ فَيُدْخِلُ أَصَابِعَهُ فِي أُصُولِ الشَّعْرِ. حَتَّى إِذَا رَأَى أَنْ قَدِ اسْتَبْرَأَ حَفَنَ عَلَى رَأْسِهِ ثَلَاثَ حَفَنَاتٍ ثُمَّ أَفَاضَ عَلَى سَائِرِ جَسَدِهِ. ثُمَّ غَسَلَ رجُلَيْهِ(مسلم شریف ، باب صفَةِ غُسل الجنابة، غمبر (316) ا وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت سُنَّةُ الْغُسْلِ: لَيْسَ عَلَى الْمَرْأَةِ أَنْ تَنْقُضَ صَفَائِرَهَا فِي الْغُسْلِ \ عَنْ أُمّ سَلَمَةَ، قَالَتْ: قُلْتُ يَارَسُولَ اللهِ إِنّي امْرَأَةٌ أَشُدُّ ضَفْرَ رَأْسِي فَأَنْقُضُهُ لِغُسْلِ الْجَنَابَةِ؟ قَالَ: «لَا. إِنَّمَا يَكْفِيكِ أَنْ تَحْيِي عَلَى رَأْسِكِ ثَلَاثَ حَشَيَاتٍ ثُمَّ تُفِيضِينَ عَلَيْكِ الْمَاءَ فَتَطْهُرِينَ» (مسلم، بَابُ حُكْمِ ضَفَائِرِ الْمُعْتَسِلَةِ، غير 330/) وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت سُنَّةُ الْغُسْلِ: لَيْسَ عَلَى الْمَرْأَةِ أَنْ تَنْقُضَ ضَفَائِرَهَا فِي الْغُسْلِ اثُمَّ تَصُبُّ عَلَى رَأْسِهَا فَتَدْلُكُهُ دَلْكًا شَدِيدًا حَتَّى تَبْلُغَ شُؤُونَ رَأْسِهَا، (مسلم، بَابُ اسْتِحْبَابِ اسْتِعْمَالِ الْمُغْتَسِلَةِ مِنَ الْخَيْضِ فِرْصَةً مِنْ مِسْكِ فِي مَوْضِعِ الدَّمِ، نمبر (332) لغات: فَرْجَه : شرم گاه ، وَيُزِيلُ : زائل کرنا ، ختم کرنا، يُفيضُ : بہانا، پہنچانا، يتنحى: صاف کرنا۔
{8} And the sunnah of ghusl is that the bather begins by washing his hands and private parts, and removes any impurity if on his body, then performs wudu as for prayer except his feet. Then he pours water over his head and the rest of his body three times, then moves away from that place and washes his feet. And it is not required for a woman to undo her braids in ghusl if water reaches the roots of the hair. Evidence (1) hadith for establishing the sunnah of ghusl: from Aisha that when the Messenger of Allah ﷺ performed ghusl from janabah, he would begin by washing his hands, then pour water from his right onto his left and wash his private parts, then perform wudu as for prayer, then take water and insert his fingers into the roots of his hair until he saw that he had thoroughly wetted, then he would scoop three handfuls onto his head, then pour over the rest of his body, then wash his feet. (Muslim #316) Evidence (1) hadith for establishing the sunnah: from Umm Salamah who said: I said, O Messenger of Allah, I am a woman who tightly braids my hair; should I undo it for ghusl of janabah? He said: 'No. It is sufficient for you to pour three handfuls over your head, then pour water over yourself and you become pure.' (Muslim #330) Evidence (2) hadith: (from the same) then she pours over her head and rubs it vigorously until water reaches the roots of her hair. (Muslim #332) Vocabulary: فَرْجَه : private parts, وَيُزِيلُ : to remove, يُفيضُ : to pour, يتنحى: to move away.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage details the sunnah (recommended) method of performing ghusl. The matn outlines the sequence: start by washing hands and private parts, remove any impurity, then perform wudu like for prayer but leave feet until the end. Then pour water over the head and body three times, then move to a different spot to wash the feet (to avoid standing in dirty water). It also specifies that women need not undo their braids if water can reach the roots; this is a dispensation to avoid hardship. The hadith from Aisha describes the Prophet's practice exactly as in the matn. The hadith from Umm Salamah confirms that women are not required to undo braids; pouring water over the head is sufficient. A second narration adds that she should vigorously rub her head to ensure water reaches the roots. The vocabulary list translates key terms into Urdu.

Key Terms
صَفَائِر (ṣafā'ir): Braids of hair on a woman's head.
ضَفْر (ḍafr): The act of braiding hair.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when must a woman undo her braids for ghusl?
A) Never; she can always leave them.
B) Only if water does not reach the roots of her hair.
C) Always, because the fard is to wash every strand.
D) Only if she plans to pray afterwards.

Key Takeaway
Women need not undo braids for ghusl, provided water reaches the roots; otherwise they must take measures to ensure it does.

Sunnah Ghusl for Friday, Eid, and Ihram
Providing hadith proofs for the sunnah status of ghusl on Friday, Eid, and entering ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ghusl for Friday, the two Eids, and Ihram, and explain how the two hadiths together establish this as sunnah muakkadah.

Core Idea
Ghusl on Friday, Eid, and Ihram is sunnah muakkadah, not wajib—the second hadith clarifies the first.

You may have heard the hadith 'Ghusl on Friday is obligatory' and wondered why Hanafis call it sunnah. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi method of harmonizing multiple proofs, showing how the school derives the ruling that ghusl is a strongly recommended practice, not a binding obligation. We will examine the two key hadiths and see how they work together.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The matn states that the Prophet prescribed ghusl for Friday, the two Eids, and Ihram. The ruling level in the Hanafi school is sunnah muakkadah. Confirm this from the text.
The Urdu summary adds Arafah, but the core matn focuses on these three.
2
Locate the first proof (dalil)
The first hadith (Abu Sa'id al-Khudri) uses the word 'wajib'. Identify the source and the literal meaning.
Hadith transmitted by Abu Dawud and Muslim, so it is sound (sahih).
3
Locate the second proof (dalil) and its function
The second hadith (Samurah) states that wudu is sufficient and ghusl is better. This hadith provides the key to interpreting the first one: the term 'wajib' does not indicate legal obligation but strong recommendation.
The Hanafi principle: a general command can be reinterpreted in light of other evidence.
4
Note the cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
Some Shafi'i scholars hold that Friday ghusl is wajib based on the literal command. The Hanafi school responds by citing the second hadith as a clarifier (bayān).
This difference is a legitimate ikhtilaf (mukhtalaf fīh).
5
Evaluate the tarjih (preferred view)
The Hanafi muftā bihī is sunnah muakkadah. The second hadith's explicit permission of wudu overrides the apparent command of the first, in accordance with the principle of al-jamʿ wa al-tawfīq (reconciliation).
Imam al-Shaybani recorded this as the position of Āl al-Rasūl in the Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَسَنَّ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ - صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ - الْغُسْلَ لِلْجُمُعَةِ وَالْعِيدَيْنِ وَالْإِحْرَامِ

وَجْهُ (١) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ ذَلِكَ: عَنْ أَبِي سَعِيدٍ الْخُدْرِيِّ، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «غُسْلُ يَوْمِ الْجُمُعَةِ وَاجِبٌ عَلَى كُلِّ مُحْتَلِمٍ» (رَوَاهُ أَبُو دَاوُدَ وَمُسْلِمٌ)

وَجْهُ (٢) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ ذَلِكَ: عَنْ سَمُرَةَ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «مَنْ تَوَضَّأَ يَوْمَ الْجُمُعَةِ فَبِهَا وَنِعْمَتْ، وَمَنِ اغْتَسَلَ فَهُوَ أَفْضَلُ» (رَوَاهُ أَبُو دَاوُدَ وَمُسْلِمٌ)

وَجْهُ (٣) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ الْمَعَانِي الْمُوجِبَةِ لِلْغُسْلِ إِنْزَالُ الْمَنِيِّ: عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ، قَالَ: كَانَ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ يَغْتَسِلُ يَوْمَ الْفِطْرِ وَيَوْمَ الْأَضْحَى (رَوَاهُ ابْنُ مَاجَهْ)

اصول: چار مقامات پر غسل کرنا مسنون ہے، ۱ جمعہ، ۲ عیدین، ۳ حرام پہنے کے وقت، ۴ عرفہ کے وقت۔
And the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) prescribed ghusl for Friday, the two Eids, and ihram. Proof (1) hadith for that: from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri that the Prophet said: "Ghusl on Friday is obligatory upon every pubescent person." (narrated by Abu Dawud and Muslim) Proof (2) hadith for that: from Samurah, he said: "Whoever performs wudu on Friday has done well, and whoever performs ghusl is better." (narrated by Abu Dawud and Muslim) Proof (3) hadith for establishing the causes that necessitate ghusl: emission of maniy: from Ibn Abbas, he said: The Prophet used to perform ghusl on Fitr and Adha. (narrated by Ibn Majah) Principle: Ghusl is sunnah at four occasions: 1 Friday, 2 the two Eids, 3 when putting on ihram, 4 at Arafah.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. The base matn states that the Prophet (peace be upon him) prescribed ghusl for Friday, the two Eids, and for ihram. The commentator then provides hadith evidence. The first proof is the hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri where the Prophet says ghusl on Friday is 'wajib' on every person who has reached puberty. This hadith appears to command obligation, but the second proof from Samurah clarifies that performing wudu is acceptable and ghusl is better. Hence, the Hanafi school interprets 'wajib' here as sunnah muakkadah, not fard. The third proof mentions the occasions (Eid and possibly the general ruling of ghusl for maniy, though the text here is a bit jumbled). The Urdu summary concludes that ghusl is sunnah at four places: Friday, the two Eids, when entering ihram, and at Arafah. Note: The mention of Arafah is not in the original matn but is added by the commentator based on other narrations.

Key Terms
الغسل للجمعة (al-ghuslu lil-jumu'ah): Ghusl performed on Friday before the Jumu'ah prayer; considered sunnah muakkadah in the Hanafi school.
العيدين (al-`idayn): The two annual Islamic festivals: Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha.
الإحرام (al-ihram): The state of consecration for Hajj or Umrah; ghusl before entering ihram is sunnah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling of ghusl on Friday?
A) Fard
B) Wajib
C) Sunnah muakkadah
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school classifies ghusl for Friday, the two Eids, and Ihram as sunnah muakkadah, based on a balance of hadith evidence that reconciles the command 'wajib' with the permission of wudu.
