No Ghusl for Madhiy and Wadiy, Only Wudu
Establishing that madhiy and wadiy require wudu, not ghusl, with hadith and usool proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for madhiy and wadiy, identify the hadith proofs, and distinguish them from maniy.

Core Idea
Madhiy and wadiy require wudu, not ghusl, because they are not maniy.

This lesson establishes the Hanafi position that only wudu is required for madhiy and wadiy, in contrast to maniy which requires ghusl. We will examine the textual proofs from the hadith and the principle that differentiates these fluids based on their characteristics.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the emission of madhiy or wadiy. The ruling is that no ghusl is required, only wudu.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The first hadith from Tirmidhi and Abu Dawud: 'Min al-madhi al-wudu, wa min al-maniy al-ghusl.' This directly gives the ruling.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit distinction between madhiy and maniy: madhiy leads to wudu, maniy leads to ghusl. The command is clear and not subject to interpretation.
4
Note secondary proofs
The second hadith from Abdullah ibn Sa'd describes washing the private parts and testicles for madhiy and then wudu, without ghusl. The narration from Ikrimah defines the three fluids and their rulings.
The third proof is not a hadith but a statement from a tabi'i, confirming the understanding.
5
Understand the underlying principle
Madhiy and wadiy are not maniy because they do not come out with force and desire. The Urdu summary states: 'they are not maniy, and do not come out with force, so ghusl is not wajib.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَيْسَ فِي الْمَذْيِ وَالْوَدْي غُسْلٌ وَفِيهِمَا الْوُضُوءُ

وَجْهُ (١) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ ذَلِكَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «مِنَ الْمَذْيِ الْوُضُوءُ، وَمِنَ الْمَنِيِّ الْغُسْلُ» (رَوَاهُ التِّرْمِذِيُّ وَأَبُو دَاوُدَ)

وَجْهُ (٢) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ ذَلِكَ: عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ سَعْدٍ الْأَنْصَارِيِّ، قَالَ: سَأَلْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ عَمَّا يُوجِبُ الْغُسْلَ، وَعَنِ الْمَاءِ يَكُونُ بَعْدَ الْمَاءِ، فَقَالَ: «ذَاكَ الْمَذْيُ، وَكُلُّ فَحْلٍ يَمْذِي فَتَغْسِلُ مِنْ ذَلِكَ فَرْجَكَ وَأُنْثَيَيْكَ، وَتَوَضَّأْ وُضُوءَكَ لِلصَّلَاةِ» (رَوَاهُ أَبُو دَاوُدَ)

وَجْهُ (٣) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ ذَلِكَ: عَنْ عِكْرِمَةَ قَالَ: ثَلَاثَةٌ: الْمَذْيُ، وَالْوَدْيُ، وَالْمَنِيُّ. فَأَمَّا الْمَذْيُ: فَهُوَ الَّذِي يَكُونُ مَعَ الْبَوْلِ وَبَعْدَهُ فِيهِ غَسْلُ الْفَرْجِ وَالْوُضُوءُ أَيْضًا. وَأَمَّا الْمَنِيُّ: فَهُوَ الْمَاءُ الدَّافِقُ الَّذِي يَكُونُ فِيهِ الشَّهْوَةُ، وَمِنْهُ يَكُونُ الْوَلَدُ فَفِيهِ الْغُسْلُ. (مُصَنَّفُ عَبْدِ الرَّزَّاقِ)

اصول: مذی اور ودی دونوں منی نہیں ہیں، اور نہ کسی کو دکر نکلتے ہیں اس لئے ان سے غسل واجب نہیں ہو گا۔
And there is no ghusl for madhiy and wadiy, and (only) wudu is required for them. Proof (1) hadith for that: The Messenger of Allah said: 'From madhiy (requires) wudu, and from maniy (requires) ghusl.' (narrated by Tirmidhi and Abu Dawud) Proof (2) hadith for that: From Abdullah ibn Sa'd al-Ansari, he said: I asked the Prophet about what necessitates ghusl and about the water that comes after urine. He said: 'That is madhiy, and every male emits madhiy, so wash from that your private parts and testicles, and perform wudu as for prayer.' (narrated by Abu Dawud) Proof (3) from Ikrimah: Three things: madhiy, wadiy, and maniy. As for madhiy: it occurs with urine or after it, requiring washing the private part and wudu. As for maniy: it is the fluid that spurts out with desire, and from it comes the child; it requires ghusl. (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq) Principle: Madhiy and wadiy are both not maniy, and they do not come out with force, so ghusl is not obligatory from them.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. The matn states that madhiy (pre-ejaculatory fluid) and wadiy (thin fluid after urine) do not require ghusl; they only require wudu. The commentator provides three proofs. The first is a hadith where the Prophet explicitly distinguishes: madhiy requires wudu, maniy requires ghusl. The second hadith expands on the ruling, describing that madhiy comes from every male and necessitates washing the private parts and testicles, and then wudu. The third narration from Ikrimah defines the three types of fluids: madhiy (fluid with or after urine, requiring washing and wudu), wadiy (similar), and maniy (spurting fluid with desire that requires ghusl). The Urdu summary explains that madhiy and wadiy are not maniy and do not gush out forcefully, therefore ghusl is not wajib. The key distinction is based on the nature of the fluid: maniy is discharged with force and desire, while madhiy and wadiy are not.

Key Terms
المذي (al-madhi): A thin, sticky fluid that exits from the private part due to desire or foreplay, but without the force or pleasure of orgasm. It requires wudu and washing the affected area.
الودي (al-wadi): A thick, white fluid that sometimes exits after urination. It has the same ruling as madhiy: wudu and washing are required, not ghusl.
المني (al-maniy): The fluid that spurts out with force and desire during orgasm; it requires ghusl (ritual bath).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling for madhiy?
A) Ghusl is required
B) Only wudu is required
C) Nothing is required
D) Both wudu and ghusl are required

Key Takeaway
Madhiy and wadiy require only wudu, not ghusl, as explicitly stated in the hadith and distinguished from maniy.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
Water Overcome by Pure Substances: Ruling and Proofs
Matn + proofs on impermissible water for purification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on water mixed with a dominant pure substance and identify the two hadith proofs that support it.

Core Idea
Water loses its purifying ability when another substance overwhelmingly changes its nature.

This lesson from Al-Quduri addresses two categories of water that cannot be used for purification: water extracted from trees/fruits, and water whose natural character has been overcome by another substance. The matn states the ruling concisely, and the commentary provides two hadith proofs to ground the second category. By the end, you will understand the evidentiary basis for the Hanafi position and the principle of 'mugallab' (overcome).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two impermissible water types
Read the matn: 'ولا يجوز بما اعتصر من الشجرة والثمر' (juices from trees/fruits) and 'ولا بماء غلب عليه غيره فأخرجه عن طبع الماء' (water overcome by other substance). Recognise that both are impermissible for purification.
The first type is extracted juices; the second is water whose nature has changed due to a pure additive.
2
Analyse the first hadith (Abu Umamah)
The hadith states that water is only made impure (najis) if its smell, taste, or colour changes. The Hanafi school applies this to pure substances: even if the additive is pure, if it dominates, the water loses its purifying status.
The hadith is about najasah, but the 'illa (effective cause) is change in properties; for pure additives, the same effect (loss of purifying ability) applies.
3
Analyse the second hadith (Ibn Mas'ud)
The Prophet used nabidh (date-infused water) for wudu, calling it 'pure water'. This shows that as long as the water dominates (mugallab), the mixture remains tahur. The second hadith provides the counterpoint to the first: the water in nabidh was dominant, so it was permissible.
The second hadith is used synergistically with the first to establish the boundary: if the additive overcomes, it's impermissible; if it's overcome, it's permissible.
4
Synthesise the principles (Usul)
The Urdu principles summarise: natural water sources (rain, sea, wells) are pure; water mixed with a pure substance remains permissible as long as the substance is overcome (mugallab). The ruling in the matn is an exception to this general permissibility.
The usul confirms the general rule and the specific exception.
5
Apply to a new scenario
Test the principle: Is water mixed with thick mango pulp (which changes colour and taste) permissible for wudu? Answer: No, because the additive dominates and changes the water's nature.
If the additive is overcome (e.g., a few drops of rose water in a large bucket), it remains permissible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلا يَجُوزُ بِمَا اُعْتُصِرَ مِنْ الشَّجَرَةِ وَالثَّمَرِ وَلَا بِمَاءٍ غَلَبَ عَلَيْهِ غَيْرُهُ فَأَخْرَجَهُ عَنْ طَبْعِ الْمَاءِ كَالأَشْرِبَةِ وَمَاءُ الْبَاقِلَاءِ وَمَاءُ الزَّرْدَج .
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا بِمَاءٍ غَلَبَ عَلَيْهِ غَيْرُهُ فَأَخْرَجَهُ عَنْ طَبْعِ الْمَاءِ \ عَنْ أَبِي أُمَامَةَ الْبَاهِلِي قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «إِنَّ الْمَاءَ لَا يُنَجِّسُهُ شَيْءٌ إِلَّا مَا غَلَبَ عَلَى رِيحِهِ وَطَعْمِهِ وَلَوْنِهِ» (ابن ماجه ، بَابُ الْحَيَاضِ ، 521/ طحاوي، بَابُ الْمَاءِ يَقَعُ فِيهِ النَّجَاسَةُ، 15)
وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا بِمَاءٍ غَلَبَ عَلَيْهِ غَيْرُهُ فَأَخْرَجَهُ عَنْ طَبْعِ الْمَاءِ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ مَسْعُودٍ، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ لَهُ لَيْلَةَ الْحِنَ عِنْدَكَ طَهُورٌ» قَالَ: لَا، إِلَّا شَيْءٌ مِنْ نَبِيدٍ فِي إِدَاوَةٍ، قَالَ: «ثَمَرَةٌ طَيِّبَةٌ وَمَاءٌ طَهُورٌ» فَتَوَضَّأَ (ابن ماجه بَابُ الْوُضُوءُ بِالنَّبِيذ، نمبر 384/سنن الدارقطني ، بَابُ الْوُضُوءِ بِالنَّبِيذِ، نمبر 241)
اصول: آسمان کا بر ساپانی، وادی، چشمہ ، کنواں، اور سمندرکا پانی پاک ہے ان سے پاکی حاصل کرنا جائز ہے۔
اصول: پانی میں پاک شی ملا دی جائے تو جب تک وہ شی مغلوب ہو اس سے وضو اور غسل جائز ہے۔
And it is not permissible with what is expressed from the tree and fruit, nor with water that another thing has overcome, removing it from the nature of water, like beverages and bean water and safflower water. Proof (1): Hadith for establishing 'nor with water that another thing has overcome, removing it from the nature of water' from Abu Umamah al-Bahili, he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Indeed water is not made impure by anything except what overcomes its smell, taste, and color.' Proof (2): Hadith for establishing 'nor with water that another thing has overcome, removing it from the nature of water' from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said to him on the night of the jinn: 'Do you have purification?' He said: No, except some nabidh in a small waterskin. He said: 'A good fruit and pure water' and he performed wudu with it. Principle: Rainwater, valley water, spring water, well water, and sea water are pure; it is permissible to obtain purification from them. Principle: If a pure thing is mixed with water, as long as that thing is overcome (in quantity), wudu and ghusl are permissible with it.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage contains two rulings from the matn of Al-Quduri on water that is not permissible for purification. First, water expressed from trees or fruits (like grape juice) cannot be used because it is no longer naturally pure water. Second, water that has been overcome by another substance such that it loses its natural character (like beverages, bean water, or safflower water) is also impermissible. The commentary then provides two hadith proofs for the second ruling: the first from Abu Umamah stating that water is only rendered impure if its smell, taste, or color changes; the second from Ibn Mas'ud where the Prophet used nabidh (a drink from dates) as water because it was mixed but the water was still dominant. The Urdu principles at the end summarize that natural water sources are pure, and water mixed with a pure substance is still usable as long as the added substance is overcome (mugallab).

Key Terms
ماء طهور (ma' tahūr): Water that is inherently pure and purifying (can be used for wudu and ghusl).
مغلوب (mugallab): Something (pure) added to water that is less in quantity than the water, so the water's nature remains dominant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, is it permissible to perform wudu with water that has been mixed with saffron to the point that it changes the water's color and smell?
A) Yes, because saffron is pure.
B) No, because the water's nature has been overcome.
C) Yes, as long as the saffron is less than half.
D) No, unless the water is from a sea.

Key Takeaway
Water loses its purifying ability when a pure substance dominates and changes its natural properties, as evidenced by the hadiths of Abu Umamah and Ibn Mas'ud.

Taharah — Purification
beginner
8 min
Rulings on Water Mixed with Pure Substances and Water with Impurity (with Proofs)
Rulings on water mixed with pure substances and water with impurity, with proofs from hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi rulings on water purity: (1) water mixed with a pure substance that changes its properties is valid for purification, and (2) water into which any impurity falls is invalid, and cite the prophetic proofs for each.

Core Idea
Water mixed with a pure additive remains valid; water touched by impurity becomes invalid — the Prophet's commands settle the rule.

This passage from Al-Quduri presents two core rulings of taharah regarding water. The first permits purification with water that has been mixed with a pure substance, even if it changes in color, taste, or smell. The second declares any water into which impurity falls to be unusable for wudu or ghusl, regardless of quantity. The text then supports these rulings with hadith from the Prophet (peace be upon him), illustrating how the Hanafi school derives its positions from the sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
Read the matn and distinguish the first ruling (water changed by pure additive) from the second (water with impurity). Note the key phrases: 'وَتَجُوزُ الطَّهَارَةُ بِمَاءٍ خَالَطَهُ شَيْءٌ طَاهِرٌ' and 'وَكُلُّ مَاءٍ وَقَعَتْ فِيهِ نَجَاسَةٌ لَمْ يَجْزِ الْوُضُوءُ بِهِ'.
The first ruling uses 'خالطه' (mixed), the second uses 'وقعت فيه' (fell into).
2
Analyze the proof for the first ruling
Examine the hadith of washing the deceased with water and sidr. Note that sidr is a pure additive that changes water. The Prophet's command indicates permissibility despite the change.
Hadith source: Muslim, Ibn Majah.
3
Analyze the proofs for the second ruling
Three hadith are cited: prohibition of urinating in standing water, prohibition of bathing in standing water while junub, and command to wash hands after sleep. Each implies impurity renders water unusable.
The first two directly address najasah; the third is precautionary.
4
Derive the Hanafi position
From these proofs, the Hanafi school concludes that any amount of impurity invalidates water for purification, and that pure additives do not affect validity as long as the water remains called 'water'.
Contrast with other schools that require water not to have changed at all.
5
Apply to modern scenarios
Consider cases: soap in bathwater (valid), a drop of oil (valid), a drop of urine in a large tank (invalid). Identify the operative factor: pure additive vs. impurity.
The additive must be pure and not overpower the water's original substance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَتَجُوزُ الطَّهَارَةُ بِمَاءٍ خَالَطَهُ شَيْءٌ طَاهِرٌ فَغَيَّرَ أَحَدَ أَوْصَافِهِ كَمَاءِ الْمَةِ وَالْمَاءُ الَّذِي يَخْتَلِطُ بِهِ الْأَشْنَانُ وَالصَّابُونُ وَالزَّعْفَرَانُ . وَكُلُّ مَاءٍ وَقَعَتْ فِيهِ تَجَاسَةٌ لَمْ يَجْزَ الْوُضُوءُ بِهِ قَلِيلًا كَانَ الْمَاءُ أَوْ كَثِيرًا لِأَنَّ النَّبِيَّ - صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ - أَمَرَ بِحِفْظِ الْمَاءِ مِنْ النَّجَاسَةِ فَقَالَ لا يَبُولَنَّ أَحَدُكُمْ فِي الْمَاءِ الدَّائِم» أَيْ الرَّاكِدِ وَلَا يَغْتَسِلَنَّ فِيهِ مِنْ الْجَنَابَةِ» وَقَالَ - عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ - «إِذَا اسْتَيْقَظَ أَحَدُكُمْ مِنْ مَنَامِهِ فَلَا يَغْمِسَنَّ يَدَهُ فِي الْإِنَاءِ حَتَّى يَغْسِلَهَا ثَلَاثًا فَإِنَّهُ لَا يَدْرِي أَيْنَ بَاتَتْ يَدُهُ»
وجه : (ا) الحديث لثبوت وَتَجُوزُ الطَّهَارَةُ بِمَاءٍ خَالَطَهُ شَيْءٌ طَاهِرٌ فَغَيَّرَ أَحَدَ أَوْصَافِهِ \ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ رَضِيَ اللهُ عَنْهُمَا، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ، خَرَّ رَجُلٌ مِنْ بَعِيرِهِ، فَوْقِصَ فَمَاتَ، فَقَالَ: «اغْسِلُوهُ بِمَاءٍ وَسِدْرٍ، وَكَفَنُوهُ فِي ثَوْبَيْهِ، (مسلم، بَابُ مَا يُفْعَلُ بِالْمُحْرِمِ إِذَا ماتَ ، غمبر 1206/ ابن ماجه، بَابُ الْمُحْرِمِ يَمُوتُ ، نمبر 3084)
توجه (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَكُلُّ مَاءٍ وَقَعَتْ فِيهِ تَجَاسَةٌ لَمْ يَجْزَ الْوُضُوءُ بِهِ \ أَنَّهُ سَمِعَ أَبَا هُرَيْرَةَ، أَنَّهُ سَمِعَ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ يَقُولُ: «لاَ يَبُولَنَّ أَحَدُكُمْ فِي المَاءِ الدَّائِمِ الَّذِي لَا يَجْرِي، ثُمَّ يَغْتَسِلُ فِيهِ» (بخاري شريف، بَابُ البَوْلِ فِي المَاءِ الدَّائِمِ، نمبر 239/ مسلم، بَابُ النَّهْيِ عَنِ البَوْلِ فِي المَاءِ الرَّاكدِ، نمبر 282)
وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَكُلُّ مَاءٍ وَقَعَتْ فِيهِ تَجَاسَةٌ لَمْ يَجْزَ الْوُضُوءُ بِهِ اسَمِعَ أَبَا هُرَيْرَةَ، يَقُولُ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «لَا يَغْتَسِلْ أَحَدُكُمْ فِي الْمَاءِ الدَّائِمِ وَهُوَ جُنُبٌ»(مسلم، بَابُ النَّهْي عَنِ الْاغْتِسَالِ فِي الْمَاءِ الرَّاكِدِ، نمبر 283
وجه : (۳) الحديث لثبوت وَكُلُّ مَاءٍ وَقَعَتْ فِيهِ نَجَاسَةٌ لَمَّ يَجُزَ الْوُضُوءُ بِهِ أَعَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ، أَنَّهُ أَخْبَرَهُ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «إِذَا اسْتَيْقَظَ أَحَدُكُمْ فَلْيُفْرِغْ عَلَى يَدِهِ ثَلَاثَ مَرَّاتٍ قَبْلَ أَنْ يُدْخِلَ يَدَهُ فِي إِنَائِهِ، فَإِنَّهُ لا يَدْري فِيمَ بَاتَتْ يَدُهُ ،مسلم ، بَابُ كَرَاهَةِ غَمْسِ الْمُتَوَضِى وَغَيْرِهِ يَدَهُ الْمَشْكُوكَ فِي نَجَاسَتِهَا فِي الْإِنَاءِ قَبْلَ غَسْلِهَا ثَلَاثًا ، غمبر 278/ ترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ إِذَا اسْتَيْقَظَ أَحَدُكُمْ مِنْ مَنَامِهِ، نمبر 24)
اصول: پانی کی مزید صفائی کے لئے کوئی شمی ملا دی جائے تو اس سے وضو اور غسل جائز ہوتا ہے۔
And purification is permissible with water that a pure thing has mixed with and changed one of its descriptions, like water of the sea? [unclear] and water mixed with tooth powder, soap, and saffron. And every water into which impurity falls, wudu is not permissible with it, whether the water is little or much, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) commanded to protect water from impurity, saying: 'Let none of you urinate in standing water' i.e., stagnant, 'nor bathe in it from janabah.' And he said: 'When one of you wakes from sleep, he should not dip his hand into the vessel until he washes it three times, for he does not know where his hand spent the night.' Proof (a): Hadith for establishing 'purification with water mixed with a pure thing that changed one of its descriptions' from Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them) that a man fell from his camel and was killed, and the Prophet said: 'Wash him with water and sidr, and shroud him in his two garments.' Proof (1): Hadith for establishing 'every water into which impurity falls, wudu is not permissible with it' that he heard Abu Huraira say that the Messenger said: 'Let none of you urinate in standing water that does not flow, then bathe in it.' Proof (2): Hadith for establishing 'every water into which impurity falls, wudu is not permissible with it' from Abu Huraira that the Messenger said: 'Let none of you bathe in standing water while junub.' Proof (3): Hadith for establishing 'every water into which impurity falls, wudu is not permissible with it' from Abu Huraira that the Prophet said: 'When one of you wakes, he should pour water over his hand three times before inserting his hand into his vessel, for he does not know where his hand spent the night.' Principle: If something is added to water for further purification, then wudu and ghusl are permissible with it.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage contains two key rulings from the matn. First, water mixed with a pure substance (e.g., tooth powder, soap, saffron) that changes one of its properties (color, taste, or smell) is still valid for purification according to the Hanafi school. The hadith of washing the deceased with water and sidr (lotus leaves) supports this, as sidr is a pure additive that changes water's properties. Second, any water into which an impurity falls becomes unfit for wudu or ghusl, regardless of the water's quantity. Three hadiths support this: prohibition of urinating in standing water and bathing in it while junub, and the command to wash hands after sleep before dipping them. The Urdu principle clarifies that additives intended for cleaning do not render water impure.

Key Terms
ماء خالطه شيء طاهر (mā' khālaṭahu shay' ṭāhir): Water mixed with a pure substance that changes one of its three properties (color, taste, smell).
نجاسة (najāsah): Impurity (e.g., urine, blood) that renders water impermissible for purification if it falls into it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a small amount of urine falls into a large tank of water, what is the ruling for using that water for wudu?
A) It is permissible because the water is abundant.
B) It is not permissible because any impurity makes water unusable.
C) It is permissible only if the water's properties did not change.
D) It is makruh but valid.

Key Takeaway
Water mixed with a pure additive remains valid for purification; water contaminated by impurity becomes invalid, regardless of quantity.

Taharah — Purification
beginner
6 min
Purification with Water Mixed with Pure Substances
Ruling with hadith evidence on water mixed with pure substances.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on using water mixed with a pure substance and apply the hadith proof to justify its permissibility.

Core Idea
Water remains pure for purification even if a pure substance changes its color, taste, or smell — as long as it is still called water.

This lesson addresses a common question: can water that has changed colour or smell (e.g., from soap or saffron) still be used for wudu? Al-Quduri’s ruling and the supporting hadith provide clarity. The Hanafi position is that such water remains valid, provided the mixed substance is pure and the water has not been transformed into a different substance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The act is purification (taharah) with water that has been mixed with a pure substance and has changed one of its descriptions. The ruling is 'jā'iz' (permissible), meaning the purification is valid.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith from Ibn Abbas: when a man died during Hajj, the Prophet ordered to wash him with water and sidr. This shows that water mixed with sidr (a pure leaf) is permissible for washing.
Sidr is a pure substance.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's command 'wash him with water and sidr' indicates that using such mixed water is permissible. The imperative here indicates permissibility (ibāha) according to Hanafi usul, as there is no evidence to make it mandatory.
Hanafi rule: al-amr yufīdu al-ibāha unless there is a qarīna for wujūb.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) require water to remain completely unchanged (mutlaq) for purification. They do not accept this hadith as proof for general permissibility, but restrict it to the specific case of washing a deceased.
This is a legitimate ikhtilāf.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school considers the hadith as general proof for any purification, not just the deceased, because the 'illah (reason) is the permissibility of using water mixed with a pure substance. This is the mufta bihi position.
The Hanafi principle: 'amr of the Prophet is general unless specified.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَتَجُوزُ الطَّهَارَةُ بِمَاءٍ خَالَطَهُ شَيْءٌ طَاهِرٌ فَغَيَّرَ أَحَدَ أَوْصَافِهِ كَمَاءِ الْمَةِ وَالْمَاءُ الَّذِي يَخْتَلِطُ بِهِ الْأَشْنَانُ وَالصَّابُونُ وَالزَّعْفَرَانُ . عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ رَضِيَ اللهُ عَنْهُمَا، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ، خَرَّ رَجُلٌ مِنْ بَعِيرِهِ، فَوْقِصَ فَمَاتَ، فَقَالَ: «اغْسِلُوهُ بِمَاءٍ وَسِدْرٍ، وَكَفَنُوهُ فِي ثَوْبَيْهِ».
Purification is permissible with water that a pure substance has mixed with and changed one of its descriptions, like water of rose, and water that is mixed with tooth powder, soap, and saffron. From Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them), from the Prophet (peace be upon him): A man fell from his camel, his neck was broken, and he died. He said: “Wash him with water and sidr, and shroud him in his two garments.”
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage from Al-Quduri states a ruling on water mixed with pure substances. The ruling is that such water remains pure and permissible for purification (wudu or ghusl) even if one of its three properties (color, taste, smell) has changed, provided the substance mixed is itself pure. Examples given are rose water, water mixed with tooth powder, soap, or saffron. The hadith proof from Ibn Abbas provides evidence: when a man died in a state of ihram, the Prophet ordered to wash him with water and sidr (a type of lotus leaves). This demonstrates that water mixed with a pure substance (sidr) is acceptable for purification. The Hanafi school holds that this ruling applies as long as the substance is pure and the water is still called water. If the change is so extreme that it is no longer called water, then it is not valid. But here, the change is minimal.

Key Terms
طَهَارَة (tahārah): Purification, specifically wudu or ghusl for worship.
خَالَطَهُ (khālaṭahu): Mixed with, such that the water's properties are changed but it is still called water.
أَوْصَافِهِ (awṣāfihi): Its descriptions: color, taste, smell.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Al-Quduri, water mixed with which of the following is permissible for purification?
A) Water mixed with saffron
B) Water mixed with urine
C) Water mixed with wine
D) Water mixed with blood

Key Takeaway
Water mixed with a pure substance remains valid for purification even if it changes one of its three properties, as proven by the hadith of washing with sidr.

Water Contaminated by Impurity: Absolute Hanafi Ruling
Ruling with hadith proofs that any water containing impurity is invalid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on water contaminated by impurity and identify the hadith evidence used to support it.

Core Idea
Any water with impurity is unfit for wudu, regardless of quantity, based on prophetic hadith.

This lesson examines the foundational Hanafi position on water impurity as presented in Al-Quduri. The text declares that any water, whether little or much, becomes impure when an impurity falls into it, rendering wudu invalid. We will analyse the hadith proofs cited and explore the intra-Hanafi dispute that later qualified this absolute ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Read the opening statement: 'any water in which an impurity falls, wudu is not permissible, whether little or much.' This is the core ruling – absolute and unconditional.
The phrase 'kullu ma'in' (any water) indicates generality.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The text cites multiple hadith, beginning with the prohibition of urinating in still water and bathing in it. Identify the key hadith and its source.
The primary hadith is ‘No one should urinate in still water then bathe in it.’
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (legal implication)
Explain how the prohibition implies that the water becomes impure. The imperative 'la yabulanna' indicates prohibition, and the consequence of bathing in it is implicitly invalid if the water is impure.
Hanafi usul: an imperative prohibition (nahy) indicates the act is haram and its object is impure.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (intra-Hanafi)
Abu Hanifa holds the absolute view. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf & Muhammad) differentiate: large water (two qullas or more) only becomes impure if its properties change. Identify this dispute.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school.
5
Evaluate the tarjih (preferred view)
Later Hanafi scholars (mutakhkhirin) prefer the Sahibayn's view for large water. Know that the mufta bihi differs from the matn's apparent meaning.
This demonstrates the evolution of fiqh within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَكُلُّ مَاءٍ وَقَعَتْ فِيهِ تَجَاسَةٌ لَمْ يَجْزَ الْوُضُوءُ بِهِ قَلِيلًا كَانَ الْمَاءُ أَوْ كَثِيرًا لِأَنَّ النَّبِيَّ - صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ - أَمَرَ بِحِفْظِ الْمَاءِ مِنْ النَّجَاسَةِ فَقَالَ لا يَبُولَنَّ أَحَدُكُمْ فِي الْمَاءِ الدَّائِم» أَيْ الرَّاكِدِ وَلَا يَغْتَسِلَنَّ فِيهِ مِنْ الْجَنَابَةِ» وَقَالَ - عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ - «إِذَا اسْتَيْقَظَ أَحَدُكُمْ مِنْ مَنَامِهِ فَلَا يَغْمِسَنَّ يَدَهُ فِي الْإِنَاءِ حَتَّى يَغْسِلَهَا ثَلَاثًا فَإِنَّهُ لَا يَدْرِي أَيْنَ بَاتَتْ يَدُهُ». وَعَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ: عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ... (الحديث السابق) وَعَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ: أَنَّهُ سَمِعَ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ يَقُولُ: «لاَ يَبُولَنَّ أَحَدُكُمْ فِي المَاءِ الدَّائِمِ الَّذِي لَا يَجْرِي، ثُمَّ يَغْتَسِلُ فِيهِ». وَعَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «لَا يَغْتَسِلْ أَحَدُكُمْ فِي الْمَاءِ الدَّائِمِ وَهُوَ جُنُبٌ». وَعَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ: أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «إِذَا اسْتَيْقَظَ أَحَدُكُمْ فَلْيُفْرِغْ عَلَى يَدِهِ ثَلَاثَ مَرَّاتٍ قَبْلَ أَنْ يُدْخِلَ يَدَهُ فِي إِنَائِهِ، فَإِنَّهُ لا يَدْري فِيمَ بَاتَتْ يَدُهُ».
And any water in which an impurity falls, wudu is not permissible with it, whether the water is little or much, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) commanded to protect water from impurity and said: 'Let none of you urinate in still water' i.e. stagnant, 'and let him not perform ghusl from janabah in it.' And he (peace be upon him) said: 'When any of you wakes from sleep, let him not dip his hand into the vessel until he washes it three times, for he does not know where his hand spent the night.'
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage states a key Hanafi ruling: any water, regardless of quantity, becomes impure if an impurity falls into it. This is the view of Imam Abu Hanifah. The text provides three hadith proofs: 1) Prohibition of urinating in stagnant water and then bathing in it. 2) Prohibition of bathing in stagnant water while in janabah. 3) The hadith about not dipping the hand without washing it first, indicating that if the hand is impure, the water becomes impure. The Hanafi school takes these hadith as evidence that impurities render water impure regardless of quantity. However, this ruling is qualified by the next lesson on running water and large ponds.

Key Terms
نَجَاسَة (najāsah): Impurity, such as urine, blood, or wine.
مَاء دَائِم (mā' dā'im): Still water that does not flow.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited in the text, what does the Prophet prohibit regarding stagnant water?
A) Drinking from it
B) Urinating in it and bathing in it
C) Using it for cooking
D) Storing it in vessels

Key Takeaway
The absolute Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa) holds that any water touched by impurity becomes impure regardless of quantity, based on prophetic hadith, though the mufta bihi view qualifies for large water.

Running Water and Large Ponds: Exception to Impurity Rule
Ruling on running water and large ponds with hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for impurity in running water and large ponds, identify the condition for purity, and cite the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Running water and vast ponds remain pure unless impurity leaves a visible trace.

You already know that still water in small amounts becomes impure when impurity falls into it. This lesson presents an important exception: running water (like rivers) and very large ponds do not become impure unless the impurity changes the water's smell, taste, or colour. The reason is that flow prevents settling, and vastness prevents the impurity from reaching the far side. A hadith from Abu Umamah supports this principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two water bodies
Note the two types: running water (mā' jārī) and a large pond (ghadīr 'aẓīm). Both are exceptions to the general rule.
Running water flows; large pond is so vast that moving one side doesn't affect the other.
2
State the condition for purity
In both cases, wudu is permissible only if no trace of the impurity is visible (lā yurā athar).
Trace means visible change in smell, taste, or colour.
3
Understand the rationale
Running water: impurity does not settle due to flow. Large pond: impurity likely does not reach the opposite side.
The principle is that impurity is removed or diluted beyond detection.
4
Examine the hadith proof
The hadith states water is not impure unless its properties are overcome. This proves the criterion is visible change.
This hadith is used by Hanafis to support the exception, while Shafi'is use it to argue that all water remains pure until change.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا الْمَاءُ الْجَارِي إِذَا وَقَعَتْ فِيهِ نَجَاسَةٌ جَازَ الْوُضُوءُ بِهِ إِذَا لَمْ يُرَ هَا أَثَرٌ؛ لِأَنَّهَا لَا تَسْتَقِرُّ مَعَ جَرَيَانِ الْمَاءِ. وَالْغَدِيرُ الْعَظِيمُ الَّذِي لا يَتَحَرَّكُ أَحَدُ طَرَفَيْهِ إِلَى آخِرِهِ جَازَ الْوُضُوءُ مِنْ الْجَانِبِ الْأُخَرِ لِأَنَّ الظَّاهِرَ أَنَّ النَّجَاسَةَ لَا تَصِلُ إِلَيْهِ. عَنْ أَبِي أُمَامَةَ الْبَاهِلِيَ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «إِنَّ الْمَاءَ لَا يُنَجِّسُهُ شَيْءٌ إِلَّا مَا غَلَبَ عَلَى رِيحِهِ وَطَعْمِهِ وَلَوْنِهِ».
As for running water, if impurity falls into it, wudu is permissible with it when no trace of it is seen, because it does not settle with the flow of water. And a large pond, one side of which does not move to the other, wudu is permissible from the other side because the apparent assumption is that the impurity does not reach it. From Abu Umamah al-Bahili, he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: “Water is not made impure by anything except what overcomes its smell, taste, and color.”
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage provides an exception to the previous general rule. Running water (such as a river) does not become impure when an impurity falls into it, as long as no trace of the impurity is visible. The reason is that the flow prevents the impurity from settling. Similarly, a large pond (ghadir) that is so vast that moving one side does not affect the other side is treated like running water: wudu from the opposite side is valid because the impurity does not reach it. The hadith from Abu Umamah is cited as evidence: water is only impure if its properties (smell, taste, color) are overcome by impurity. This hadith supports the view that impurity does not affect large quantities or flowing water unless it changes the water. Note: This hadith is often used by the Shafi'i school to argue that quantity matters. The Hanafi school uses it to support the exception for running water and large ponds.

Key Terms
مَاء جَارِي (mā' jārī): Flowing water, such as a river or stream.
غَدِير (ghadīr): A large pond or body of water that does not flow.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the condition for performing wudu with running water after an impurity falls into it?
A) The impurity must be removed first.
B) No trace of the impurity is seen.
C) The water must be flowing fast.
D) The impurity must be solid.

Key Takeaway
Running water and vast ponds remain ritually pure after an impurity falls unless a trace of that impurity is visible.

Creatures Without Flowing Blood Do Not Spoil Water
Ruling with hadith proof on creatures without flowing blood

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on water when a creature without flowing blood dies in it and explain the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Death of an insect in water does not make it impure – the exception is creatures without flowing blood.

We often worry about a fly falling into our drink – is the water still pure? The Hanafi school gives a clear ruling based on the Prophet's guidance. In this lesson, we examine the legal category of creatures that lack flowing blood (nafs sā'ilah) and why their death does not spoil water. A key hadith about a fly in a vessel provides the proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its subject
The passage states that the death of a creature without flowing blood does not make water impure. Identify the act (a creature dying in water) and the hukm (water remains pure).
The hukm is that the water stays tahir and can be used for purification.
2
Understand the exception: nafs sā'ilah
The key concept is 'nafs sā'ilah' – flowing blood. Creatures with blood that flows when cut are the general rule; those without are the exception. Examples given: mosquitoes, flies, wasps, scorpions.
If an animal with flowing blood dies in water, it becomes najis. This is the opposite ruling.
3
Analyze the hadith evidence
The hadith: When a fly falls into a vessel, dip it entirely then throw it away. The Prophet did not order discarding the water. This implies the water remains pure – otherwise he would have ordered disposal.
The hadith also mentions healing in one wing – relevant to the command to dip fully, but the legal point is the absence of impurity declaration.
4
Confirm the Hanafi position
This ruling is from zahir al-riwayah and is mufta bihi. The Shafi'i school agrees in essence but adds the condition that the creature must not produce blood when cut. The Hanafi position is based on the general principle that carcasses are impure except those without flowing blood.
The authority weight is zahir al-riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَوْتُ مَا لَيْسَ لَهُ نَفْسٌ سَائِلَةٌ إِذَا مَاتَ فِي الْمَاءِ لَا يُنَجِّسُهُ كَالْبَقَ وَالدُّبَابِ وَالزَّنَابِيرِ وَالْعَقَارِبِ. عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «إِذَا وَقَعَ الدُّبَابُ فِي إِنَاءِ أَحَدِكُمْ فَلْيَغْمِسْهُ كُلَّهُ، ثُمَّ لِيَطْرَحْهُ، فَإِنَّ فِي أَحَدِ جَنَاحَيْهِ شِفَاءٌ، وَفِي الْآخَرِ دَاءً». وَعَنْ سَلْمَانَ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: ...
And the death of what has no flowing blood, if it dies in water, does not make it impure, like mosquitoes, flies, wasps, and scorpions. From Abu Hurairah (may Allah be pleased with him) that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'When a fly falls into the vessel of one of you, let him dip it entirely, then throw it away, for in one of its wings there is a cure, and in the other a disease.' And from Salman, he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: ...
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage deals with a specific category: creatures that do not have flowing blood (i.e., insects and similar small creatures). If such a creature dies in water, it does not render the water impure. Examples given are mosquitoes, flies, wasps, and scorpions. The hadith about the fly falling into a vessel is cited as evidence: the Prophet instructs to dip the fly completely (to extract the cure from one wing) and then remove it, but he does not declare the water impure. This indicates that the fly's death does not spoil the water. The Hanafi school holds this ruling as an exception to the general rule that carcasses are impure. The basis is that these creatures do not have flowing blood (sā'ilah), so their death does not release impure blood.

Key Terms
نَفْس سَائِلَة (nafs sā'ilah): Flowing blood; a creature with blood that flows when cut.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is the correct Hanafi ruling when a fly dies in a cup of water?
A) The water becomes impure (najis) and must be discarded.
B) The water remains pure (tahir) and can be used for purification.
C) The water is pure but its use is disliked (makruh).
D) The water becomes impure only if the fly was carrying visible najasah.

Key Takeaway
Creatures without flowing blood (nafs sā'ilah) dying in water do not render it impure – a clear exception based on the hadith of the fly.

Purity of Flowing Water and Large Ponds
Matn ruling on flowing water and large pond with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the purity of flowing water and large ponds when najasa falls into them, apply the condition of no trace, and cite the hadith proofs.

Core Idea
Flowing water and large ponds remain pure unless a trace of najasa appears — size and movement matter, not volume alone.

This lesson examines two important water sources: flowing water (rivers, streams) and large standing ponds. The Hanafi school rules that these waters remain pure (tahir) and permissible for wudu even if najasa falls into them, as long as no change in color, taste, or smell is evident. The reasoning is that flowing water does not allow najasa to settle, and in large ponds the najasa is assumed not to reach the opposite side. The lesson also presents the primary hadith proofs that establish this principle, highlighting a subtle difference with the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two water types
The passage distinguishes flowing water (al-ma' al-jari) from a large pond (al-ghadir al-'azim). Note how each is defined — flow vs. size preventing movement across.
The Hanafi definition relies on observable physical characteristics.
2
State the ruling for each
For flowing water: wudu is valid if no trace of najasa is seen. For a large pond: wudu from the opposite side is valid because najasa is presumed not to reach it.
The ruling is mubah (permissible) but the core is that water remains pure.
3
Understand the rationale
The rationale (ta'lil) is given: najasa does not settle in flowing water; in a large pond, it does not travel to the other side.
This is a practical reasoning based on common observation.
4
Examine the hadith proofs
Two hadith are cited: the first from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri about Bi'r Buda'ah (water is pure, nothing makes it impure); the second from Abu Umamah specifying that impurity only occurs when smell, taste, or color change.
The second hadith provides the key condition: change in properties indicates impurity.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some Shafi'is hold that if the water volume is less than two qullas, any najasa makes it impure even without trace. The Hanafi position relies on absence of trace regardless of volume.
This difference stems from different interpretations of the hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا الْمَاءُ الْجَارِي إِذَا وَقَعَتْ فِيهِ نَجَاسَةٌ جَازَ الْوُضُوءُ بِهِ إِذَا لَمْ يُرَ هَا أَثَرٌ؛ لِأَنَّهَا لَا تَسْتَقِرُّ مَعَ جَرَيَانِ الْمَاءِ. وَالْغَدِيرُ الْعَظِيمُ الَّذِي لا يَتَحَرَّكُ أَحَدُ طَرَفَيْهِ إِلَى آخِرِهِ جَازَ الْوُضُوءُ مِنْ الْجَانِبِ الْأُخَرِ لِأَنَّ الظَّاهِرَ أَنَّ النَّجَاسَةَ لَا تَصِلُ إِلَيْهِ. وَعَنْ أَبِي سَعِيدٍ الْخُدْرِيِّ، قَالَ: قِيلَ: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، أَتَتَوَضَّأُ مِنْ بِئْرِ بُضَاعَةَ، وَهِيَ بِئْرٌ يُلْقَى فِيهَا الْحِيَضُ، وَلُحُومُ الْكِلَابِ، وَالنَّتْنُ؟ فَقَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «إِنَّ الْمَاءَ طَهُورٌ لا يُنَجِّسُهُ شَيْءٌ» (سنن الترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ أَنَّ الْمَاءَ لَا يُنَجِّسُهُ شَيْءٌ، نمبر 66 / أَبُو دَاوُدَ، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي بِئْرِ بُضَاعَةَ، 66). وَعَنْ أَبِي أُمَامَةَ الْبَاهِلِيِّ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «إِنَّ الْمَاءَ لَا يُنَجِّسُهُ شَيْءٌ إِلَّا مَا غَلَبَ عَلَى رِيحِهِ وَطَعْمِهِ وَلَوْنِهِ» (ابْنُ مَاجَهْ، بَابُ الْحِيَاضِ، 521؛ شَرْحُ مَعَانِي الْآثَارِ، بَابُ الْمَاءِ يَقَعُ فِيهِ النَّجَاسَةُ، 24).
And as for flowing water, when najasa falls into it, wudu with it is valid if no trace of it is seen, because it does not settle with the flow of water. And a large pond, one side of which does not move to the other, wudu from the other side is valid, because the apparent assumption is that the najasa does not reach it. And from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, he said: It was said: O Messenger of Allah, do you perform wudu from Bi'r Buda'ah, a well into which menstrual cloths, dog meat, and filth are thrown? The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Verily water is pure, nothing makes it impure.' (Sunan al-Tirmidhi, chapter: What came concerning that water is not made impure by anything, no. 66; Abu Dawud, chapter: What came concerning Bi'r Buda'ah, no. 66). And from Abu Umamah al-Bahili, he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Verily water is not made impure by anything except that which overcomes its smell, taste, and color.' (Ibn Majah, chapter: Basins, no. 521; Sharh Ma'ani al-Athar, chapter: Water into which najasa falls, no. 24).
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the matn of Al-Quduri on the purity of flowing water and large ponds. The author states that flowing water remains pure if najasa falls into it, as long as no trace (color, taste, smell) of the najasa is apparent. The reason given is that najasa does not settle in flowing water. Similarly, a large pond (ghadir 'azim) that is so large that movement on one side does not affect the other; wudu from the opposite side is valid because the najasa is assumed not to reach it. The author then provides two hadith proofs: the first from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri about Bi'r Buda'ah, where the Prophet declared water naturally pure and not made impure by any substance. The second from Abu Umamah, specifying that water is only impure when its color, taste, or smell changes. These hadith support the Hanafi position that water is considered pure unless a trace of najasa is evident.

Key Terms
الْمَاءُ الْجَارِي (al-ma' al-jari): Flowing water, such as rivers and streams, where the water moves continuously.
الْغَدِيرُ الْعَظِيمُ (al-ghadir al-'azim): A large body of standing water, such that movement on one side does not reach the other.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, when does flowing water become impure after najasa falls into it?
A) Immediately upon contact with najasa.
B) Only if the water changes in color, taste, or smell.
C) Only if the volume is less than two qullas.
D) Never, regardless of any change.

Key Takeaway
Water is inherently pure; najasa only affects it when its properties visibly change.

Purity of Water When Bloodless Animals Die in It
Matn ruling with prophetic evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that the death of an animal without flowing blood in water does not make the water impure, and identify the hadith evidence used by the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Only animals with flowing blood can make water impure upon death; bloodless creatures leave the water pure.

The Hanafi school has specific rulings about what makes water impure. This passage addresses a common scenario: small insects or bloodless creatures falling into water and dying. The matn states a clear rule, and then provides prophetic hadiths as evidence. This lesson will unpack that rule and the proofs behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
From the matn: the death of animals without flowing blood (e.g., flies, mosquitoes, wasps, scorpions) in water does not make the water impure. Similarly, water-dwelling creatures like fish, frogs, and crabs also do not make water impure when they die in it.
The ruling applies regardless of the amount of water.
2
Locate the Dalil
Three hadiths are cited: the fly hadith (Bukhari), the Salman hadith (Daraqutni), and the sea water hadith (Tirmidhi). The first two directly address bloodless creatures; the third confirms that even dead sea creatures (some of which have blood?) are permissible, supporting the principle.
The fly hadith commands submerging the fly, implying the liquid remains pure.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
In the fly hadith, the Prophet (ﷺ) orders the fly to be fully submerged and then removed, rather than discarding the liquid. This indicates that the liquid is not rendered impure. The Salman hadith explicitly states that the food/drink and the wudu water are permissible (halal) when a bloodless creature dies in it.
The command to submerge the fly shows that the water remains pure; otherwise, one would not be instructed to handle the fly in the liquid.
4
Note the Ikhtilaf
Some Shafi'i scholars hold that if a large number of bloodless insects die in a small amount of water, the water may become impure due to the sheer quantity of dead matter. The Hanafi position maintains that the hadiths are general and do not specify quantity; the default is purity regardless of number.
This is a legitimate area of ikhtilaf, with both schools offering valid proofs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَوْتُ مَا لَيْسَ لَهُ نَفْسٌ سَائِلَةٌ إِذَا مَاتَ فِي الْمَاءِ لَا يُنَجِّسُهُ كَالْبَقِّ وَالدُّبَابِ وَالزَّنَابِيرِ وَالْعَقَارِبِ. وَمَوْتُ مَا يَعِيشُ فِي الْمَاءِ كَالسَّمَكِ وَالضِّفْدَعِ وَالسَّرَطَانِ فِي. وَعَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «إِذَا وَقَعَ الذُّبَابُ فِي إِنَاءِ أَحَدِكُمْ فَلْيَغْمِسْهُ كُلَّهُ، ثُمَّ لِيَطْرَحْهُ، فَإِنَّ فِي أَحَدِ جَنَاحَيْهِ شِفَاءً، وَفِي الْآخَرِ دَاءً» (بخاري بَابُ إِذَا وَقَعَ الذُّبَابُ فِي الإِنَاءِ، نمبر 5782). وَعَنْ سَلْمَانَ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «يَا سَلْمَانُ كُلُّ طَعَامٍ وَشَرَابٍ وَقَعَتْ فِيهِ دَابَّةٌ لَيْسَ لَهَا دَمٌ فَمَاتَتْ فِيهِ فَهُوَ حَلَالٌ أَكْلُهُ وَشُرْبُهُ وَوُضُوؤُهُ» (سنن الدارقطني بَابُ كُلِّ طَعَامٍ وَقَعَتْ فِيهِ دَابَّةٌ لَيْسَ لَهَا دَمٌ، نمبر 84; السنن الكبرى للبيهقي، بَابُ مَا لَا نَفْسَ لَهُ سَائِلَةٌ إِذَا مَاتَ فِي الْمَاءِ الْقَلِيلِ، نمبر 1193). وَعَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ، أَنَّهُ سَمِعَ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ يَقُولُ: «هُوَ الطَّهُورُ مَاؤُهُ الْحِلُّ مَيْتَتُهُ» (سنن الترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي مَاءِ الْبَحْرِ أَنَّهُ طَهُورٌ، نمبر 69; أَبُو دَاوُدَ، بَابُ الْوُضُوءِ بِمَاءِ الْبَحْرِ، 83).
And the death of that which has no flowing blood, when it dies in water, does not make it impure, like mosquitoes, flies, wasps, and scorpions. And the death of that which lives in water, like fish, frog, and crab, in. And from Abu Hurayrah (may Allah be pleased with him) that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'When a fly falls into the vessel of one of you, let him submerge it completely, then throw it away, for in one of its wings there is cure and in the other disease.' (Bukhari, chapter: When a fly falls into the vessel, no. 5782). And from Salman, he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'O Salman, every food and drink into which a creature that has no blood falls and dies, its eating, drinking, and wudu (with it) are permissible.' (Sunan al-Daraqutni, chapter: Every food into which a creature with no blood falls, no. 84; al-Sunan al-Kubra al-Bayhaqi, chapter: What has no flowing blood when it dies in little water, no. 1193). And from Abu Hurayrah, that he heard the Prophet (peace be upon him) say: 'It (sea water) is pure, its water is purifying and its dead are permissible.' (Sunan al-Tirmidhi, chapter: What came concerning sea water being pure, no. 69; Abu Dawud, chapter: Wudu with sea water, 83).
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage continues the matn rulings on water purity. It states that the death of animals without flowing blood (e.g., mosquitoes, flies, wasps, scorpions) in water does not make the water impure. The same applies to creatures that live in water, like fish, frogs, and crabs. The author then provides hadith evidence: the fly hadith from Bukhari indicates that a fly falling into liquid does not render it impure; rather, one should submerge it completely. The hadith from Salman explicitly states that food or drink into which a bloodless creature falls and dies is permissible to eat, drink, and use for wudu. The sea water hadith confirms that water from the sea is pure even though its dead animals (fish etc.) are permissible to eat. These proofs establish the Hanafi position that only animals with flowing blood (like mammals and birds) can make water impure upon death; bloodless creatures do not.

Key Terms
نَفْسٌ سَائِلَةٌ (nafs sa'ilah): Flowing blood; an animal with blood that flows (i.e., has a circulatory system).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following animals, if it dies in water, does NOT make the water impure according to the Hanafi school?
A) A chicken
B) A fly
C) A cat
D) A sheep

Key Takeaway
The death of animals without flowing blood (e.g., flies, mosquitoes, scorpions) in water does not render the water impure according to the Hanafi school, and this is supported by authentic hadith.

Ruling on Used Water (Musta'mal)
Matn ruling on used water with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on musta'mal water and explain the evidence from the Sunnah that supports it.

Core Idea
Musta'mal water is pure but not purifying — it cannot be reused for wudu or ghusl.

You may have wondered whether water left over from wudu can be reused. The Hanafi school answers with a subtle but important distinction: the water is still pure and can be used for drinking or cooking, but it has lost its legal ability to remove ritual impurity. This lesson unpacks the ruling and the prophetic evidence behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act under discussion? Using used water for wudu. What is the ruling? It is not permissible (la yajuz) and the hukm level is haram in the Hanafi school.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites several hadith. Identify each: Jabir (Bukhari 194), al-Sa'ib (Bukhari 190), Ibn Abbas (Abu Dawud 137), and Abu Hurayrah (Muslim 283).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does each hadith prove the point? The Prophet pouring wudu water on Jabir shows it is not intended for another wudu. Drinking wudu water indicates it is not reserved for purification. The prohibition of bathing in stagnant water while junub implies that used water is not purifying.
The Ibn Abbas hadith is a demonstration of wudu, not directly about musta'mal but supports the overall context.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Shafi'is differ: they consider musta'mal water both pure and purifying, so it can be reused for wudu. The cross-madhhab status is mukhtalaf fih.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The mufta bihi is the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf that musta'mal is tahir but not mutahhir. It is the relied-upon view in the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا الْمَاءُ الْمُسْتَعْمَلُ فَلَا يَجُوزُ اسْتِعْمَالُهُ فِي طَهَارَةِ الْأَحْدَاثِ. عَنْ جَابِرٍ، قَالَ: جَاءَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ يَعُودُنِي، وَأَنَا مَرِيضٌ لَا أَعْقِلُ، فَتَوَضَّأَ وَصَبَّ عَلَيَّ مِنْ وَضُوئِهِ، فَعَقَلْتُ (بخاري بَابُ صَبِّ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَضُوءَهُ عَلَى الْمُغْمَى عَلَيْهِ، نمبر 194). وَعَنِ السَّائِبِ بْنِ يَزِيدَ، قَالَ: ذَهَبَتْ بِي خَالَتِي إِلَى النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فَقَالَتْ: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، إِنَّ ابْنَ أُخْتِي وَجِعٌ فَمَسَحَ رَأْسِي وَدَعَا لِي بِالْبَرَكَةِ، ثُمَّ تَوَضَّأَ فَشَرِبْتُ مِنْ وَضُوئِهِ (بخاري، بَابٌ، نمبر 190). وَقَالَ لَنَا ابْنُ عَبَّاسٍ: أَتُحِبُّونَ أَنْ أُرِيَكُمْ كَيْفَ كَانَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ يَتَوَضَّأُ؟ فَدَعَا بِإِنَاءٍ فِيهِ مَاءً فَاغْتَرَفَ غَرْفَةً بِيَدِهِ الْيُمْنَى فَتَمَضْمَضَ وَاسْتَنْشَقَ، ثُمَّ أَخَذَ أُخْرَى فَجَمَعَ بِمَا يَدَيْهِ، ثُمَّ غَسَلَ وَجْهَهُ (أَبُو دَاوُدَ، بَابُ الْوُضُوءِ مَرَّتَيْنِ، نمبر 137). وَعَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «لَا يَغْتَسِلْ أَحَدُكُمْ فِي الْمَاءِ الدَّائِمِ وَهُوَ جُنُبٌ» (مسلم، بَابُ النَّهْيِ عَنِ الْاغْتِسَالِ فِي الْمَاءِ الرَّاكِدِ، نمبر 283).
And as for used water, its use for purification from hadath is not permissible. From Jabir, he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) came to visit me while I was ill and unconscious, so he performed wudu and poured some of his wudu water over me, and I regained consciousness. (Bukhari, chapter: The Prophet pouring his wudu water over an unconscious person, no. 194). And from al-Sa'ib ibn Yazid, he said: My maternal aunt took me to the Prophet (peace be upon him) and said: 'O Messenger of Allah, my sister's son is sick.' So he wiped my head and prayed for blessing for me, then he performed wudu and I drank from his wudu water. (Bukhari, chapter, no. 190). And Ibn Abbas said to us: Do you want me to show you how the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) performed wudu? He called for a vessel containing water, scooped a handful with his right hand, rinsed his mouth and nose, then took another handful and combined with his two hands, then washed his face. (Abu Dawud, chapter: Wudu twice, no. 137). And from Abu Hurayrah, he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Let none of you bathe in stagnant water while he is junub.' (Muslim, chapter: Prohibition of bathing in stagnant water, no. 283).
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on used water (al-ma' al-musta'mal), which is water that has been used for wudu or ghusl. According to the Hanafi school, such water is considered pure (tahir) but not purifying (mutahhir); therefore it cannot be used again for removing hadath (ritual impurity). The author provides several hadith. The hadith of Jabir shows that the Prophet used his wudu water for another purpose (pouring on Jabir), indicating that water used for wudu is not suitable for another wudu. The hadith of al-Sa'ib shows the Prophet's wudu water being drunk, again implying it is not used for purification. The hadith of Ibn Abbas describing the Prophetic wudu is a demonstration. The hadith of Abu Hurayrah prohibits bathing in stagnant water while junub, which implies that water used for ghusl should not be reused. These hadith collectively support the Hanafi view that musta'mal water is legally pure but cannot be used for wudu or ghusl. Note: Hanafis consider musta'mal water to be tahir (pure) but not mutahhir (purifying).

Key Terms
الْمَاءُ الْمُسْتَعْمَلُ (al-ma' al-musta'mal): Water that has been used for wudu or ghusl, i.e., water that has touched a limb in purification from hadath.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is permissible because the water is still pure.
B) It is not permissible because the water is impure.
C) It is not permissible because the water is pure but not purifying.
D) It is permissible only if the water is abundant.

Key Takeaway
Musta'mal water is tahir (pure) but not mutahhir (purifying); it cannot be used for wudu or ghusl.

Definition and Ruling of Used Water
Definition and ruling of used water

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of used water (mā' musta'mal) and identify its ruling according to the Hanafi school (tahir but not mutahhir).

Core Idea
Used water is pure but cannot purify — it lacks the quality of mutahhir.

This lesson presents the foundational Hanafi definition and ruling of used water from the matn of Al-Quduri. Understanding this concept is crucial because it determines which waters are valid for wudu, ghusl, and other acts of purification. The principle stated here is that a water must be both tahir (pure) and mutahhir (purifying) to be suitable for purification; used water only has the first quality.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition
Read the matn carefully. It defines used water as water that has been used either to remove an impurity (hadath) or on the body for a worship act (qurbah) like wudu or ghusl.
2
Classify the ruling
The text and commentary state that used water is tahir (pure) but not mutahhir (purifying). This is the central ruling.
3
Apply the principle
The Urdu asl (principle) explains that for water to be useful for purification, it must be both tahir and mutahhir. Used water fails the second condition.
4
Recall the consequence
Because used water is not mutahhir, it cannot be used for wudu, ghusl, or any other act of purification. If used, the purification is invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ا وَالْمُسْتَعْمَلُ كُلُّ مَاءٍ أُزِيلَ بِهِ حَدَتْ أَوْ اسْتُعْمِلَ فِي الْبَدَنِ عَلَى وَجْهِ الْقُرْبَةِ.

اصول: پاکی کے لئے پانی کا طاہر اور مطہر دونوں ہو نا ضروری ہے، اور ماء مستعمل طاہر تو ہے مطہر نہیں ہے۔
And the used water is every water that removes an impurity or is used on the body for the purpose of worship.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This is the matn of Al-Quduri defining used water (الماء المستعمل). It is water that has been used either to physically remove an impurity (hadath) or in an act of worship (qurbah) such as wudu or ghusl. The ruling is that it is tahir (pure) but not mutahhir (purifying). The Urdu principle explains that for water to be suitable for purification, it must be both inherently pure and capable of purifying others; used water lacks the latter quality. This is the Hanafi position.

Key Terms
الماء المستعمل (al-mā' al-musta'mal): Water that has been used to remove an impurity or used for an act of worship (wudu/ghusl).
طاهر (tāhir): Pure in itself; not impure (najis).
مطهر (muṭahhir): Capable of purifying other things, i.e., can be used for wudu/ghusl to remove hadath or najasah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is pure and purifying.
B) It is impure.
C) It is pure but not purifying.
D) It is impure but becomes pure after being left out.

Key Takeaway
Used water is pure but cannot be used for purification because it is tahir, not mutahhir.

Ruling on Tanning, Hair and Bones of Dead Animals
States ruling on tanned hides and purity of hair and bones with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the purity of tanned hides and of hair and bones of dead animals, and cite the primary evidence.

Core Idea
Tanning purifies the hide of any dead animal except pig and human; hair and bones are pure even without tanning.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on the purification of animal hides through tanning and the inherent purity of hair and bones from dead animals. These rulings are based on explicit hadith and Quranic evidence, with important exceptions for pig and human skin. Understanding these distinctions is essential for determining the validity of salah and wudu using these materials.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
The matn first states that every tanned hide becomes pure and permissible for prayer and wudu, then states that hair and bones of dead animals are pure. Note the two separate rulings.
The first ruling has exceptions; the second ruling is unconditional.
2
Note the exceptions
The matn explicitly excludes the skin of a pig and of a human from the purifying effect of tanning. Why are these excluded? Because they are najis al-ayn (inherently impure) and cannot be purified by any method.
Other schools may also exclude dog, but Hanafi only excludes pig and human.
3
Examine the primary hadith for tanning
The text cites the hadith 'Any hide that is tanned, it has become pure' (أَيُّمَا إِهَابِ دُبَغَ فَقَدْ طَهُرَ). This is a general statement covering all hides. The Hanafi school uses its generality to include all animals except those excluded by other evidence.
The hadith is narrated by Ibn Abbas and Aisha, and is ahad but accepted.
4
Examine the Quranic verse as supporting evidence
The verse 6:145 mentions that carrion, blood, and pig flesh are impure. By implication, pig skin is included in the prohibition, hence excluded from the general ruling of purification by tanning.
The verse does not mention hides, but the Hanafi school uses it to argue that pig skin remains impure.
5
Examine the evidence for hair and bones
The text presents several proofs: the hadith from Thawban about buying a necklace of sinew and bangles of ivory (showing use of bone/ivory from dead animals), and the narration from Abdullah ibn Ukaym prohibiting benefit from hide and sinew. The Hanafi school reconciles these by holding that the prohibition applies only to hides (which require tanning) and sinew (which is like hide), but hair and bones are inherently pure.
The last proof from Umm Salamah is incomplete in the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ا وَكُلُّ إِهَابٍ ذُبِغَ فَقَدْ طَهُرَ وَجَازَتْ الصَّلَاةُ عَلَيْهِ وَالْوُضُوءُ مِنْهُ إِلَّا جِلْدَ الْخِنْزِيرِ وَالْآدَمِي. وَشَعْرُ الْمَيْتَةِ وَعَظْمُهَا طَاهِرَانِ.

وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَكُلُّ إهَابِ دُبغَ فَقَدْ طَهُرَ \ عَنْ ابْن عَبَّاس قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ الله صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «أَيُّمَا إِهَابِ دُبَغَ فَقَدْ طَهُرَ» (سنن النسائي، جُلُودُ الميتة، نمبر 4241/ (مسلم بَابُ طَهَارَة جُلُود الميتة بالدباغ، نمبر 366)

وجه : (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَكُلُّ إِهَابِ دُبغَ فَقَدْ طَهُرَ \ عَنْ عَائِشَةَ، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «فَكَاةُ الْمَيْتَة دبَاغُهَا » السنن النسائي، جُلُودُ الْميتة، نمبر 4246)

لوجه: (1) الآية لثبوت كُل إهَابٍ دُبغَ فَقَدْ طَهُرَ إلَّا جِلْدَ الْخُنْزيرِ والا دَمِي إِلَّا أَن يَكُونَ مَيْتَةً أَوْ دَمَا مَّسْفُوحًا أَوْ لَحْمَ خِنزِيرٍ فَإِنَّهُ رِجْسٌ أَوْ فِسْقًا أُهِلَّ لِغَيْرِ اللَّهِ بِهِ(سورة الانعام 6، الآية 145)

وجه (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَشَعْرُ الْمَيْتَةِ وَعَظْمُهَا طَاهِرَانِ \ وَقَالَ: «يَا ثَوْبَانُ اذْهَبْ بِهَذَا إِلَى آلِ فُلَانٍ - أَهْلِ بَيْتِ بِالْمَدِينَةِ - إِنَّ هَؤُلَاءِ أَهْلِ بَيْتي أَكْرَهُ أَنْ يَأْكُلُوا طَيِّبَاتِهِمْ فِي حَيَاتِهِمُ الدُّنْيَا، يَا ثَوْبَانُ اشْتَرِ لِفَاطِمَةَ قِلَادَةً مِنْ عَصَبِ، وَسِوَارَيْنِ مِنْ عَاجِ ابو داؤد، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي الِانْتِفَاعِ بالعاج، نمبر 4213)

وجه (۲) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَشَعْرُ الْمَيْتَةِ وَعَظْمُهَا طَاهِرَانِ أَعَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عُكَيْمٍ، قَالَ: قُرئَ عَلَيْنَا كِتَابُ رَسُول الله صَلّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ بأَرض جُهَيْنَةَ وَأَنَا غُلَامٌ شَابٌ: «أَنْ لَا تَسْتَمْتِعُوا مِنَ الْمَيْتَةِ بِاهَاب وَلَاَ عَصَب سنن ابي داؤد ، بَابُ مَنْ رَوَى أَنْ لَا يَنْتَفِعَ بِإِهَابِ الميتة،نمبر 4127/ سنن النسائى ، مَا يُدبَعُ به جُلُودُ الْميتة، نمبر 4251)

وجه (۳) الحديث لثبوت وَشَعْرُ الْمَيْتَةِ وَعَظْمُهَا طَاهِرَانِ أَنْ لَا تَسْتَمْتَعُوا مِنَ الْمَيْتَةِ بِاهَابٍ، وَلَا عصب» (سنن ابي داؤد ، باب من روى أَنْ لا ينتفع باهَابِ الْمَيِّتة، نمبر 4127)

النبي

وجه : (۴) الحديث لثبوت وَشَعْرُ الْمَيْتَةِ وَعَظْمُهَا طَاهِرَانِ اسَمِعْتُ أُمِّ سَلَمَةَ زَوْجَ [؟]

اصول: جانور کی کھال دباغت سے پاک ہو جاتی ہے، لیکن نجس العین جانور و انسان کی کھال قابل انتفاع نہیں۔
And every hide that is tanned, it has become pure, and prayer upon it and wudu from it are permissible, except the skin of a pig and of a human. And the hair of a dead animal and its bone are pure.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This is a detailed ruling from Al-Quduri with proofs. The matn establishes that tanning (dibagh) purifies the hide of any dead animal, making it permissible for use in prayer and wudu. Two exceptions are stated: pig skin and human skin. Additionally, the hair and bones of a dead animal are declared pure (tahir) without requiring tanning. The text then provides multiple pieces of evidence: a hadith from Ibn Abbas and another from Aisha that tanning purifies; a Quranic verse (6:145) that implicitly exempts pig skin; hadith about Thawban regarding use of hair and bones; a narration from Abdullah ibn Ukaym prohibiting use of hide and sinew; and an incomplete hadith from Umm Salamah. The Urdu principle reaffirms that tanning purifies the hide, but the skin of a pig and human cannot be utilized.

Key Terms
إِهَاب (ihāb): The skin of an animal that has not been tanned; usually refers to the hide of a dead animal.
دِبَاغ (dibāgh): The process of tanning that removes moisture and impurities from a hide, making it pure for use.
شَعْرُ الْمَيْتَةِ (sha‘r al-maytah): The hair of a dead animal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is NOT purified by tanning?
A) The hide of a cow that died naturally.
B) The hide of a pig.
C) The hide of a sheep that died.
D) The hide of a goat.

Key Takeaway
Tanning purifies hides of dead animals except pig and human; hair and bones are inherently pure in the Hanafi school.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
Purifying a Well When an Animal Dies: Hanafi Ruling and Evidence
Hanafi ruling on well purification with prescribed bucket amounts and evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on purifying a well after an animal dies, specify the required number of buckets for small and medium animals, and explain the proof from the actions of Ibn al-Zubayr and Imam Ali.

Core Idea
Removing contaminated water in prescribed amounts purifies a well — necessity (darurah) permits this method.

What happens when a mouse or a chicken falls into your well? Is the water still pure? The Hanafi school gives a clear ruling: the well becomes impure, but it can be purified by removing a specific number of buckets of water. This lesson presents the ruling, the animals categorized by size, and the proofs from the practice of the Companions, showing how the school derives its guidance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal act and its ruling
Recognize that the act is purifying a well (bi'r) after an impurity (najasah) – specifically a dead animal – falls into it. The ruling is that removal (nazh) of water is obligatory (wajib).
2
Note the categories of animals and bucket counts
The text classifies animals into two groups: small (mouse, sparrow, etc.) requiring 20–30 buckets, and medium (pigeon, chicken, cat) requiring 40–60 buckets. This is a standard, not an arbitrary figure.
3
Examine the primary proof: action of Ibn al-Zubayr
The passage cites the precedent of Ibn al-Zubayr ordering the removal of water from Zamzam after a person died in it. This shows the principle of emptying the well to purify it.
This is a qawl sahabi – the statement/action of a Companion – which is a source of law in Hanafi usul.
4
Consider additional proofs from Ali and Sha'bi
The narration from Ali (remove until water overpowers) and from Sha'bi (40 buckets for birds/cats) provide further support for the prescribed numbers.
5
Acknowledge differences within and outside the school
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad differed slightly on exact numbers, and the Shafi'i school uses different thresholds. The mufta bihi position is the numbers given in the matn.

Source Text

وَإِذَا وَقَعَ فِي الْبِئْرِ نَجَاسَةٌ نُزِحَتْ وَكَانَ نَنْحُ مَا فِيهَا مِنْ الْمَاءِ طَهَارَةً لَهَا فَإِنْ مَاتَتْ فِيهَا فَأَرَةٌ أَوْ عُصْفُورٌ أَوْ صَعْوَةٌ أَوْ سُودَانِيَّةٌ إِلَى آخِرِهِ أَوْ سَامٌ أَبْرَصُ نُرِحَ مِنْهَا مَا بَيْنَ عِشْرِينَ دَلْوَا إِلَى ثَلَاثِينَ بِحَسَبِ كُبْرِ الْحَيَوَانِ وَصِغَرِهِ إِلَى آخِرِهِ .

وَإِنْ مَاتَتْ فِيهَا حَمَامَةٌ أَوْ دَجَاجَةٌ أَوْ سِتَّوْرٌ تُرحَ مِنْهَا مَا بَيْنَ أَرْبَعِينَ دَلُّو إِلَى سِتِّينَ .

صَلّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ, تَقُولُ: سَمِعْتُ رَسُولَ الله صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ يَقُولُ: «لَا بَأْسَ بمسك الْمَيْتَةِ إِذَا دُبعَ, وَلَا بَأسَ بِصُوفَهَا وَشَعْرهَا وَقُرُونهَا إذَا غُسِلَ بِالْمَاءِ». (سنن الدار قطني، باب الدباغ، نمبر 116/السنن الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ الْمَنْعِ مِنَ الانْتِفَاعِ بِشَعْرِ الميتة، نمبر 83)

وجه : (۱) قول التابعي لثبوت وَإِذَا وَقَعَ فِي الْبِئْرِ نَجَاسَةٌ نُزِحَتْ \ عَنْ عَطَاءٍ، أَنَّ حَبَشِيًّا، وَقَعَ فِي زَمْزَمَ فَمَاتَ ، قَالَ : فَأَمَرَ ابْنُ الزُّبَيْرِ أَنْ يُنْزَفَ مَاءُ زَمْزَمَ قَالَ : فَجَعَلَ الْمَاءُ لَا يَنْقَطِعُ قَالَ: فَنَظَرُوا فَإِذَا عَيْنٌ تَنْبُعُ مِنْ قِبَلِ الْحَجَرِ الْأَسْوَدِ قَالَ: فَقَالَ ابْنُ الزُّبَيْرِ : حَسْبُكُمْ (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، في الْفَأْرَةِ وَالدَّجَاجَةِ وَأَشْبَاهِهِمَا تَقَعُ فِي الْبِثْرِ، نمبر 1713)

لوجه: (ا)قول الصحابي لثبوت فَإِنْ مَاتَتْ فِيهَا فَأَرَةٌ أَوْ عُصْفُورٌ أَوْ صَعْوَةٌ نُرِحَ مِنْهَا \ عَنْ عَلِيَّ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ قَالَ: «إِذَا سَقَطَتِ الْفَأْرَةُ أَوِ الدَّابَّةُ فِي الْبِئْرِ، فَانْزَحْهَا حَتَّى يَغْلِبَكَ الْمَاءُ» شرح معاني الاثار ، بَابُ الْمَاءِ يَقَعُ فِيهِ النَّجَاسَةُ ، غبر 34/ مصنف عبدالرزاق، بَابُ الْبِثْرِ تَقَعُ فِيهِ الدَّابَّةُ، 271/ مصنف ابن شيبه، فِي الْفَأْرَةِ وَالدَّجَاجَةِ وَأَشْبَاهِهِمَا تَقَعُ فِي الْبِثْرِ، 1711)

وجه: (ا)قول التابعي لثبوت وَإِنْ مَاتَتْ فِيهَا حَمَامَةٌ أَوْ دَجَاجَةٌ أَوْ سِنَّوْرٌ نُرِحَ مِنْهَا \ عَنِ الشَّعْبِيِّ فِي الطَّيْرِ وَالسَّنَّوْرِ وَنَحْوِهِمَا يَقَعُ فِي الْبِئْرِ، قَالَ: «يُنْزَحُ مِنْهَا أَرْبَعُونَ دَلْوَا» (شرح معاني الاثار، بَابُ الْمَاءِ يَقَعُ فِيهِ النَّجَاسَةُ، نمبر 37 مصنف عبدالرزاق، بَابُ الْبِثْرِ تَقَعُ فِيهِ الدابَّةُ ، نمبر 272/ مصنف ابن ابي شيبه فِي الْفَأَرَةِ وَالدَّجَاجَةِ وَأَشْبَاهِهِمَا تَقَعُ فِي الْبِتْرِ، نمبر 1713)

اصول : کنواں میں ناپا کی گر جائے تو کنواں ناپاک ہو جاتا ہے، لیکن اس کے پانی کو نکال دے تو کنواں کا پانی، اس کی دیوار ، اور رسی ڈول سب پاک شمار کیا جائے گا، کیونکہ اس میں ضرورت ہے۔

لغت : فَأَرَةٌ: چوہا۔ عُصْفُورَةٌ : چڑیا- صَعْوَةٌ : ممولا، سُودَانِيَّةٌ : بھیجنا۔ سَامٌ أَبْرَصُ : چھپکلی۔
And when an impurity falls into a well, it is removed, and whatever water is in it becomes a purification for it. Then if a mouse, sparrow, ṣaʿwah, sudāniyyah, or a gecko dies in it, between twenty and thirty buckets are removed depending on the size of the animal. And if a pigeon, chicken, or cat dies in it, between forty and sixty buckets are removed.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage details the Hanafi method of purifying a well (bi'r) after an impurity, specifically a dead animal, falls into it. The ruling: the water must be removed (nazh) from the well. The number of buckets (dalw) to be removed depends on the size of the animal. Small creatures (mouse, sparrow, etc.) require 20–30 buckets; medium animals (pigeon, chicken, cat) require 40–60 buckets. The text then cites as evidence: a narration from Ibn al-Zubayr regarding a dead Ethiopian in Zamzam, a report from Ali saying 'remove until the water overpowers you', and a statement from al-Sha'bi prescribing forty buckets for birds and cats. The Urdu principle explains the rationale: the well becomes impure, but removing the water purifies the water, walls, rope, and bucket due to necessity. Vocabulary is provided for the animal names.

Key Terms
الْبِئْر (al-bi'r): A well; a water source dug into the ground.
نُزِحَتْ / نَرح (nuzihat / narah): To remove water from a well using a bucket; the action of purification by extracting water.
دَلْو (dalw): A bucket used for drawing water from a well; the unit of measurement for the amount to be removed.
فَأَرَة (fa'ra): Mouse; a small rodent.
دَجَاجَة (dajaja): Chicken; a medium-sized bird.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how many buckets of water must be removed from a well if a chicken dies in it?
A) 10–20
B) 20–30
C) 30–40
D) 40–60

Key Takeaway
Removing a prescribed number of buckets of water – 20–30 for small animals, 40–60 for medium animals – is obligatory to purify a well after a dead animal falls in.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
10 min
Purifying a Well from Impurities (Najasah)
Stating Hanafi rulings on purifying wells with graded bucket removals and the unknown time case.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the graded bucket removal requirements for different animals in a well and apply the rule for when the animal is found without known time.

Core Idea
The purification of a well is graded by the size of the animal and whether it decomposed; a dead animal found later requires repeating past prayers.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi rulings on purifying a well contaminated by najasah. The central principle is that the water itself is purified by removal, but the quantity required depends on what fell into it. We will explore the graded scale from small to large animals, the use of a medium bucket as a standard, and the special case when a dead animal is found without known time. Al-Quduri presents these rules along with proofs from athar and hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the source of impurity
Determine what fell into the well: a mouse, a hen, a dog, etc. The size and condition (decomposed or not) dictate the removal requirement.
Small animals include mouse, sparrow, gecko; medium include pigeon, hen, cat; large include dog, sheep, human.
2
Apply the bucket count rule
For small: 20-30 medium buckets; medium: 40-60; large: all water. Use a medium bucket as standard; larger buckets can be counted if equivalent.
The medium bucket (dalw al-wasat) is the unit of measure.
3
Check for decomposition
If the animal has swelled or decomposed, the well must be completely emptied regardless of its size.
Decomposition overrides the size-based grading.
4
Handle the case of a spring well
If the well is a natural spring that cannot be fully drained, remove an amount equivalent to its total water volume.
Continuous drawing is used to meet the requirement.
5
Apply the unknown time rule
If a dead animal is found without knowing when it fell and without decomposition, Abu Hanifa requires repeating all prayers performed with that water within a day and night, and washing everything touched. The Sahibayn hold no repetition is needed until the time is known.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; the mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view.
