وَإِذَا وَقَعَ فِي الْبِئْرِ نَجَاسَةٌ نُزِحَتْ وَكَانَ نَزْحُ مَا فِيهَا مِنَ الْمَاءِ طَهَارَةً لَهَا فَإِنْ مَاتَتْ فِيهَا فَأْرَةٌ أَوْ عُصْفُورٌ أَوْ صَعْوَةٌ أَوْ سُودَانِيَّةٌ أَوْ سَامُّ أَبْرَصَ نُزِحَ مِنْهَا مَا بَيْنَ عِشْرِينَ دَلْوًا إِلَى ثَلَاثِينَ بِحَسَبِ كِبَرِ الْحَيَوَانِ وَصِغَرِهِ . وَإِنْ مَاتَتْ فِيهَا حَمَامَةٌ أَوْ دَجَاجَةٌ أَوْ سِنَّوْرٌ نُزِحَ مِنْهَا مَا بَيْنَ أَرْبَعِينَ دَلْوًا إِلَى سِتِّينَ . فَإِنْ مَاتَ فِيهَا كَلْبٌ أَوْ شَاةٌ أَوْ آدَمِيٌّ نُزِحَ جَمِيعُ مَائِهَا . وَعَدَدُ الدِّلَاءِ يُعْتَبَرُ بِدَلْوِ الْوَسَطِ الْمُسْتَعْمَلِ لِلْآبَارِ فَإِنْ نُزِحَ مِنْهَا بِدَلْوٍ عَظِيمٍ قَدْرُ مَا يَسَعُ مِنَ الدَّلْوِ الْوَسَطِ وَاحْتُسِبَ بِهِ جَازَ . وَإِنِ انْتَفَخَ الْحَيَوَانُ فِيهَا أَوْ تَفَسَّخَ نُزِحَ جَمِيعُ مَائِهَا صَغِيرًا كَانَ الْحَيَوَانُ أَوْ كَبِيرًا . وَإِنْ كَانَتِ الْبِئْرُ مَعِينًا لَا تُنْزَحُ وَقَدْ وَجَبَ نَزْحُ مَا فِيهَا أَخْرَجُوا مِقْدَارَ مَا كَانَ فِيهَا مِنَ الْمَاءِ . وَإِذَا وُجِدَ فِي الْبِئْرِ فَأْرَةٌ مَيْتَةٌ أَوْ غَيْرُهَا وَلَا يَدْرُونَ مَتَى وَقَعَتْ وَلَمْ تَنْفَحْ وَلَمْ تَتَنَفَّسْ أَعَادُوا صَلَاةَ يَوْمٍ وَلَيْلَةٍ إِذَا كَانُوا تَوَضَّئُوا مِنْهَا وَغَسَلُوا كُلَّ شَيْءٍ أَصَابَهُ مَاؤُهَا . وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ لَيْسَ عَلَيْهِمْ إِعَادَةُ شَيْءٍ حَتَّى يَتَحَقَّقُوا مَتَى وَقَعَتْ . وَسُؤْرُ الْآدَمِيِّ وَمَا يُؤْكَلُ لَحْمُهُ طَاهِرٌ . وَجْهٌ : (1) قَوْلُ التَّابِعِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ حُكْمِ الْفَأْرَةِ وَغَيْرِهَا : عَنْ عَطَاءٍ أَنَّ حَبَشِيًّا وَقَعَ فِي زَمْزَمَ فَمَاتَ فَأَمَرَ ابْنُ الزُّبَيْرِ أَنْ يُنْزَفَ مَاءُ زَمْزَمَ فَجَعَلَ الْمَاءُ لَا يَنْقَطِعُ فَنَظَرُوا فَإِذَا عَيْنٌ تَنْبُعُ مِنْ قِبَلِ الْحَجَرِ الْأَسْوَدِ فَقَالَ ابْنُ الزُّبَيْرِ : حَسْبُكُمْ . (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة) وَوَجْهٌ : (2) قَوْلُ الصَّحَابِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ حُكْمِ الْفَأْرَةِ وَغَيْرِهَا : عَنْ عَلِيٍّ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ قَالَ : إِذَا سَقَطَتِ الْفَأْرَةُ أَوِ الدَّابَّةُ فِي الْبِئْرِ فَانْزَحْهَا حَتَّى يَغْلِبَكَ الْمَاءُ . (شرح معاني الآثار) وَوَجْهٌ : (3) قَوْلُ التَّابِعِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ حُكْمِ الْحَمَامَةِ وَالدَّجَاجَةِ وَالسِّنَّوْرِ : عَنِ الشَّعْبِيِّ فِي الطَّيْرِ وَالسِّنَّوْرِ وَنَحْوِهِمَا يَقَعُ فِي الْبِئْرِ قَالَ : يُنْزَحُ مِنْهَا أَرْبَعُونَ دَلْوًا . (شرح معاني الآثار) وَوَجْهٌ : (4) قَوْلُ التَّابِعِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ حُكْمِ الْكَلْبِ وَغَيْرِهِ : عَنْ عَطَاءٍ قَالَ : إِذَا سَقَطَ الْكَلْبُ فِي الْبِئْرِ فَأُخْرِجَ حِينَ سَقَطَ نُزِعَ مِنْهَا عِشْرُونَ دَلْوًا فَإِنْ أُخْرِجَ حِينَ مَاتَ نُزِعَ مِنْهَا سِتُّونَ أَوْ سَبْعُونَ دَلْوًا فَإِنْ تَفَسَّخَ نُزِعَ مَاؤُهَا فَإِنْ لَمْ يَسْتَطِيعُوا نُزِعَ مِنْهَا مِائَتَا دَلْوٍ وَعِشْرُونَ وَمِائَةٌ . (مصنف عبد الرزاق) وَوَجْهٌ : (5) الْآيَةُ لِاعْتِبَارِ الدَّلْوِ الْوَسَطِ : ﴿فَكَفَّارَتُهُ إِطْعَامُ عَشَرَةِ مَسَاكِينَ مِنْ أَوْسَطِ مَا تُطْعِمُونَ أَهْلِيكُمْ﴾ (المائدة: 89) وَوَجْهٌ : (6) قَوْلُ الصَّحَابِيِّ لِلْبِئْرِ الْمَعِينِ : قِصَّةُ زَمْزَمَ مَعَ ابْنِ الزُّبَيْرِ . (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة) وَوَجْهٌ : (7) الْحَدِيثُ لِطَهَارَةِ سُؤْرِ الْآدَمِيِّ : عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ : دَخَلْتُ مَعَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ أَنَا وَخَالِدُ بْنُ الْوَلِيدِ عَلَى مَيْمُونَةَ فَجَاءَتْنَا بِإِنَاءٍ مِنْ لَبَنٍ . (سنن الدارقطني)
And if an impurity falls into the well, it is removed (by drawing water), and the removal of what is in it of water is purification for it. If a mouse, sparrow, wagtail, sudaniyya (black bird), or gecko dies in it, between twenty to thirty buckets are removed according to the size of the animal. If a pigeon, hen, or cat dies in it, between forty to sixty buckets are removed. If a dog, sheep, or human dies in it, all its water is removed. The number of buckets is considered by the medium-sized bucket used for wells; if water is removed with a large bucket that holds the equivalent of a medium bucket and is counted accordingly, it is permissible. If the animal swells or decomposes in it, all its water is removed, whether the animal is small or large. If the well is a natural spring that cannot be drained, and it is obligatory to remove what is in it, they remove an amount equivalent to what was in it of water. If a dead mouse or other animal is found in the well and they do not know when it fell, and it has not swelled nor decomposed, they repeat the prayers of a day and night if they performed wudu from it, and they wash everything that its water touched. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: They do not have to repeat anything until they ascertain when it fell. The leftover water (su'r) of a human and that whose meat is eaten is pure.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage from Al-Quduri presents the Hanafi rulings on purification of wells contaminated by najasah (impurity). It is a ruling-with-proof passage, where the matn states graded obligations depending on the animal that died in the well, and the commentary provides proofs from hadith and athar. The key principle: removal of water purifies the well, but the required quantity varies. For small animals like mice and birds, 20-30 medium buckets suffice. For medium animals like cats and chickens, 40-60 buckets. For large animals like dogs, sheep, or humans, the entire well must be emptied. If the animal decomposes, full removal is required regardless of size. If the well is a spring that cannot be fully drained, they must remove an amount equal to its total water volume (e.g., by continuous drawing). A special case: if a dead animal is found without knowledge of when it fell and no decomposition, Abu Hanifa requires repetition of all prayers performed with that water within a day and night, and washing anything touched. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that nothing is repeated until the time is known, following the principle of certainty. Finally, su'r (leftover water) of humans and halal-meat animals (e.g., sheep, cows, chickens) is pure, based on the hadith of Ibn Abbas.

Key Terms
فَأْرَةٌ (fa'ra): A mouse or rat; one of the small animals whose death in a well requires 20-30 buckets.
دَلْو (dalw): A bucket used for drawing water; the standard measure for purification is the medium-sized bucket (dalw al-wasat).
نَزْح (nazh): Removal of water from a well for purification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Al-Quduri, how many buckets should be removed if a chicken dies in a well?
A) 20-30 buckets
B) 40-60 buckets
C) All water
D) 10-20 buckets

Key Takeaway
Well purification in the Hanafi madhab is graded: small animals need 20-30 buckets, medium 40-60, large all water; decomposition requires full removal; unknown time requires repeating one day and night's prayers (Abu Hanifa).

Taharah — Purification
beginner
5 min
Ruling on Leftover Water (Su'r)
Stating the Hanafi ruling on the purity of leftover water (su'r).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that the leftover water (su'r) of a human and halal-meat animals is pure, and identify the hadith proof.

Core Idea
The leftover water of a human and halal-meat animals is pure (tahir).

In this short lesson, we examine the ruling on su'r, the water left after drinking. The Hanafi position is straightforward: the su'r of a human and any animal whose meat is halal to eat is pure. The proof is a hadith from Ibn Abbas. This ruling is important for daily wudu and drinking water from shared vessels.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject: su'r
Su'r refers to the water left in a vessel after a person or animal has drunk from it.
The ruling applies to the leftover water, not the animal's saliva directly.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The su'r of a human and any halal-meat animal is tahir (pure).
This includes the su'r of permissible birds and livestock.
3
Identify the proof
The hadith of Ibn Abbas: he, Khalid, and the Prophet entered Maimuna's house and were given a vessel of milk. The Prophet drank and gave it to Ibn Abbas.
This shows the Prophet's leftover drink was consumed by Ibn Abbas, indicating purity.

وَإِذَا وَقَعَ فِي الْبِئْرِ نَجَاسَةٌ نُزِحَتْ وَكَانَ نَزْحُ مَا فِيهَا مِنَ الْمَاءِ طَهَارَةً لَهَا فَإِنْ مَاتَتْ فِيهَا فَأْرَةٌ أَوْ عُصْفُورٌ أَوْ صَعْوَةٌ أَوْ سُودَانِيَّةٌ أَوْ سَامُّ أَبْرَصَ نُزِحَ مِنْهَا مَا بَيْنَ عِشْرِينَ دَلْوًا إِلَى ثَلَاثِينَ بِحَسَبِ كِبَرِ الْحَيَوَانِ وَصِغَرِهِ . وَإِنْ مَاتَتْ فِيهَا حَمَامَةٌ أَوْ دَجَاجَةٌ أَوْ سِنَّوْرٌ نُزِحَ مِنْهَا مَا بَيْنَ أَرْبَعِينَ دَلْوًا إِلَى سِتِّينَ . فَإِنْ مَاتَ فِيهَا كَلْبٌ أَوْ شَاةٌ أَوْ آدَمِيٌّ نُزِحَ جَمِيعُ مَائِهَا . وَعَدَدُ الدِّلَاءِ يُعْتَبَرُ بِدَلْوِ الْوَسَطِ الْمُسْتَعْمَلِ لِلْآبَارِ فَإِنْ نُزِحَ مِنْهَا بِدَلْوٍ عَظِيمٍ قَدْرُ مَا يَسَعُ مِنَ الدَّلْوِ الْوَسَطِ وَاحْتُسِبَ بِهِ جَازَ . وَإِنِ انْتَفَخَ الْحَيَوَانُ فِيهَا أَوْ تَفَسَّخَ نُزِحَ جَمِيعُ مَائِهَا صَغِيرًا كَانَ الْحَيَوَانُ أَوْ كَبِيرًا . وَإِنْ كَانَتِ الْبِئْرُ مَعِينًا لَا تُنْزَحُ وَقَدْ وَجَبَ نَزْحُ مَا فِيهَا أَخْرَجُوا مِقْدَارَ مَا كَانَ فِيهَا مِنَ الْمَاءِ . وَإِذَا وُجِدَ فِي الْبِئْرِ فَأْرَةٌ مَيْتَةٌ أَوْ غَيْرُهَا وَلَا يَدْرُونَ مَتَى وَقَعَتْ وَلَمْ تَنْفَحْ وَلَمْ تَتَنَفَّسْ أَعَادُوا صَلَاةَ يَوْمٍ وَلَيْلَةٍ إِذَا كَانُوا تَوَضَّئُوا مِنْهَا وَغَسَلُوا كُلَّ شَيْءٍ أَصَابَهُ مَاؤُهَا . وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ لَيْسَ عَلَيْهِمْ إِعَادَةُ شَيْءٍ حَتَّى يَتَحَقَّقُوا مَتَى وَقَعَتْ . وَسُؤْرُ الْآدَمِيِّ وَمَا يُؤْكَلُ لَحْمُهُ طَاهِرٌ . وَجْهٌ : (1) قَوْلُ التَّابِعِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ حُكْمِ الْفَأْرَةِ وَغَيْرِهَا : عَنْ عَطَاءٍ أَنَّ حَبَشِيًّا وَقَعَ فِي زَمْزَمَ فَمَاتَ فَأَمَرَ ابْنُ الزُّبَيْرِ أَنْ يُنْزَفَ مَاءُ زَمْزَمَ فَجَعَلَ الْمَاءُ لَا يَنْقَطِعُ فَنَظَرُوا فَإِذَا عَيْنٌ تَنْبُعُ مِنْ قِبَلِ الْحَجَرِ الْأَسْوَدِ فَقَالَ ابْنُ الزُّبَيْرِ : حَسْبُكُمْ . (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة) وَوَجْهٌ : (2) قَوْلُ الصَّحَابِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ حُكْمِ الْفَأْرَةِ وَغَيْرِهَا : عَنْ عَلِيٍّ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ قَالَ : إِذَا سَقَطَتِ الْفَأْرَةُ أَوِ الدَّابَّةُ فِي الْبِئْرِ فَانْزَحْهَا حَتَّى يَغْلِبَكَ الْمَاءُ . (شرح معاني الآثار) وَوَجْهٌ : (3) قَوْلُ التَّابِعِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ حُكْمِ الْحَمَامَةِ وَالدَّجَاجَةِ وَالسِّنَّوْرِ : عَنِ الشَّعْبِيِّ فِي الطَّيْرِ وَالسِّنَّوْرِ وَنَحْوِهِمَا يَقَعُ فِي الْبِئْرِ قَالَ : يُنْزَحُ مِنْهَا أَرْبَعُونَ دَلْوًا . (شرح معاني الآثار) وَوَجْهٌ : (4) قَوْلُ التَّابِعِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ حُكْمِ الْكَلْبِ وَغَيْرِهِ : عَنْ عَطَاءٍ قَالَ : إِذَا سَقَطَ الْكَلْبُ فِي الْبِئْرِ فَأُخْرِجَ حِينَ سَقَطَ نُزِعَ مِنْهَا عِشْرُونَ دَلْوًا فَإِنْ أُخْرِجَ حِينَ مَاتَ نُزِعَ مِنْهَا سِتُّونَ أَوْ سَبْعُونَ دَلْوًا فَإِنْ تَفَسَّخَ نُزِعَ مَاؤُهَا فَإِنْ لَمْ يَسْتَطِيعُوا نُزِعَ مِنْهَا مِائَتَا دَلْوٍ وَعِشْرُونَ وَمِائَةٌ . (مصنف عبد الرزاق) وَوَجْهٌ : (5) الْآيَةُ لِاعْتِبَارِ الدَّلْوِ الْوَسَطِ : ﴿فَكَفَّارَتُهُ إِطْعَامُ عَشَرَةِ مَسَاكِينَ مِنْ أَوْسَطِ مَا تُطْعِمُونَ أَهْلِيكُمْ﴾ (المائدة: 89) وَوَجْهٌ : (6) قَوْلُ الصَّحَابِيِّ لِلْبِئْرِ الْمَعِينِ : قِصَّةُ زَمْزَمَ مَعَ ابْنِ الزُّبَيْرِ . (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة) وَوَجْهٌ : (7) الْحَدِيثُ لِطَهَارَةِ سُؤْرِ الْآدَمِيِّ : عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ : دَخَلْتُ مَعَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ أَنَا وَخَالِدُ بْنُ الْوَلِيدِ عَلَى مَيْمُونَةَ فَجَاءَتْنَا بِإِنَاءٍ مِنْ لَبَنٍ . (سنن الدارقطني)
And if an impurity falls into the well, it is removed (by drawing water), and the removal of what is in it of water is purification for it. If a mouse, sparrow, wagtail, sudaniyya (black bird), or gecko dies in it, between twenty to thirty buckets are removed according to the size of the animal. If a pigeon, hen, or cat dies in it, between forty to sixty buckets are removed. If a dog, sheep, or human dies in it, all its water is removed. The number of buckets is considered by the medium-sized bucket used for wells; if water is removed with a large bucket that holds the equivalent of a medium bucket and is counted accordingly, it is permissible. If the animal swells or decomposes in it, all its water is removed, whether the animal is small or large. If the well is a natural spring that cannot be drained, and it is obligatory to remove what is in it, they remove an amount equivalent to what was in it of water. If a dead mouse or other animal is found in the well and they do not know when it fell, and it has not swelled nor decomposed, they repeat the prayers of a day and night if they performed wudu from it, and they wash everything that its water touched. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: They do not have to repeat anything until they ascertain when it fell. The leftover water (su'r) of a human and that whose meat is eaten is pure.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage from Al-Quduri presents the Hanafi rulings on purification of wells contaminated by najasah (impurity). It is a ruling-with-proof passage, where the matn states graded obligations depending on the animal that died in the well, and the commentary provides proofs from hadith and athar. The key principle: removal of water purifies the well, but the required quantity varies. For small animals like mice and birds, 20-30 medium buckets suffice. For medium animals like cats and chickens, 40-60 buckets. For large animals like dogs, sheep, or humans, the entire well must be emptied. If the animal decomposes, full removal is required regardless of size. If the well is a spring that cannot be fully drained, they must remove an amount equal to its total water volume (e.g., by continuous drawing). A special case: if a dead animal is found without knowledge of when it fell and no decomposition, Abu Hanifa requires repetition of all prayers performed with that water within a day and night, and washing anything touched. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that nothing is repeated until the time is known, following the principle of certainty. Finally, su'r (leftover water) of humans and halal-meat animals (e.g., sheep, cows, chickens) is pure, based on the hadith of Ibn Abbas.

Key Terms
سُؤْر (su'r): The leftover water after an animal or human has drunk from a vessel; ruled pure for humans and halal-meat animals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Al-Quduri, the leftover water (su'r) of which of the following is pure?
A) Dog
B) Pig
C) Human
D) Cat

Key Takeaway
Su'r of humans and halal-meat animals is pure.

Impurity of Su'r: Dog, Pig, and Predatory Animals
Ruling on su'r of dog, pig, and predatory animals with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the su'r of dog, pig, and predatory animals and identify the proofs (dalil) that establish it.

Core Idea
The leftover water of a dog, pig, or predatory animal is impure (najis).

This lesson addresses the legal purity status of water left over after certain animals have drunk from a vessel. The Hanafi school rules that such water is impure and cannot be used for purification. The matn concisely states the ruling, and the following proofs from hadith and Quran establish the evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its subjects
Read the matn and note the three categories: dog, pig, and predatory beasts (siba'). The ruling is that their leftover water is najis (impure).
Su'r is the leftover water after an animal drinks.
2
Examine the hadith proof for dog su'r
Consider the hadith about washing a vessel seven times after a dog drinks. The command to wash implies the water is impure because washing is required to remove impurity.
The hadith is from Bukhari and Daruqutni.
3
Examine the Quranic proof for pig su'r
Allah says 'the pig, for it is an abomination (rijs)'. This verse directly declares the pig as impure, so its leftover water inherits that impurity.
Quran 6:145.
4
Connect the prohibition on eating predatory animals to their su'r
The Prophet forbade eating every fanged beast of prey. Since their flesh is haram, their saliva and leftover water are also impure by extension, based on the principle that what is forbidden to consume also imparts impurity to its remnants.
Hadith from Abu Tha'labah, agreed upon.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَسُؤْرُ الْكَلْبِ وَالْخِنْزِيرِ وَسِبَاعِ الْبَهَائِم نَجِسٌ. وَالدَّلِيلُ: عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ، قَالَ: إِنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «إِذَا شَرِبَ الكَلْبُ فِي إِنَاءِ أَحَدِكُمْ فَلْيَغْسِلْهُ سَبْعًا» (بخاري). وَعَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فِي الْكَلْبِ يَلَغُ فِي الْإِنَاءِ أَنَّهُ يَغْسِلُهُ ثَلَاثًا أَوْ خَمْسًا أَوْ سَبْعًا (دارقطني). وَقَالَ تَعَالَى: «الْخِنزِيرِ فَإِنَّهُ رِجْسٌ» (الأنعام 145). وَعَنْ أَبِي ثَعْلَبَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ: أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ نَهَى عَنْ أَكْلِ كُلِّ ذِي نَابٍ مِنَ السِّبَاعِ (بخاري ومسلم).
The leftover water of the dog, pig, and predatory beasts is impure. Evidence: From Abu Hurairah, he said: The Messenger of Allah said: When a dog drinks from a vessel of one of you, let him wash it seven times. And from Abu Hurairah from the Prophet regarding a dog lapping in a vessel: that he washes it three or five or seven times. And Allah said: The pig, for it is an abomination. And from Abu Tha'labah: The Messenger of Allah forbade eating every fanged beast of prey.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on the leftover water (su'r) of certain animals. The matn states that the su'r of dog, pig, and predatory animals is najis. The Hanafi school considers this ruling established by multiple proofs: the hadith of the dog requiring seven washes, the Quranic verse declaring pig as rijs (impure), and the prohibition on eating predatory animals, which implies their saliva is impure. The different narrations about washing three, five, or seven times are reconciled by the seven-times ruling being the most authentic and the one acted upon. The authority weight is Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
سُؤْر (su'r): The leftover water or liquid in a vessel after an animal has drunk from it.
سِبَاع (siba'): Predatory beasts with fangs that hunt and kill prey.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) It is impure (najis).

D) It depends on the dog's diet.

Key Takeaway
The su'r of dog, pig, and predatory animals is najis, established by hadith and Quran, and any water they leave cannot be used for purification.

Su'r of Cat and Free-Range Chicken is Pure
Ruling and proofs for purity of leftover water from cat and free-range chicken

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the su'r of a cat and free-range chicken, cite the primary dalil, and explain the wajh al-dalalah of the hadith.

Core Idea
The su'r of a cat and free-range chicken is pure – the Prophet’s explicit statement overrides customary assumptions.

This lesson addresses a common question in daily life: what to do with water a cat or chicken has drunk? The Hanafi school, relying on clear hadith proofs, rules that such leftover water is pure and can be used for purification. Understanding this ruling helps remove unnecessary hardship in ritual purity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Determine the hukm on su'r of cat and free-range chicken as stated in the matn.
The matn says 'tahir' (pure).
2
Locate the dalil
Which hadith is cited to support the ruling? The passage quotes multiple hadith from Abu Hurairah and Anas.
The hadith: 'It is not impure; rather it is from those who go around among you.'
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove purity? The explicit negation of najasah (impurity) is a clear indication (dalalah qati') of purity.
The Prophet also drank from the cat's su'r, showing permissibility.
4
Note the scope
Does the ruling apply to all cats and chickens? Only free-range chicken (al-mukhallah) is included; confined chicken may differ if it consumes impurities.
The term 'al-mukhallah' restricts the ruling.
5
Evaluate the authority
What is the epistemological weight? The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah, based on ahad hadith but with clear meaning.
The dalil is zanni al-thubut but qat'i al-dalalah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَسُؤْرُ الْهِرَّةِ وَالدَّجَاجَةِ الْمُخَلَّاةِ طَاهِرٌ. وَالدَّلِيلُ: عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ، قَالَ: إِنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «إِذَا وَلَغَتْ فِيهِ الهِرَّةُ غُسِلَ مَرَّةً» (ترمذي). وَقَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «إِنَّهَا لَيْسَتْ بِنَجَسِ، إِنَّمَا هِيَ مِنَ الطَّوَّافِينَ عَلَيْكُمْ أَوِ الطَّوَّافَاتِ» (ترمذي، أبو داود). وَعَنْ أَنَسٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ قَالَ: شَرِبَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ مِنْ سُؤْرِ الْهِرَّةِ (الشمائل المحمدية).

And the Messenger of Allah said: It is not impure; rather it is from those who go around among you. And from Anas: The Messenger of Allah drank from the leftover water of a cat.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage establishes that the su'r of a cat and a free-range chicken is pure. The Hanafi school relies on the hadith where the Prophet explicitly stated the cat is not impure because it is a domestic animal that frequently moves around people. The command to wash the vessel once if a cat laps is interpreted as a recommendation (sunnah) not a requirement, further indicating purity. The su'r of a free-range chicken is also pure because it eats grains and is not confined to impure substances. The authority weight is from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
الْمُخَلَّاة (al-mukhallah): A chicken that is free to roam and forage for itself, not confined to a coop.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Su'r of Mule and Donkey is Questionable
Ruling on leftover water of mule and donkey

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the su'r of mule and donkey and apply the procedure when only such water is available.

Core Idea
Doubtful water requires both wudu and tayammum — precaution over certainty.

This lesson addresses a unique category in Hanafi taharah: mashkuk (doubtful) water. The leftover water of mules and donkeys is neither declared pure nor impure due to conflicting evidence. You will learn the ruling, the evidence behind it, and the practical steps when only such water is available.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling status
Note that the su'r of mule and donkey is declared mashkuk (doubtful), not definitively pure (tahir) or impure (najis).
Mashkuk is a distinct third category in Hanafi fiqh.
2
Understand the conditional procedure
When no other water is available, one must perform wudu with the mashkuk water and also perform tayammum.
Both acts are obligatory in this situation; order does not matter.
3
Examine the evidence
The proof includes a hadith forbidding donkey meat, implying impurity, and a narration that Ibn Umar disliked the su'r, indicating uncertainty.
The evidence is zanni (speculative), leading to the mashkuk status.
4
Contrast with other schools
Imam al-Shafi'i considers the su'r pure because the animal's body is pure. The Hanafi school retains the doubt.
The practical difference: Shafi'is would only need wudu, while Hanafis require both.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَسُؤْرُ الْبَغْلِ وَالْحِمَارِ مَشْكُوكٌ فِيهِمَا فَإِنْ لَمْ يَجِدْ غَيْرَهُمَا تَوَضَّأَ بِهِمَا وَتَيَمَّمَ وَأَيَّهُمَا قَدَّمَهُ جَازَ. الدَّلِيلُ: عَنْ جَابِرِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا، قَالَ: «نَهَى رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ يَوْمَ خَيْبَرَ عَنْ لُحُومِ الْحُمُرِ الْأَهْلِيَّةِ، وَرَخَّصَ في الخيل» (بخاري ومسلم). وَعَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ أَنَّهُ كَانَ يَكْرَهُ سُؤْرَ الْحِمَارِ (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة).
The leftover water of a mule and a donkey is questionable concerning them. If one does not find water other than them, he performs ablution with them and also performs tayammum, and whichever he presented first is permissible. Evidence: From Jabir ibn Abdullah, he said: The Messenger of Allah forbade on the day of Khaybar the meat of domestic donkeys, and permitted horses. And from Ibn Umar: He disliked the leftover water of a donkey.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage deals with the su'r of mule and donkey, which is considered mashkuk (doubtful). The Hanafi school holds that it is unclear whether these animals' saliva is pure or impure because the textual evidence is conflicting: the prohibition of donkey meat suggests impurity, while the fact that the Prophet rode a donkey suggests its body is not fundamentally impure. Since the issue is unresolved, when no other water is available, one must perform wudu with this water (as it may be pure) and also perform tayammum (as it may be impure). The order does not matter; both acts are required for certainty. The authority weight is from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
مَشْكُوك (mashkuk): Doubtful; the ruling is not definitively established as pure or impure.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Use it for wudu and it is sufficient.
B) Perform tayammum only.
C) Perform wudu with it and also tayammum.
D) Skip the prayer until finding pure water.

Key Takeaway
The leftover water of mule and donkey is mashkuk; in necessity, one must perform both wudu and tayammum.

Ruling on Leftover Water of Mules and Donkeys
Ruling with proofs for the doubtful status of mule and donkey su'ur.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the leftover water (su'ur) of mules and donkeys, explain why it is considered mashkuk (doubtful), and apply the required action of combining wudu and tayammum.

Core Idea
The leftover water of mules and donkeys is mashkuk—neither pure nor impure—requiring both wudu and tayammum.

In this lesson, we explore the Hanafi ruling on the leftover water of mules and donkeys, which is classified as mashkuk (doubtful) due to conflicting evidence. Al-Quduri's matn instructs that when only such water is available, one must perform both wudu and tayammum as a precaution. We will examine the three proofs that lead to this unique category.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is using the su'ur (leftover water) of mules or donkeys for wudu. The ruling is that this water is mashkuk (doubtful).
Mashkuk is a distinct Hanafi category between tahir (pure) and najis (impure).
2
Understand the category 'mashkuk'
Mashkuk means doubtful. The Hanafi school uses it when evidence for purity and impurity conflict. It requires ihtiyat (precaution).
Other schools may not have this intermediate category.
3
Analyze the primary evidence
The hadith of Khaybar prohibits donkey meat but permits horse meat. This creates a contradiction: prohibition suggests impurity, permission suggests purity.
See Sahih al-Bukhari 4219 and Sahih Muslim 1936.
4
Examine supporting evidence
The Prophet rode a donkey (hadith of Mu'adh), which implies the donkey is pure and thus its su'ur pure. However, Ibn Umar disliked using donkey su'ur, indicating impurity. These reinforce the doubt.
Bukhari 2856 and Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah 304.
5
Derive the practical requirement
Because the status is mashkuk, one must perform both wudu with the water and tayammum to be certain of purification. The order does not matter.
This is a wajib combination due to ihtiyat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَسُؤْرُ الْبَغْلِ وَالْحِمَارِ مَشْكُوكٌ فِيهِمَا فَإِنْ لَمْ يَجِدْ غَيْرَهُمَا تَوَضَّأَ بِهِمَا وَتَيَمَّمَ وَأَيَّهُمَا قَدَّمَهُ جَازَ.
وجه : (1) الحديث لثبوت: عَنْ جَابِرِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا، قَالَ: «نَهَى رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ يَوْمَ خَيْبَرَ عَنْ لُحُومِ الحْمُرِ الْأَهْلِيَّةِ، وَرَخَّصَ في الخيل» (بخاري بَابُ غَزْوَةِ خَيْبَرَ، غبر 4219/ مسلم، بَابُ تَحريم أكل لحم الحمر الإنسيَّة، غبر 1936)
وجه : (2) الحديث لثبوت: عَنْ مُعَادٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ، قَالَ: كُنْتُ رِدْفَ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ عَلَى حِمَارٍ يُقَالُ لَهُ عُفَيْرٌ (بخاري بَابُ اسْمِ الْفَرَسِ وَالحِمَارِ، نمبر 2856)
وجه : (3) قول الصحابي لثبوت: عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ «أَنَّهُ كَانَ يَكْرَهُ سُؤْرَ الْحِمَارِ» (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، فِي الْوُضُوءِ بِسُؤْرِ الْحِمَارِ وَالْكَلْبِ، مَنْ كَرِهَهُ، نمبر 304)
اصول: گدھے اور خچر کے گوشت کو شریعت نے بعض موقع پر حلال قرار دیا، اور بعض موقع پر حرام، اس لئے ان کا جو ٹھا مشکوک ہو گیا، یعنی پاک بھی نہیں اور ناپاک بھی نہیں۔
لغت : الحِمَارِ گدھا، وَالْبَغْلِ: فجر
And the leftover water of the mule and the donkey is doubtful concerning them both. If he does not find other than them, he performs wudu with them and performs tayammum, and whichever he precedes is permissible.
Evidence 1: The hadith for confirmation: From Jabir ibn Abdullah (may Allah be pleased with them both), he said: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forbade on the day of Khaybar the meat of domesticated donkeys, and permitted horses.'
Evidence 2: The hadith for confirmation: From Mu'adh (may Allah be pleased with him), he said: 'I was riding behind the Prophet (peace be upon him) on a donkey called 'Ufayr.'
Evidence 3: The saying of the Companion for confirmation: From Ibn Umar, that he disliked the leftover water of the donkey.
Principle: The meat of the donkey and mule was declared permissible by the Shari'ah on some occasions, and forbidden on some occasions, so their leftover became doubtful, i.e., it is neither pure nor impure.
Lexicon: الحمار = donkey, والبغل = mule.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the matn of Al-Quduri regarding the status of leftover water (su'ur) of mules and donkeys. The ruling states that such water is mashkuk (doubtful) in terms of purity—it is neither definitively pure (tahir) nor definitively impure (najis). Therefore, if a person has no other water available for wudu, he must perform wudu with this doubtful water and also perform tayammum (dry ablution) to ensure ritual purification. It does not matter which he performs first. The passage then provides three evidences from the Sunnah and the practice of the Companions to support this ruling. The first hadith from Jabir indicates that the prohibition of donkey meat at Khaybar implies impurity, while the permission for horses suggests purity; this contradiction creates doubt. The second hadith shows the Prophet riding a donkey, indicating its permissibility. The third is the practice of Ibn Umar, who disliked using donkey leftover water, indicating its doubtful status. The Urdu commentary explains that the contradictory rulings on donkey and mule meat (halal at times, haram at others) lead to their su'ur being considered mashkuk—not pure, not impure.

Key Terms
سُؤْر (su'ur): The leftover water in a vessel after an animal or person drinks from it.
مَشْكُوك (mashkuk): Doubtful; a legal category where purity is uncertain, requiring ihtiyat (precaution).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what must a person do if the only water available is the leftover (su'ur) of a mule or donkey?
A) Perform wudu with it and no further action.
B) Perform wudu with it and also perform tayammum.
C) Perform tayammum only and ignore the water.
D) Use the water only if no other option, and repeat wudu later.

Key Takeaway
The leftover water of mules and donkeys is mashkuk, requiring both wudu and tayammum to ensure valid purification.

The Purity of Cat Leftover Water
Ruling and proof for the purity of cat su'ur

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on cat leftover water and explain the proof from hadith.

Core Idea
Cat leftover water is pure; the vessel is washed once as a recommended sunnah.

This passage from Al-Quduri addresses a practical question of daily life: if a cat drinks from a vessel, is the water impure? The Hanafi school rules it pure, based on a hadith that categorizes cats as domestic companions. Let's examine the ruling and the proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
What is the act (cat drinking) and what is the required action (wash once)?
The phrase 'غُسِلَ مَرَّةً' clearly indicates a single wash.
2
Determine the hukm level
Is the washing wajib, sunnah, or mubah? The water is pure; the wash is recommended (mustahabb) to remove the cat's saliva, not because of impurity.
The Hanafi position is that the water is tahir, and washing is a sunnah.
3
Locate the dalil
The matn cites the hadith: 'إنها ليست بنجس' – explicit negation of najasah.
The hadith is from Sunan al-Tirmidhi and Sunan Abi Dawud.
4
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove the ruling? The explicit words 'ليست بنجس' show that the cat's saliva is not impure. The phrase 'من الطوافين' provides the rationale: cats frequently circle around people, so treating their saliva as impure would cause hardship.
This is a clear dalala (indication) from the text.
5
Note the cross-madhhab context
Although most schools agree, some early scholars required seven washes. The Hanafi school relies on this hadith and rejects the stricter view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا وَلَغَتْ فِيهِ الْهِرَّةُ غُسِلَ مَرَّةً
وجه : (1) الحديث لثبوت: عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «إِنَّهَا لَيْسَتْ بِنَجَسٍ، إِنَّمَا هِيَ مِنَ الطَّوَّافِينَ عَلَيْكُمْ أَوِ الطَّوَّافَاتِ» (سنن الترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي سُؤْرِ الْهِرَّةِ، نمبر 92، ابوداؤد، بَابُ سُؤْرِ الْهِرَّةِ، نمبر 75)
And when a cat drinks from it (the vessel), it is washed once.
Evidence (1) The hadith for confirmation: The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'It is not impure; it is only one of those who go around among you or go around (circumambulate).'
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage gives the Hanafi ruling on the leftover water (su'ur) of a cat (hirra). According to the matn, if a cat drinks from a vessel of water, the water remains pure; it should be washed once (i.e., the utensil is washed once as a recommended precaution). The proof is the hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) explicitly states that the cat is not impure (najis) because it is one of the 'tawwafin' – those that frequently go around among people. This indicates that cats are considered domestic animals that are permissible to have in homes, and their saliva is pure. The Hanafi school thus considers cat su'ur as tahir (pure), and only a single wash of the utensil is recommended, not obligatory.

Key Terms
وَلَغَتْ (walaghat): The act of an animal lapping water with its tongue from a vessel.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how many times must a vessel be washed if a cat drinks from it?
A) Seven times, one with dust.
B) Once.
C) Three times.
D) Not washed at all.

Key Takeaway
Cat leftover water is pure (tahir); the vessel is washed once as a sunnah, based on the hadith that the cat is not impure.

Conditions for Tayammum: Travel and Distance
Ruling and proofs for tayammum conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for tayammum according to the Hanafi school and identify the evidence that establishes the mile-distance criterion.

Core Idea
Tayammum is wajib when water is absent, but the Hanafi school requires a minimum distance of one mile from the city.

This lesson begins the chapter on tayammum (dry ablution). You will examine the precise conditions under which tayammum becomes valid, focusing on the requirement of travel or being outside the city at a distance of approximately one mile. We will also trace the Quranic, hadith, and Companion evidence that supports this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Locate the ruling on tayammum in the matn. What is the legal status (hukm) of tayammum when conditions are met?
The matn implicitly indicates wujub (obligation) as a substitute.
2
State the conditions for tayammum
According to the matn, two conditions are required: (1) absence of water (lam yajid al-ma'), and (2) being a traveler (musafir) or outside the city (kharj al-misr) with a distance of about a mile or more.
The mile distance is a Hanafi specification.
3
Locate the primary dalil
The Quranic verse (al-Nisa 43 / al-Ma'idah 6) is cited. Identify the operative phrase that indicates the ruling.
The conditional 'if you do not find water' triggers the substitute.
4
Analyze the companion evidence
Multiple reports from Ibn Umar show he performed tayammum at distances of one to three miles from Medina and did not repeat prayers. How does this support the Hanafi distance condition?
These actions establish the mile as a practical minimum.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school does not require a specific distance; tayammum is valid whenever water is absent. Understand the point of ikhtilaf.
The Hanafi position is based on the practice of Ibn Umar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ التَّيَمُّمِ
وَمَنْ لَمْ يَجِدْ الْمَاءَ وَهُوَ مُسَافِرٌ أَوْ خَارِجَ الْمِصْرِ وَبَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَ الْمِصْرِ نَحْوُ الْمِيلِ أَوْ أَكْثَرُ
وجه : (1) الآية لثبوت: {فَلَمْ تَجِدُوا مَاءً فَتَيَمَّمُوا صَعِيدًا طَيِّبًا} (سورة النساء: 43 / سورة المائدة: 6)
وجه : (2) الحديث لثبوت: عَنْ أَبِي ذَرٍ، قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «الصَّعِيدُ الطَّيِّبُ وَضُوءُ الْمُسْلِمِ وَلَوْ إِلَى عَشْرِ سِنِينَ» (أبو داؤد، بَابُ الْجُنُبِ يَتَيَمَّمُ، غبر 332 / سنن الترمذي، بَابُ التَّيَمُّمِ لِلْجُنُبِ، غبر 124)
وجه : (3) قول الصحابي لثبوت: عَنْ نَافِعٍ، قَالَ: «تَيَمَّمَ ابْنُ عُمَرَ عَلَى رَأْسِ مِيلٍ أَوْ مِيلَيْنِ مِنَ الْمَدِينَةِ, فَصَلَّى الْعَصْرَ فَقَدِمَ وَالشَّمْسُ مُرْتَفِعَةٌ» (سنن الدار قطني، بَابٌ فِي بَيَانِ الْمَوْضِعِ الَّذِي يَجُوزُ التَّيَمُّمُ فِيهِ، نمبر 719)
وجه : (4) قول الصحابي لثبوت: «وَأَقْبَلَ ابْنُ عُمَرَ مِنْ أَرْضِهِ بِالخُرُفِ فَحَضَرَتِ العَصْرُ بِمَرْبَدِ النَّعَمِ فَصَلَّى ثُمَّ دَخَلَ المَدِينَةَ وَالشَّمْسُ مُرْتَفِعَةٌ فَلَمْ يُعِدْ» (بخاري بَابُ التَّيَمُّمِ فِي الحَضَرِ، إِذَا لَمْ يَجِدِ المَاءَ، وَخَافَ فَوْتَ الصَّلاةِ، نمبر 337)
وجه : (5) قول الصحابي لثبوت: «أَنَّ ابْنَ عُمَرَ كَانَ يَتَيَمَّمُ عِنْدَ مَرْبَدِ النَّعَمِ, وَصَلَّى وَهُوَ عَلَى ثَلَاثَةِ أَمْيَالٍ مِنَ الْمَدِينَةِ» (سنن الدار قطني، بَابٌ فِي بَيَانِ الْمَوْضِعِ الَّذِي يَجُوزُ التَّيَمُّمُ فِيهِ، غبر 717)
اصول: بیماری کا خوف ہو، یا پانی ایک میل سے دور ہو اور مسافر ہو یا شہر دور تو مٹی سے طہارت حاصل کرلے۔
Chapter of Tayammum
And whoever does not find water while he is a traveler or outside the city, and between him and the city is about a mile or more.
Evidence (1) The ayah for confirmation: 'And if you do not find water, then perform tayammum with clean earth' (Surah al-Nisa: 43 / Surah al-Ma'idah: 6)
Evidence (2) The hadith for confirmation: From Abu Dharr, the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Clean earth is the wudu of the Muslim, even if for ten years.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on the junub performing tayammum, no. 332; Tirmidhi, chapter on tayammum for the junub, no. 124)
Evidence (3) The saying of the Companion for confirmation: From Nafi', he said: 'Ibn Umar performed tayammum at a distance of a mile or two from Medina, then prayed Asr, and then came (to Medina) while the sun was still high.' (Sunan al-Daraqutni, chapter on the location where tayammum is permissible, no. 719)
Evidence (4) The saying of the Companion for confirmation: 'Ibn Umar came from his land at al-Khuruf, and Asr came at Marbad al-Na'm, so he prayed (with tayammum), then entered Medina while the sun was high, and he did not repeat (the prayer).' (Sahih al-Bukhari, chapter on tayammum in the city when water is not found and one fears missing the prayer, no. 337)
Evidence (5) The saying of the Companion for confirmation: 'Ibn Umar would perform tayammum at Marbad al-Na'm and pray while he was three miles from Medina.' (Sunan al-Daraqutni, chapter on the location... no. 717)
Principle: If there is fear of illness, or water is a mile away, and one is a traveler or far from the city, then he obtains purification with earth.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage begins the chapter on Tayammum (dry ablution) and presents the conditions under which tayammum is permissible. According to the matn of Al-Quduri, tayammum is allowed for a person who is traveling (musafir) or who is outside the city (misr) and the distance between him and the city is approximately one mile or more, and he does not find water. The passage then provides multiple evidences from the Quran, Sunnah, and the practice of the Companions. The primary evidence is the Quranic verse: 'If you do not find water, then perform tayammum with clean earth' (al-Nisa 43, al-Ma'idah 6). The hadith from Abu Dharr emphasizes that clean earth suffices as purification even for ten years. The actions of Ibn Umar reported by Nafi' show that he would perform tayammum when he was one to two miles away from Medina and then pray without repeating later. These reports establish that tayammum is valid when water is not accessible within a mile or more. The Urdu commentary summarizes the principle: tayammum is allowed if there is fear of illness, or water is a mile away, and one is traveling or far from the city.

Key Terms
التَّيَمُّم (al-tayammum): Dry ablution using clean earth as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or harmful.
الْمِيل (al-mil): A unit of distance; approximately 1.6-2 km depending on the historical definition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how far from the city must one be to perform tayammum if water is not found?
A) Any distance, no minimum.
B) One mile or more.
C) Half a mile.
D) Three miles exactly.

Key Takeaway
Tayammum is wajib for a traveler or one outside the city when water is absent and the distance from the city is approximately one mile or more.

Taharah — Purification

8 min
Conditions Permitting Tayammum
Ruling with proof: conditions for tayammum from Quran, Sunnah, and companion practice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which tayammum is permissible in the Hanafi school and identify the Quranic and hadith proofs for each condition.

Core Idea
When water is absent or harmful, pure earth purifies; the Quran and Sunnah clearly permit tayammum.

Tayammum is a divine concession (rukhsah) that allows purification when water is unavailable or its use would cause harm. In this lesson, we extract the precise conditions from the classical Hanafi text and examine the evidence (adillah) that establishes each condition. You will learn not just the rulings, but how the Hanafi school derives them from the primary sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the triggering factors (asbab) for tayammum
Read the opening lines of the passage and list the circumstances that make tayammum permissible: lack of water while traveling, being outside the city at a distance of about a mile or more, illness, fear of harm from cold water.
These are the causes (asbab) for the permissibility of tayammum.
2
Locate the primary proof from the Quran
Find the two Quranic verses cited (4:43 and 5:6) and note that the imperative 'fatayammamu' indicates obligation (wujub) according to Hanafi usul.
The same verses also specify the method, but here we focus on the permission itself.
3
Examine the hadith proofs for the traveler
Read the hadith of Abu Dharr that 'clean earth is the ablution of the Muslim, even for ten years' and the hadith of Amr ibn al-As for the ill person. Understand how these reinforce the Quranic permission.
The hadith of Amr shows the Prophet did not censure tayammum even in a cold night when water was available but harmful.
4
Analyze the practice of Ibn Umar as evidence for distance
Several narrations from Ibn Umar show he performed tayammum at distances from one to three miles outside Madinah and did not repeat his prayer. This establishes the 'mile or more' rule for those outside the city.
The Hanafi school uses the action of a companion as a proof (qawl sahabi) in matters where there is no known disagreement.
5
Summarize the conditions as a legal principle
The text gives a concise 'asl' (principle) in Urdu: if there is fear of illness, or water is a mile away while traveling, or the city is distant, then tayammum is valid. Write this principle in your own words.
This principle captures the essence of the conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ التَّيَمُّمِ
ل وَمَنْ لَمْ يَجِدْ الْمَاءَ وَهُوَ مُسَافِرٌ أَوْ خَارِجَ الْمِصْرِ وَبَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَ الْمِصْرِ نَحْوُ الْمِيلِ أَوْ أَكْثَرُ ل وجه : (1) الآية لثبوت وَمَنْ لَمْ يَجِدْ الْمَاءَ وَهُوَ مُسَافِرٌ فَلَمْ تَجِدُوا مَاءً فَتَيَمَّمُوا صَعِيدًا طيِّبًا فَأَمْسَحُوا بِوُجُوهِكُمْ وَأَيْدِيكُم) (سورة النساء5 ، أيت نمبر 6)
وجه: (٢) الآية لثبوت وَمَنْ لَمْ يَجِدْ الْمَاءَ وَهُوَ مُسَافِرًا ﴿وَإِن كُنتُم مَّرْضَى أَوْ عَلَى سَفَرٍ أَوْ جَاءَ أَحَدٌ مِّنكُم مِّنَ الْغَابِطِ أَوْ لَمَسْتُمُ النِّسَاءَ فَلَمْ تَجِدُوا مَاءً فَتَيَمَّمُوا صَعِيدًا طَيِّبًا فَأَمْسَحُوا بِوُجُوهِكُمْ وَأَيْدِيكُم مِّنْةً ) (سورة المائدة 5 أيت نمبر 6)
وجه: (٣) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ لَمْ يَجِدْ الْمَاءَ وَهُوَ مُسَافِرٌ \ عَنْ أَبِي ذَرٍ... قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «الصَّعِيدُ الطَّيِّبُ وَضُوءُ الْمُسْلِمِ وَلَوْ إِلَى عَشْرِ سِنِينَ(ابو داؤد، بَابُ الْجُنُبِ يَتَيَمَّمُ، غبر 332 /سنن الترمذي، بَابُ التَّيَمُّمِ لِلْجُنُبِ إِذَا لَمْ يَجِدِ الْمَاءَ، غمبر (124)
وجه (۴) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ لَمْ يَجِدْ الْمَاءَ وَهُوَ مُسَافِرٌ \ عَنْ أَبِي ذَرٍ، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: الصَّعِيدُ الطَّيِّبُ طَهُورٌ مَا لَمْ يُوجَدِ الْمَاءُ وَلَوْ إِلَى عَشْرِ حِجَجٍ فَإِذَا وَجَدْتَ الْمَاءَ فَأَمِسَّهُ بَشَرَتَكَ (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، الرَّجُلُ يَجْنُبُ وَلَيْسَ يَقْدِرُ عَلَى الْمَاءِ ، غبر 1661) وجه : (۵) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَمَنْ لَمْ يَجِدْ الْمَاءَ وَهُوَ مُسَافِرٌ عَنْ نَافِعِ, قَالَ: «تَيَمَّمَ ابْنُ عُمَرَ عَلَى رَأْسِ مِيلَ أَوْ مِيلَيْنِ مِنَ الْمَدِينَةِ, فَصَلَّى الْعَصْرَ فَقَدِمَ وَالشَّمْسُ مُرْتَفِعَةٌ (سنن الدار قطني، بَابٌ فِي بَيَانِ الْمَوْضِعِ الَّذِي يَجُوزُ التَّيَمُّمُ فِيهِ وَقَدْرِهِ مِنَ الْبَلَدِ وَطَلَبِ الْمَاءِ، نمبر 719) وجه: (٢) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَمَنْ لَمْ يَجِدْ الْمَاءَ وَهُوَ مُسَافِرٌ \ وَأَقْبَلَ ابْنُ عُمَرَ: «مِنْ أَرْضِهِ بِالخُرُفِ فَحَضَرَتِ العَصْرُ بِمَرْبَدِ النَّعَمِ فَصَلَّى ثُمَّ دَخَلَ المَدِينَةَ وَالشَّمْسُ مُرْتَفِعَةٌ فَلَمْ يُعِدْ» (بخاري بَابُ التَّيَمُّمِ فِي الحَضَرِ، إِذَا لَمْ يَجِدِ المَاءَ، وَخَافَ فَوْتَ الصَّلاةِ، نمبر 337) وجه : (٧) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَمَنْ لَمْ يَجِدْ الْمَاءَ وَهُوَ مُسَافِرٌ \ أَنَّ ابْنَ عُمَرَ كَانَ يَتَيَمَّمُ عَرْبَدِ النَّعَمِ, وَصَلَّى وَهُوَ عَلَى ثَلَاثَةِ أَمْيَالٍ مِنَ الْمَدِينَةِ(سنن الدار قطني، بَابٌ فِي بَيَانِ الْمَوْضِعِ الَّذِي يَجُوزُ التَّيَمُّمُ فِيهِ وَقَدْرِهِ مِنَ الْبَلَدِ وَطَلَبِ الْمَاءِ ، غمبر (717)
اصول: بیماری کا خوف ہو، یا پانی ایک میل سے دور ہو اور مسافر ہو یا شہر دور تو مٹی سے طہارت حاصل کرلے۔
أَوْ كَانَ يَجِدُ الْمَاءَ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ مَرِيْضٌ فَخَافَ إِنِ اسْتَعْمَلَ الْمَاءَ اشْتَدَّ مَرَضَهُ، أَوْ خَافَ الْجُنُبُ إِنْ اغْتَسَلَ بِالْمَاءِ أَنْ يَقْتُلَهُ الْبَرْدُ أَوْ يُفْرِضَهُ فَإِنَّهُ يَتَيَمَّمُ بِالصَّعِيْدِ.
وَالتَّيَمُّمُ ضَرْبَتَانِ يَمْسَحُ بِإِحْدَاهُمَا وَجْهَهُ وَبِالْأُخْرَى ذِرَاعَيْهِ إِلَى الْمِرْفَقَيْنِ إِلَى الْمِرْفَقَيْنِ وَالتَّيَمُّمُ مِنْ الْجَنَابَةِ وَالْحْدَثِ سَوَاءٌ
ل وجه : (۱) الأية لثبوت أَوْ كَانَ يَجِدُ الْمَاءَ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ مَرِيضٌ لَا يُكَلِّفُ اللَّهُ نَفْسًا إِلَّا وُسْعَهَا لَهَا مَا كَسَبَتْ وَعَلَيْهَا مَا اكْتَسَبَتْ ) (سورة البقرة 2 ، أيت نمبر 286)
وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت أَوْ كَانَ يَجِدُ الْمَاءَ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ مَرِيْضٌ \ أَنَّ عَمْرَو بْنَ الْعَاصِ: " أَجْنَبَ فِي لَيْلَةٍ بَارِدَةٍ، فَتَيَمَّمَ وَتَلاَ: {وَلاَ تَقْتُلُوا أَنْفُسَكُمْ إِنَّ اللَّهَ كَانَ بِكُمْ رَحِيمًا} [النساء: 29] فَذَكَرَ لِلنَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فَلَمْ يُعَنِّفْ " (بخاري بَابٌ : إِذَا خَافَ الْجُنُبُ عَلَى نَفْسِهِ الْمَرَضَ أَوِ المَوْتَ، أَوْ خَافَ العَطَشَ، تَيَمَّمَ، نمبر 345)
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَالتَّيَمُّمُ ضَرْبَتَانِ يَمْسَحُ بِإِحْدَاهُمَا وَجْهَهُ \ عَنْ عَمَّارِ بْنِ يَاسِرٍ، حِينَ تَيَمَّمُوا مَعَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ «فَأَمَرَ الْمُسْلِمِينَ، فَضَرَبُوا بِأَكُفِّهِمُ التَّرَابَ، وَلَم يَقْبِضُوا مِنَ التُّرَابِ شَيْئًا، فَمَسَحُوا بِوُجُوهِهِمْ مَسْحَةً وَاحِدَةً، ثُمَّ عَادُوا، فَضَرَبُوا بِأَكُفِّهِمُ الصَّعِيدَ مَرَّةً أُخْرَى، فَمَسَحُوا بِأَيْدِيهِمْ» (سنن ابن ماجه بَابٌ في التَّيَمُّم ضَرْبَتَيْنِ، نمبر 571/ ابو داؤد بَابُ التَّيَمُّم، نمبر 318) وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَالتَّيَمُّمُ ضَرْبَتَانِ يَمْسَحُ بِإِحْدَاهُمَا وَجْهَهُ \ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «التَّيَمُّمُ ضَرْبَتَانِ ضَرْبَةً لِلْوَجْهِ, وَضَرْبَةً لِلْيَدَيْنِ إِلَى الْمِرْفَقَيْنِ»(سنن الدار قطني، بَابُ التَّيَمُّم، نمبر 685)
وجه (۳) الحديث لثبوت وَالتَّيَمُّمُ ضَرْبَتَانِ يَمْسَحُ بِإِحْدَاهُمَا وَجْهَهُ \ عَنْ عَمَّارِ بْنِ يَاسِرٍ قَالَ: سَأَلْتُ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ عَنِ التَّيَمُّم «فَأَمَرَني ضَرْبَةً وَاحِدَةً لِلْوَجْهِ وَالْكَفَّيْنِ» (ابو داؤد، بَابُ التَّيَمُّم، نمبر 327)
توجه: (1) الآية لثبوت وَالتَّيَمُّمُ مِنْ الْجَنَابَةِ وَالْحَدَثِ سَوَاءٌ \ أَوْ جَاءَ أَحَدٌ مِّنكُم مِّنَ
اصول: تیم میں دو ضربے ہیں، ایک ضرب سے منہ پونچھے اور دوسرے سے ہاتھ ۔
Chapter of Tayammum. And whoever does not find water while traveling or outside the city and between him and the city is about a mile or more: (1) the verse for proof: '...and you find no water, then perform tayammum with clean earth...' (Surah an-Nisa, 5:6). (2) the verse for proof: '...and if you are ill or on a journey or one of you comes from the lavatory or you have touched women and you find no water, then perform tayammum with clean earth...' (Surah al-Ma'idah, 5:6). (3) the hadith for proof: from Abu Dharr... the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Clean earth is the ablution of the Muslim, even if for ten years.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on the junub performing tayammum, no. 332; Tirmidhi, chapter on tayammum for the junub when no water is found, no. 124). (4) the hadith for proof: from Abu Dharr from the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Clean earth is a purifier as long as water is not found, even for ten pilgrimages. And if you find water, let it touch your skin.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, chapter on a man who becomes junub and cannot find water, no. 1661). (5) the saying of a companion for proof: from Nafi' that Ibn Umar performed tayammum at a distance of a mile or two from Madinah and prayed Asr, then entered Madinah while the sun was still high. (Sunan ad-Daraqutni, chapter on the place where tayammum is permitted and its distance from the city and seeking water, no. 719). (6) the saying of a companion for proof: Ibn Umar came from his land at al-Khuruf and Asr came at Marbad an-Na'am, so he prayed, then entered Madinah while the sun was still high and did not repeat. (Bukhari, chapter on tayammum in residence when one does not find water and fears missing the prayer, no. 337). (7) the saying of a companion for proof: Ibn Umar used to perform tayammum at Marbad an-Na'am and pray while he was three miles from Madinah. (Sunan ad-Daraqutni, chapter on the place where tayammum is permitted and its distance, no. 717). Principle: If there is fear of illness, or water is a mile away and one is a traveler, or the city is far, then one obtains purification with earth. Or if one finds water but is ill and fears that using water would worsen the illness, or a junub fears that bathing with water would kill him due to cold or cause hardship, then he performs tayammum with clean earth. And tayammum is two strikes: with one he wipes his face, and with the other his arms to the elbows, to the elbows. And tayammum from janabah and from minor impurity is the same. (1) the verse for proof: 'Allah does not burden a soul beyond its capacity...' (Surah al-Baqarah, 2:286). (2) the hadith for proof: that Amr ibn al-As became junub on a cold night, performed tayammum and recited 'Do not kill yourselves...' (Surah an-Nisa, 4:29), and the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not censure him. (Bukhari, chapter: if a junub fears illness or death or thirst, he performs tayammum, no. 345). (1) the hadith for proof: from Ammar ibn Yasir when they performed tayammum with the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'He commanded the Muslims to strike the earth with their palms, not grasping anything, and wipe their faces once, then repeat and strike the earth again and wipe their hands.' (Sunan Ibn Majah, chapter on tayammum with two strikes, no. 571; Abu Dawud, chapter on tayammum, no. 318). (2) the hadith for proof: from Ibn Umar from the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Tayammum is two strikes: a strike for the face and a strike for the hands to the elbows.' (Sunan ad-Daraqutni, chapter on tayammum, no. 685). (3) the hadith for proof: from Ammar ibn Yasir said: 'I asked the Prophet (peace be upon him) about tayammum, and he commanded me to do one strike for the face and the palms.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on tayammum, no. 327). Attention: (1) the verse for proof that tayammum from janabah and from hadath is the same: '...or one of you comes from the lavatory...' Principle: In tayammum there are two strikes: with one strike he wipes his face, and with the second his hands.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage is the complete chapter on Tayammum from Al-Quduri's matn with the author's commentary providing proofs (wujuh) from the Quran, Hadith, and sayings of the Companions, along with a principle (asl) in Urdu summarizing the conditions. The ruling establishes when tayammum is permissible: if water is not found while traveling, or if one is outside the city at a distance of about a mile or more. The author then cites multiple proofs: two Quranic verses (from Surah an-Nisa and al-Ma'idah) that command tayammum when water is absent; several hadith reports emphasizing that pure earth serves as a purification even for extended periods; and the practice of Ibn Umar, who performed tayammum when a mile or more away from Madinah and did not repeat his prayer upon returning—demonstrating that tayammum is valid when water is not reasonably accessible. The principle (asl) at the bottom of page 41 distills these conditions: fear of illness, water being a mile away while traveling, or the city being distant—then purification is achieved with earth. On page 42, additional conditions are added: even if water is present, if one is ill and using water would worsen the condition, or if a junub fears death from cold or severe hardship, tayammum is also allowed. The method of tayammum is then specified: it consists of two strikes on pure earth—one for wiping the face, and one for wiping the arms to the elbows. Tayammum is the same whether one is in a state of major impurity (janabah) or minor impurity (hadath). Further proofs for the method include the hadith of Ammar ibn Yasir describing two strikes, and the hadith of Ibn Umar explicitly mentioning two strikes. A third hadith from Ammar mentions one strike for face and palms, which may indicate a more concise form or a difference in practice; the author includes it as a proof but the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is two strikes for face and arms. The final note (tawajjuh) refers to the Quranic verse for the equality of tayammum for both types of impurity. The Urdu principle at the end reiterates the method: two strikes, first for the face, second for the hands.

Key Terms
التيمم (al-tayammum): Purification with pure earth (sa'id) as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or harmful.
الصعيد (al-sa'id): The surface of the earth, including soil, sand, stone, or anything that can be used for tayammum.
الميل (al-mil): A unit of distance, approximately 1.6 km or one mile. Used here to define the distance from a city.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a condition for tayammum according to the Hanafi school in this passage?
A) Being a traveler (musafir) outside the city
B) Being outside the city at a mile or more
C) Illness that would worsen with water
D) Fear of death from cold water in janabah

Key Takeaway
Tayammum is permitted when water is not found or harmful, for travelers, those outside the city, the ill, and those fearing harm from cold water.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
Method of Tayammum: Two Strikes and Its Scope
Ruling with proof: method of tayammum (two strikes) and its equality for all impurities.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the Hanafi method of tayammum (two strikes) and explain that it substitutes for both wudu and ghusl.

Core Idea
Tayammum is performed with two strikes: one for the face, one for the hands to the elbows; it removes both major and minor impurity.

Having established the conditions for tayammum, we now turn to its precise method and legal scope. The Hanafi school, based on clear hadith evidence, requires two distinct strikes on pure earth—one for wiping the face and one for wiping the arms to the elbows. This method applies equally whether one is in a state of minor impurity (hadath) or major impurity (janabah). In this lesson, we analyse the hadith proofs and understand why the school insists on two strikes despite some reports mentioning one.

Guided Path
1
Read the method statement
The text states: 'التيمم ضربتان يمسح بإحداهما وجهه وبالأخرى ذراعيه إلى المرفقين' — Tayammum is two strikes: with one he wipes his face, with the other his arms to the elbows. Memorise this key phrase.
This is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) Hanafi method.
2
Identify the hadith proofs for two strikes
The passage cites three hadith: (i) the hadith of Ammar ibn Yasir describing two strikes with the Prophet; (ii) the hadith of Ibn Umar explicitly stating 'tayammum is two strikes: a strike for the face and a strike for the hands to the elbows'; (iii) another hadith of Ammar mentioning one strike for face and palms (which the school interprets as abrogated or for special cases).
The inclusion of a one-strike hadith shows the author's thoroughness, but the two-strike position is preferred.
3
Understand the equality of tayammum for janabah and hadath
The text says 'والتيمم من الجنابة والحدث سواء' — tayammum from major impurity and minor impurity is the same. The proof is that the Quranic verse for tayammum is cited after mentioning both states (جنابت, غائط, لمس النساء).
This simplifies the process: no extra steps are needed for janabah.
4
Analyse the wajibat (obligatory components) of tayammum
From the method description, the wajibat are: (i) two strikes, (ii) wiping the face with the first, (iii) wiping the arms to the elbows with the second. Unlike wudu, there is no wiping of the head or feet.
Omission of any wajib would require repeating the tayammum.
5
Apply the ruling: tayammum substitutes for water purification completely
Once performed, tayammum removes the state of impurity (hadath) just as water would. The same acts that require wudu or ghusl can be performed, including prayer, touching the Quran, etc.
Tayammum does not remove the underlying impurity but permits worship; it is a temporary concession.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ التَّيَمُّمِ
ل وَمَنْ لَمْ يَجِدْ الْمَاءَ وَهُوَ مُسَافِرٌ أَوْ خَارِجَ الْمِصْرِ وَبَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَ الْمِصْرِ نَحْوُ الْمِيلِ أَوْ أَكْثَرُ ل وجه : (1) الآية لثبوت وَمَنْ لَمْ يَجِدْ الْمَاءَ وَهُوَ مُسَافِرٌ فَلَمْ تَجِدُوا مَاءً فَتَيَمَّمُوا صَعِيدًا طيِّبًا فَأَمْسَحُوا بِوُجُوهِكُمْ وَأَيْدِيكُم) (سورة النساء5 ، أيت نمبر 6)
وجه: (٢) الآية لثبوت وَمَنْ لَمْ يَجِدْ الْمَاءَ وَهُوَ مُسَافِرًا ﴿وَإِن كُنتُم مَّرْضَى أَوْ عَلَى سَفَرٍ أَوْ جَاءَ أَحَدٌ مِّنكُم مِّنَ الْغَابِطِ أَوْ لَمَسْتُمُ النِّسَاءَ فَلَمْ تَجِدُوا مَاءً فَتَيَمَّمُوا صَعِيدًا طَيِّبًا فَأَمْسَحُوا بِوُجُوهِكُمْ وَأَيْدِيكُم مِّنْةً ) (سورة المائدة 5 أيت نمبر 6)
وجه: (٣) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ لَمْ يَجِدْ الْمَاءَ وَهُوَ مُسَافِرٌ \ عَنْ أَبِي ذَرٍ... قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «الصَّعِيدُ الطَّيِّبُ وَضُوءُ الْمُسْلِمِ وَلَوْ إِلَى عَشْرِ سِنِينَ(ابو داؤد، بَابُ الْجُنُبِ يَتَيَمَّمُ، غبر 332 /سنن الترمذي، بَابُ التَّيَمُّمِ لِلْجُنُبِ إِذَا لَمْ يَجِدِ الْمَاءَ، غمبر (124)
وجه (۴) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ لَمْ يَجِدْ الْمَاءَ وَهُوَ مُسَافِرٌ \ عَنْ أَبِي ذَرٍ، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: الصَّعِيدُ الطَّيِّبُ طَهُورٌ مَا لَمْ يُوجَدِ الْمَاءُ وَلَوْ إِلَى عَشْرِ حِجَجٍ فَإِذَا وَجَدْتَ الْمَاءَ فَأَمِسَّهُ بَشَرَتَكَ (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، الرَّجُلُ يَجْنُبُ وَلَيْسَ يَقْدِرُ عَلَى الْمَاءِ ، غبر 1661) وجه : (۵) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَمَنْ لَمْ يَجِدْ الْمَاءَ وَهُوَ مُسَافِرٌ عَنْ نَافِعِ, قَالَ: «تَيَمَّمَ ابْنُ عُمَرَ عَلَى رَأْسِ مِيلَ أَوْ مِيلَيْنِ مِنَ الْمَدِينَةِ, فَصَلَّى الْعَصْرَ فَقَدِمَ وَالشَّمْسُ مُرْتَفِعَةٌ (سنن الدار قطني، بَابٌ فِي بَيَانِ الْمَوْضِعِ الَّذِي يَجُوزُ التَّيَمُّمُ فِيهِ وَقَدْرِهِ مِنَ الْبَلَدِ وَطَلَبِ الْمَاءِ، نمبر 719) وجه: (٢) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَمَنْ لَمْ يَجِدْ الْمَاءَ وَهُوَ مُسَافِرٌ \ وَأَقْبَلَ ابْنُ عُمَرَ: «مِنْ أَرْضِهِ بِالخُرُفِ فَحَضَرَتِ العَصْرُ بِمَرْبَدِ النَّعَمِ فَصَلَّى ثُمَّ دَخَلَ المَدِينَةَ وَالشَّمْسُ مُرْتَفِعَةٌ فَلَمْ يُعِدْ» (بخاري بَابُ التَّيَمُّمِ فِي الحَضَرِ، إِذَا لَمْ يَجِدِ المَاءَ، وَخَافَ فَوْتَ الصَّلاةِ، نمبر 337) وجه : (٧) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَمَنْ لَمْ يَجِدْ الْمَاءَ وَهُوَ مُسَافِرٌ \ أَنَّ ابْنَ عُمَرَ كَانَ يَتَيَمَّمُ عَرْبَدِ النَّعَمِ, وَصَلَّى وَهُوَ عَلَى ثَلَاثَةِ أَمْيَالٍ مِنَ الْمَدِينَةِ(سنن الدار قطني، بَابٌ فِي بَيَانِ الْمَوْضِعِ الَّذِي يَجُوزُ التَّيَمُّمُ فِيهِ وَقَدْرِهِ مِنَ الْبَلَدِ وَطَلَبِ الْمَاءِ ، غمبر (717)
اصول: بیماری کا خوف ہو، یا پانی ایک میل سے دور ہو اور مسافر ہو یا شہر دور تو مٹی سے طہارت حاصل کرلے۔
أَوْ كَانَ يَجِدُ الْمَاءَ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ مَرِيْضٌ فَخَافَ إِنِ اسْتَعْمَلَ الْمَاءَ اشْتَدَّ مَرَضَهُ، أَوْ خَافَ الْجُنُبُ إِنْ اغْتَسَلَ بِالْمَاءِ أَنْ يَقْتُلَهُ الْبَرْدُ أَوْ يُفْرِضَهُ فَإِنَّهُ يَتَيَمَّمُ بِالصَّعِيْدِ.
وَالتَّيَمُّمُ ضَرْبَتَانِ يَمْسَحُ بِإِحْدَاهُمَا وَجْهَهُ وَبِالْأُخْرَى ذِرَاعَيْهِ إِلَى الْمِرْفَقَيْنِ إِلَى الْمِرْفَقَيْنِ وَالتَّيَمُّمُ مِنْ الْجَنَابَةِ وَالْحْدَثِ سَوَاءٌ
ل وجه : (۱) الأية لثبوت أَوْ كَانَ يَجِدُ الْمَاءَ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ مَرِيضٌ لَا يُكَلِّفُ اللَّهُ نَفْسًا إِلَّا وُسْعَهَا لَهَا مَا كَسَبَتْ وَعَلَيْهَا مَا اكْتَسَبَتْ ) (سورة البقرة 2 ، أيت نمبر 286)
وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت أَوْ كَانَ يَجِدُ الْمَاءَ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ مَرِيْضٌ \ أَنَّ عَمْرَو بْنَ الْعَاصِ: " أَجْنَبَ فِي لَيْلَةٍ بَارِدَةٍ، فَتَيَمَّمَ وَتَلاَ: {وَلاَ تَقْتُلُوا أَنْفُسَكُمْ إِنَّ اللَّهَ كَانَ بِكُمْ رَحِيمًا} [النساء: 29] فَذَكَرَ لِلنَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فَلَمْ يُعَنِّفْ " (بخاري بَابٌ : إِذَا خَافَ الْجُنُبُ عَلَى نَفْسِهِ الْمَرَضَ أَوِ المَوْتَ، أَوْ خَافَ العَطَشَ، تَيَمَّمَ، نمبر 345)
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَالتَّيَمُّمُ ضَرْبَتَانِ يَمْسَحُ بِإِحْدَاهُمَا وَجْهَهُ \ عَنْ عَمَّارِ بْنِ يَاسِرٍ، حِينَ تَيَمَّمُوا مَعَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ «فَأَمَرَ الْمُسْلِمِينَ، فَضَرَبُوا بِأَكُفِّهِمُ التَّرَابَ، وَلَم يَقْبِضُوا مِنَ التُّرَابِ شَيْئًا، فَمَسَحُوا بِوُجُوهِهِمْ مَسْحَةً وَاحِدَةً، ثُمَّ عَادُوا، فَضَرَبُوا بِأَكُفِّهِمُ الصَّعِيدَ مَرَّةً أُخْرَى، فَمَسَحُوا بِأَيْدِيهِمْ» (سنن ابن ماجه بَابٌ في التَّيَمُّم ضَرْبَتَيْنِ، نمبر 571/ ابو داؤد بَابُ التَّيَمُّم، نمبر 318) وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَالتَّيَمُّمُ ضَرْبَتَانِ يَمْسَحُ بِإِحْدَاهُمَا وَجْهَهُ \ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «التَّيَمُّمُ ضَرْبَتَانِ ضَرْبَةً لِلْوَجْهِ, وَضَرْبَةً لِلْيَدَيْنِ إِلَى الْمِرْفَقَيْنِ»(سنن الدار قطني، بَابُ التَّيَمُّم، نمبر 685)
وجه (۳) الحديث لثبوت وَالتَّيَمُّمُ ضَرْبَتَانِ يَمْسَحُ بِإِحْدَاهُمَا وَجْهَهُ \ عَنْ عَمَّارِ بْنِ يَاسِرٍ قَالَ: سَأَلْتُ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ عَنِ التَّيَمُّم «فَأَمَرَني ضَرْبَةً وَاحِدَةً لِلْوَجْهِ وَالْكَفَّيْنِ» (ابو داؤد، بَابُ التَّيَمُّم، نمبر 327)
توجه: (1) الآية لثبوت وَالتَّيَمُّمُ مِنْ الْجَنَابَةِ وَالْحَدَثِ سَوَاءٌ \ أَوْ جَاءَ أَحَدٌ مِّنكُم مِّنَ
اصول: تیم میں دو ضربے ہیں، ایک ضرب سے منہ پونچھے اور دوسرے سے ہاتھ ۔
Chapter of Tayammum. And whoever does not find water while traveling or outside the city and between him and the city is about a mile or more: (1) the verse for proof: '...and you find no water, then perform tayammum with clean earth...' (Surah an-Nisa, 5:6). (2) the verse for proof: '...and if you are ill or on a journey or one of you comes from the lavatory or you have touched women and you find no water, then perform tayammum with clean earth...' (Surah al-Ma'idah, 5:6). (3) the hadith for proof: from Abu Dharr... the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Clean earth is the ablution of the Muslim, even if for ten years.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on the junub performing tayammum, no. 332; Tirmidhi, chapter on tayammum for the junub when no water is found, no. 124). (4) the hadith for proof: from Abu Dharr from the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Clean earth is a purifier as long as water is not found, even for ten pilgrimages. And if you find water, let it touch your skin.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, chapter on a man who becomes junub and cannot find water, no. 1661). (5) the saying of a companion for proof: from Nafi' that Ibn Umar performed tayammum at a distance of a mile or two from Madinah and prayed Asr, then entered Madinah while the sun was still high. (Sunan ad-Daraqutni, chapter on the place where tayammum is permitted and its distance from the city and seeking water, no. 719). (6) the saying of a companion for proof: Ibn Umar came from his land at al-Khuruf and Asr came at Marbad an-Na'am, so he prayed, then entered Madinah while the sun was still high and did not repeat. (Bukhari, chapter on tayammum in residence when one does not find water and fears missing the prayer, no. 337). (7) the saying of a companion for proof: Ibn Umar used to perform tayammum at Marbad an-Na'am and pray while he was three miles from Madinah. (Sunan ad-Daraqutni, chapter on the place where tayammum is permitted and its distance, no. 717). Principle: If there is fear of illness, or water is a mile away and one is a traveler, or the city is far, then one obtains purification with earth. Or if one finds water but is ill and fears that using water would worsen the illness, or a junub fears that bathing with water would kill him due to cold or cause hardship, then he performs tayammum with clean earth. And tayammum is two strikes: with one he wipes his face, and with the other his arms to the elbows, to the elbows. And tayammum from janabah and from minor impurity is the same. (1) the verse for proof: 'Allah does not burden a soul beyond its capacity...' (Surah al-Baqarah, 2:286). (2) the hadith for proof: that Amr ibn al-As became junub on a cold night, performed tayammum and recited 'Do not kill yourselves...' (Surah an-Nisa, 4:29), and the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not censure him. (Bukhari, chapter: if a junub fears illness or death or thirst, he performs tayammum, no. 345). (1) the hadith for proof: from Ammar ibn Yasir when they performed tayammum with the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'He commanded the Muslims to strike the earth with their palms, not grasping anything, and wipe their faces once, then repeat and strike the earth again and wipe their hands.' (Sunan Ibn Majah, chapter on tayammum with two strikes, no. 571; Abu Dawud, chapter on tayammum, no. 318). (2) the hadith for proof: from Ibn Umar from the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Tayammum is two strikes: a strike for the face and a strike for the hands to the elbows.' (Sunan ad-Daraqutni, chapter on tayammum, no. 685). (3) the hadith for proof: from Ammar ibn Yasir said: 'I asked the Prophet (peace be upon him) about tayammum, and he commanded me to do one strike for the face and the palms.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on tayammum, no. 327). Attention: (1) the verse for proof that tayammum from janabah and from hadath is the same: '...or one of you comes from the lavatory...' Principle: In tayammum there are two strikes: with one strike he wipes his face, and with the second his hands.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage is the complete chapter on Tayammum from Al-Quduri's matn with the author's commentary providing proofs (wujuh) from the Quran, Hadith, and sayings of the Companions, along with a principle (asl) in Urdu summarizing the conditions. The ruling establishes when tayammum is permissible: if water is not found while traveling, or if one is outside the city at a distance of about a mile or more. The author then cites multiple proofs: two Quranic verses (from Surah an-Nisa and al-Ma'idah) that command tayammum when water is absent; several hadith reports emphasizing that pure earth serves as a purification even for extended periods; and the practice of Ibn Umar, who performed tayammum when a mile or more away from Madinah and did not repeat his prayer upon returning—demonstrating that tayammum is valid when water is not reasonably accessible. The principle (asl) at the bottom of page 41 distills these conditions: fear of illness, water being a mile away while traveling, or the city being distant—then purification is achieved with earth. On page 42, additional conditions are added: even if water is present, if one is ill and using water would worsen the condition, or if a junub fears death from cold or severe hardship, tayammum is also allowed. The method of tayammum is then specified: it consists of two strikes on pure earth—one for wiping the face, and one for wiping the arms to the elbows. Tayammum is the same whether one is in a state of major impurity (janabah) or minor impurity (hadath). Further proofs for the method include the hadith of Ammar ibn Yasir describing two strikes, and the hadith of Ibn Umar explicitly mentioning two strikes. A third hadith from Ammar mentions one strike for face and palms, which may indicate a more concise form or a difference in practice; the author includes it as a proof but the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is two strikes for face and arms. The final note (tawajjuh) refers to the Quranic verse for the equality of tayammum for both types of impurity. The Urdu principle at the end reiterates the method: two strikes, first for the face, second for the hands.

Key Terms
ضربتان (darbatan): Two strikes of the hands on the earth, one for the face and one for the arms to the elbows.
الذراعان (al-dhira'ayn): The two forearms, from the wrist to the elbow. In tayammum, both arms are wiped up to the elbows.
المرافق (al-marafiqa): The elbows. The limit of wiping in tayammum for the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how many strikes are required for tayammum?
A) One strike for face and hands together
B) Two strikes: one for face, one for arms to elbows
C) Three strikes: face, right arm, left arm
D) One strike for face, then wipe arms without striking

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi method of tayammum is precisely two strikes: first the face, then the arms to the elbows, and it applies equally to both minor and major impurity.
